Chapter Notes

See the end of the chapter for notes

"I have to get going."

Taiga had figured this was what Hokuto would say after he had gone quiet with his phone in his hand.

When Taiga glanced up at the clock, he saw it was just after 10 pm.

If the time passed 11, there was a sort of unsaid promise that Hokuto would be spending the night. Taiga had hoped that minute hand would have made its full round to the next hour, but Hokuto's phone called for his attention whenever it wanted. He had been more than selfish with Hokuto's time and he was in no place to ask for more.

"Oh. Okay."

He just had hoped Hokuto would share his bed with him again tonight.

Taiga paused the TV and followed Hokuto to the door. "Are you coming over tomorrow?"

Hokuto kept his eyes on his shoes as he slipped them onto his feet.

"I'll have to see."

That meant no. Taiga didn't have to look any further between the lines to know that. It was just Hokuto's polite way of saying it before it was confirmed by text from the next day.

"Alright… Just message me."

"I will."

Hokuto adjusted the bag on his shoulder one last time, a small smile warming on his lips though Taiga didn't meet his eyes.

"I'll see you soon."

"... Yeah."

The dead bolt thunked as Hokuto undid the lock before taking the handle, but before the door could unlatch, a hand grabbed at his arm, making Hokuto peer back over his shoulder to the gaze that still stayed trained on his back.

The gaze moved as Taiga's grip tightened only for a second before it barely tugged on his sleeve.

"Um… Before you go–..."

Hokuto knew well enough by now what this gaze meant without Taiga saying a word.

Whenever Taiga looked at his lips, he wanted a kiss.

Not because it was romantic.

Just because Taiga wanted to feel something.

Hokuto nodded and Taiga closed his eyes, his hold on Hokuto's shirt falling as he turned to him.

As much as Hokuto wanted to carefully hold his cheek and smile into his lips, he never did because that wasn't what this was for. There was no moment of shared endearment before Hokuto would be tempted to steal another from Taiga's lips.

All he ever did was lean in to have enough of a touch for it to be described as a kiss.

And everytime he pulled away, Taiga's eyes were the same as the first, wandering as he sought something inside him that he never found.

Nothing.

Just like before and surely the next that followed.

Hokuto turned back to the door.

"... Don't go to sleep too late."

Taiga nodded as Hokuto turned the handle.

"Matsumura."

"Hmm?"

Hokuto looked back to him after stepping through the doorway, his keys already in his hand.

"Have a safe trip."

It was just 4 words.

A lot could be said with just 4 words. And those 4 words meant a prayer of safety. A belonging to a home. An awaiting of return, even though Hokuto truly didn't know when he would be able to stand here at this door again.

Whether or not Taiga meant any of that, Hokuto smiled as his chest ached.

"I'm leaving now."

"Hey! Wooow, it looks so much cleaner in here!"

Taiga sighed sharply as he stepped back to let Juri inside.

"Like you're really one to talk."

"I'll never forget the state of your dorm room."

"That was a different time, okay? I'm a changed man. Also that was only once," Juri frowned, handing Taiga his briefcase to remove his shoes. "I had a very important tournament on my game that week and I didn't have time for my meticulous cleaning."

"Sure…"

Taiga shut the door before dropping Juri's bag by his preferred seat in the living area as Juri glanced around the room, smiling as he lowered his head to put his feet in the newly added guest slippers by the door.

"Really, it's nice to see the place picked up, though Kyomo. It makes me feel like I'm looking at where your mind is right now."

Taiga poured a mug of coffee he knew Juri would eventually ask for.

"I guess…"

Taiga had written something.

Something was the key word here. It wasn't exactly full, but it was something. It was honestly a miracle in itself that he had been able to write anything at all, though it was nowhere close to being full. It was better described as a skeleton, but only if the skeleton had no shape, no form, and didn't actually really help show where things should be put to make it feel whole.

So, it was something.

But something was better than nothing.

"So!" Juri smiled, sitting in his place on the couch as he took the mug of coffee from Taiga.

"You want to show me what you got?"

"Yeah." Taiga quickly wiped his hands on a kitchen towel.

"Let me get it."

Juri made himself comfortable, taking off his suit jacket as Taiga scurried off to take his laptop and charger from his room. When he returned, Juri was all settled in, leaning back into the couch with his coffee in hand.

"No Hokuto today?"

Taiga paused midway through setting his laptop in front of Juri, glancing up at the other to see him sip from his mug.

He sighed as his body relaxed, placing the laptop down on the coffee table.

"No."

"Not today."

Juri hummed as Taiga went to plug the charger in advance of its necessity.

It had already been around a month since Taiga had been able to be alone with Juri again.

The flooding waters had stopped filling the room and the suffocation in his chest shrank to a still painful but manageable squeeze at the mention of his fiancé or his expected child. He still didn't like thinking about that night or the embarrassment and shame that followed after, but Taiga could survive.

It was rather convenient timing as Hokuto's schedule had become steadily more occupied by either work or something else.

Taiga didn't know because he never asked.

"That's too bad! I was kind of hoping that he would make something for us!" Juri laughed, taking the laptop into his hands. "I didn't eat breakfast on purpose."

"I can make you something."

Juri blinked before looking over the back of the couch to see Taiga checking his fridge.

"....... Really?"

Taiga didn't bother to turn to him as he started to rummage through his kitchen drawers.

"Really."

Juri just chuckled as he returned his attention to the laptop with an exaggerated sigh. "Amazing how things change, huh? It feels like just yesterday I was helping you make your instant yakisoba."

"Does fried rice sound good?" Taiga said, ignoring Juri's mention of the shortcomings of his past.

"Isn't it a little early to have fried rice?"

"Consider it brunch and it counts."

Juri leaned over to unclip his briefcase with a smile.

"Then sure. Sounds great."

Taiga took out the scraps of his last meals as Juri placed a cigarette between his lips to start his reading. He didn't light it since Taiga didn't let anyone smoke inside unless it was under the kitchen vent full blast, but the editor insisted that simply the sensation helped him concentrate.

As Taiga cooked, the hums and mutterings he heard from Juri gave him no real indication on the quality of his writing as the sounds stayed neutral in their interest, but when he glanced over while removing rice from the cooker, it at least appeared that Juri was captivated with his fingers resting on his chin and his cigarette between his teeth.

While Juri's focus made no promises, Juri was bold enough to drop a manuscript midway if he found it wasn't worthwhile and his continued reading made Taiga feel that he has at least made a first step in the right direction.

After quickly dicing the assortment of leftovers and vegetables, the rest of the cooking went like a breeze as the oil sizzled loudly in the pan with the raw ingredients.

Taiga tossed it, waiting for the water to cook off before he blindly held out his hand for the bowl of whisked eggs that never came.

The pan continued to crackle as Taiga looked over to the empty space beside him, realizing his mistake.

For a moment, he hesitated, staring at nothing but a vacancy as the fire still blazed from the stove top. It was only until Juri's loud sigh pulled him back to earth, carrying Taiga finally to take the bowl himself to mute the hot steel with its contents along with the stirring of his mind.

Without another thought, Taiga finished and plated the rice on the plates with spoons before turning the fan on low and bringing them to the couch.

"How is it?"

Juri didn't look up to Taiga even as his lunch was set in front of him, leaving Taiga to sit and watch him pour over the laptop as he waited, slowly eating from the unruly mound of rice on his plate.

But soon enough, Juri replied.

"... It's interesting."

Juri sighed as he swapped the laptop and the cigarette in his mouth for his plate and its spoon.

"But it's messy."

Taiga dug his spoon into the small mountain.

"The concept of language is very interesting. It's just not very unique… I can tell you're just kind of writing things down. There's not really any order or reason."

"It might be enough to sell to the chief to get a smile, but it doesn't really have any life beyond that. This by itself isn't enough."

Taiga let a pea roll from his spoon before taking the bite. "I know…"

"Not every story has to be deep. Sometimes stories are good enough with having the 'hidden message' underneath," Juri said, throwing up a one handed air quote. "If the reader is having fun, then that's really all that matters. It doesn't have to have a deeper meaning. Sometimes stuff like that are just modes for writers to convince their readers that their words are heavier than they really are to make them feel smart. It's like movie awards. They love to give awards to the historical movies that have depth or whatever because it feels more avant-garde, but that doesn't mean the children's movie wasn't just as good."

"It's great when it works, but sometimes, all it is is an easy sell."

Juri pointed his spoon at him as he continued to eat. "I know I'm just repeating myself. You've heard me say this time and time again, but my point is that I want you to just relax and have fun with it."

"It's okay if it feels a little trivial at the start, but if you try to establish a deeper message before the story is written, you'll be beating the readers over the head with a bat while trying to tell them there's a reason for it. Just write a story that you enjoy writing."

"And this." Juri tapped the laptop before filling his spoon with food. "This isn't a bad start."

Taiga lowered his eyes back down to his plate as Juri took another bite.

Juri had always had this great ability of dragging a person down before boosting them back up. He gave crystal clear criticism that couldn't be begrudged because it was honest in nature, only making the complements that followed feel equally as earnest.

Taiga knew that he was far from what could be called a good story, but he couldn't help but feel a twinge of bitterness at the reality of Juri's words before he was encouraged that it was at least a good direction to take.

It was hard to tell if Taiga felt better or worse before Juri gave his feedback, but at least knowing that everything wasn't useless was enough for him to thank him.

"Thanks, Juri… I'll keep working on it."

"Oh. And your fried rice isn't half bad."

Taiga laughed as he gathered what was left of his lunch on the plate's side.

"Thanks."

"After we eat, back to work?"

"Yeah."

While Taiga took his laptop to work at the kitchen table to save his back from a painful slouching on his couch, Juri stuck around, claiming the coffee table with manuscripts to work diligently away from the office.

Despite pushing the boundaries of his liberties a bit far, as often as Juri was peeking over Taiga's shoulder to look at his progress, he was reading quietly, skimming and thumbing through thick packets of paper while marking pages and jotting notes in the margins.

Taiga knew that Juri had the results to justify his independence, but after a few displeased mumblings and disappointed sighs, Taiga couldn't help but notice how Juri had abandoned his work to move his attention to sorting through the CDs on Taiga's shelf.

As much as Taiga wanted to judge Juri's neglect, he was also reaching his limit too.

He tried his best to focus on the words before him, whether a book or his own writing, but he couldn't escape the nagging deep down in his core that made him continuously check his silent phone.

Each time, he was met with an empty screen and an unchanging chat box before Taiga locked and darkened the screen to only repeat the process again minutes later.

He didn't know what he was waiting for.

Well, he did, but he just didn't know why he was waiting so impatiently for the message he knew would eventually come.

Because when it finally did, all it did was make the nagging inside him twist before it sank.

Matsumura Hokuto:
I won't be available tonight.

Matsumura Hokuto:
I'm sorry.

Taiga had grown used to this response.

It wasn't too long after they started sharing Taiga's bed that Hokuto started to come over less.

After the first night Taiga had slept in his arms, he invited him again the next day, refusing to let Hokuto do work for him when he wasn't awake. Hokuto had done more than he could have ever asked of him, he couldn't ask for more.

Especially when he asked for something as selfish as asking him to kiss him.

Just so he could try to feel something from it.

For most of the nights that followed, they simply just shared the bed. Taiga would roll over and face the wall as Hokuto turned off the lights for both of them to sleep in the bed that was plenty big enough for the both of them.

But some nights when Taiga's mind still restlessly stirred until the early morning, he tugged at Hokuto's sleeve, where it never took more than a few seconds for Hokuto to collect him in his arms in his mid-slumber, whether tucking Taiga's head under his chin or pulling his back against his chest, where his warmth would ease the thoughts in Taiga's head and lull him to sleep.

Taiga's body had always run on the colder side, making his fingers and toes freezing in the night. He always wore full length pajamas and kept a thick comforter on his bed throughout the year to keep himself from getting sick on cold nights and somehow, Hokuto had become an unexpected but welcome solution to his problem.

Hokuto was like a personal space heater. Just one that held him around the waist and buried his nose into his hair in his sleep.

The only drawback was that it made Taiga's nights alone feel colder.

Taiga didn't know when he started to reach out for someone who wasn't next to him in the middle of the night, but it happened more often than he would have liked to admit.

Each time when his hand found no one beside him, Taiga would open his eyes to his bedroom that used to never feel too quiet without a heartbeat pounding steadily next to him, sparing himself only a second to think of why he was alone and who was listening to that soothing rhythm instead of him before willing himself to sleep.

It was as if the moment Taiga came to value it, it started to disappear.

Taiga stared at the message a second longer before he texted back.

Taiga:
It's okay.

He set his phone face down as modern rock began to blast over his speaker system.

"... Juri, I can't say this is exactly the right music to write to."

"Well, this is all you have, Kyomo. I'm kind of limited to your options here."

Taiga sighed as he pulled off his glasses, warming his eyes against his palms and he slouched over the counter.

"I don't think I can write anymore… My eyes hurt and the music completely took it out of me."

"Hey, don't go saying that I'm the reason why you can't write," Juri frowned as he turned the high paced music down. "They'll fire me for that."

"No, they won't," Taiga said, his voice muffled in his hands that had moved down to cover his face.

"There's a first for everything."

Taiga stayed like that, his hands over his face as the energetic guitar thrummed through his speakers.

For the first time in his life, the four walls of his home felt like they were closing in on him, his stress and the impending solitary slumber pushing down on his shoulders until his fringe grazed the keys of his laptop.

Even with Juri in his apartment, there was an absence that grew closer to swallowing him day by day and night by night he was alone.

"... I want to be somewhere that's not here…"

"Huh??"

Taiga was surprised Juri even heard him over the intensifying drumming that came to an abrupt stop.

Juri took his finger off the pause button as he watched Taiga roughly rub his eyes after letting his glasses fall from the top of his head to the counter.

"... Did I just hear Kyomoto Taiga say that he wanted to go outside?..."

Taiga paused, letting the silence sink in before inhaling sharply, his blurry eyes squinting at his screen as he took back his discarded glasses.

"Maybe."

He wished he could say Juri was overexaggerating, but the amount of times that he bluntly refused to do anything outside with Juri rightfully justified his large reaction.

"... Well, shit!!... Let's go out then!"

Taiga set his glasses back on his nose soon enough to see Juri pulling off his tie "Juri, I have work to do. You have work to do too."

"I don't have any more meetings for the rest of the day. Some reading tonight and a bit of overtime tomorrow should resolve all of that." Juri rolled up his cuffed sleeves as he grabbed his phone to check his emails one last time.

"Also, helping Kyomoto Taiga get his well needed break to get his flow back is more than reason enough, right?"

As much as Taiga knew that leaving his work on a tightening deadline wasn't the right choice, the devil on his shoulder whispering in his ear to run and Juri's enthusiasm as he packed up his things convinced Taiga to get on his feet.

"... Where are we going?"

Juri smiled as he clipped his briefcase shut.

"Don't know."

"Let's go find out."

They drove.

That's it.

They just drove.

It didn't matter where, Juri just took whatever road and whatever turn felt right at that very moment.

Taiga had forgotten how his music taste had never quite lined up with Juri's as he blasted hip hop and R&B over his speakers, driving aimlessly to go somewhere not even they knew. He stared out the window at the scenery whipping by, the sound of Juri's thumbs tapping beside him with the deep base rumbling in the car's frame.

With each passing minute, there was an anxiety stirring in Taiga's stomach telling him that each wasted should have been spent writing. He tried to ignore it and push it to the back of his mind, but his manuscript being as indefinite as their destination made it difficult to let go.

The stress must have shown on his face as Juri reassured him again after seeing the unrelenting crease in his brow.

"It'll be okay," Juri said as he switched the song again.

"Just let yourself live in the moment for a bit."

Easier said than done…

But Taiga did his best as he closed his eyes, letting the tiding tempo of Juri's music empty his mind.

"Ohh, I see the water." Juri smiled, leaning over the wheel to catch the glimpses of the sea that peeked from between towering buildings.

"How does the beach sound?"

Taiga kept his eyes shut as he sank into his seat, drifting off with the calming sway of the car.

"Whatever is fine with me."

When the car stopped and Juri shook his shoulder, they weren't at a beach.

Well, they were in the city, after all. There wasn't a stretch of beach in miles, but Juri still parked and let them out to enjoy what turned out to be just a simple common waterfront view.

The moment Taiga opened his door, the sea breeze accosted him, making him squint as he heard Juri's wind muted laugh ahead of him.

"How's this!?"

The wind carried his voice away, but Juri spoke loud enough for Taiga to hear him as he wore his usual wide toothy grin with his hair becoming a mess in the breeze. It gentled as Taiga made his way over, joining Juri in leaning over the steel railing to look over the wide stretch of water.

Taiga closed his eyes as the current tousled his hair.

"... Not bad."

Juri chuckled, squeezing Taiga's shoulder briefly before fishing his cigarettes from his pocket.

"Well, I'm sorry it's not exactly the beach, but this is nothing to complain about."

The box rattled softly as Juri tapped it against Taiga's arm.

"Can I smoke?"

Taiga brushed it away from him, but nodded.

"Go for it. We're outside."

Taiga gazed over the waves after Juri thanked him with a smile before he turned his back against the current to light the end of his cigarette, the thin line of smoke being carried away as it began to burn.

The clear sky allowed the hazy strips of clouds to reflect cleanly against the rippling and waving water below it. There was a distant call of birds Taiga couldn't see echoing around him mixed with the soothing wash of the tide. A chill touched his skin with each brush of the gentle wind as he watched the pure and cleansing scenery.

Not bad.

Not bad at all.

Taiga curled into himself as the draft picked up again, whipping past them as Juri raised his chin against it, grinning as it swept over him.

Juri chuckled when he saw Taiga blowing his unruly hair from his eyes.

After Juri reached over to brush away his bangs with the back of his fingers, Taiga could see the warm smile on Juri's lips and his cigarette still tucked between them.

"You're a mess."

Taiga watched the smoke rise and curl from the cigarette as he let Juri fix his hair, tucking it smoothly behind his ear.

Not that long ago, this surely would have made his heart ache.

He would have wondered how many times he had done something like this with his girlfriend.

His heart and mind would have been sent into chaos from how wrong it was to want something more than a smile and a fading touch and he would have warred with himself on whether it was truly love or if he was just brought to believe it was love.

He would have stood there, wishing to stay in the comfort of Juri's smile forever as his chest grew heavy with a lump in his throat he had no other choice but to swallow down.

But now, at this moment, none of that reached his mind.

Right now, all Taiga could think about was how cold it was and how warm it was when Hokuto held him.

The corner of Taiga's lips tugged up as his fingers retraced Juri's touch with his own.

"You're not exactly orderly either."

"I know."

Juri took in a deep breath of smoke before letting it all out, the cloud streaming from his lips as he stretched and buried his hands into his hair.

"It's freeing from all the office manners bullshit."

Taiga laughed as Juri smiled with him, taking another drag from his cigarette.

"I thought you were into the clean cut look."

"Yeah it looks good on me, but it's annoying to put wax in my hair everyday."

"Do you want some?" Juri asked, holding out the stick before Taiga.

"No way in hell."

Taiga pushed Juri's hand back to himself.

"Even then, at least offer me a new one."

Juri chuckled as he brought it back to his own lips.

"Suit yourself."

They stayed a bit longer, talking about nothing and everything here and there as Juri's cigarette burned down to its filter.

Taiga rested his chin in his folded arms on the railings, listening and replying, though his mind was filled with only one thing.

Actually, it was many things.

But it was one person.

It was just the small things about them and was nothing in particular.

One thing just led to the next.

Like the way he laughed through his nose when he ate reminded him of the way his canines showed when he smiled. How smooth his voice was when he taught. How gracefully his hands moved when he cooked.

The way he tucked his arm under Taiga's head when they got in bed.

They way he held him by the waist.

His face when he slept.

The mole at the corner of his lips.

The way his eyes lidded before they kissed.

Just him.

Just… Hokuto.

…

Taiga adjusted his arms on the railing, pulling them tighter around his shoulders.

… When was it that he started to notice?...

He wasn't sure.

He always knew that Hokuto was undeniably handsome, but when was it that he started to notice the details that made him handsome?

Or when was it that Taiga started to notice the things beyond just his image that made him attractive?

He hummed, mindlessly giving a response to Juri's comment about what watch he wanted to buy next as Taiga laid his cheek down in the fold of his own arms.

… He was becoming greedy.

Whether or not Hokuto treated him kinder than others, he couldn't demand his time.

Taiga had to recognize that he was sharing.

Even if deep inside, he didn't want to.

 

He wanted...

 

 

 

He couldn't.

 

 

 

Taiga blinked when Juri tapped his shoulder.

When he looked over his shoulder, he saw Juri shoving the spent smoke into his pocket ashtray.

"Are you ready to go?"

Taiga gave the water one last gaze before drawing away, hoping to leave his thoughts behind with it.

"Yeah."

"I'm ready."

They both slipped back into the car, Juri letting out a drawn breath as he shut out the cool sea breeze with his door before taking a mint from the tin he kept in his glove box to cut back the smoke on his breath.

Taiga buckled himself in as Juri sat back, crunching down on the tablet to spread over his tongue.

"So. Where now?"

Taiga took out his phone from his pocket to see no new messages. "Home?"

"No no, it's too soon to go home…"

Juri drummed his thumb against the gearshift as he thought.

"When was the last time you went to a club–?"

"I'm not going to a club."

"Alright, then what about a high end bar?"

"... Do I really look like someone who's dressed to go into a classy bar?"

Both of them looked down at what Taiga was wearing.

Taiga didn't take much time to change from his lounge clothes before Juri rushed him out the door, meaning that he was still only dressed in athletic pants and a black shirt with the oversized denim jacket Juri grabbed from his closet on the way out.

It wasn't really something that felt appropriate for a bar where the drinks probably cost more than the shirt on his back, but Juri turned back in his seat and started the car.

"... It will be fine."

Taiga groaned. "Juri!"

"Don't worry! People go to these places in casual clothes all the time!"

"I swear, if I don't see one person in there wearing sandals, I'm walking out."

Juri blindly held out his hand to Taiga as he peered behind him to start backing up the car.

"Deal?"

Taiga frowned, contemplating for a second before begrudgingly taking his hand.

"Deal."

He only took it because he was confident in it enough to believe he'd be able to go home. There was just no way someone was bold enough to go to a fancy bar like they had just decided to stop by after getting groceries.

But to his misfortune, there was one man wearing an expensive looking pair of slides at the dimly lit bar Juri led him inside of.

"... That doesn't count."

Taiga whispered just low enough for Juri to hear before his back was pushed forward.

"We never discussed the quality, so it counts. Come on."

As the sleekly dressed waitress brought them to their seat, Taiga already knew he stuck out like a sore thumb. All the patrons they walked past wore sharp and pricey formal wear while the most he had going for him was that his clothes were at least all black. He just hoped that the defused amber lighting was enough to hide the white stripes down the sides of his pants.

It was shocking how lately Juri managed to always bring him somewhere that felt out of his pay range.

In college, Juri always seemed to be strapped for cash while Taiga was comfortable with the funds from his parents. Even now, it was likely that Taiga's wage was higher than Juri's, but he just wasn't the type to indulge in extravagance in the way he did.

"Just a couple drinks, okay?" Juri whispered to him before slipping into the crescent shaped booth alongside him.

"Just a couple…"

The woman handed Juri the menu with a smile while Taiga wished he could slip under the table and disappear as just looking at the other customers around him managed to make him feel poor despite his plentiful savings.

"Hey, it's not that bad. People can hardly see you from here anyways," Juri said, nudging his elbow into Taiga's arm as he set the drink menu between them.

"Also if you keep slouching like that, you'll only attract more attention."

Taiga sighed, feeling like a scolded child as he sat up to glance through the menu where his eyes immediately crossed trying to read the small text.

The names were frilly and complicated and the list of ingredients under them only made his eyes hurt even before he had put the poison in his blood.

Sours, bitters, vermouth, triple sec, cointreau, moonshine, whatever. It went on.

Some of the drinks he could guess the flavor by the name, but others, he had no idea what they taste like besides just alcohol, and after the 4th drink, Taiga gave up.

"Just get me a glass of wine…" he muttered as he swapped menus for the one containing food.

"... They have curry here?..."

Juri propped his cheek on his palm, still studying the list of drinks. "You'd be surprised what people can make expensive nowadays."

Taiga closed the menu and pushed it away from himself.

He wasn't mentally prepared to spend 4000 yen on a curry he could make half as decent at home.

The waitress came back, Juri ordering for the both of them as Taiga gazed blankly past the woman, staring at the booth across that was empty of eyes that could watch him.

His eyes stayed on the unoccupied booth as Juri handed the woman the menus with a smile and brief words of thanks before she walked away with the order of an aged brandy, a sweeter bodied red wine, and a charcuterie board to share.

"Are you going to be able to drive after this?"

Juri took out his phone from his pocket as he let out a tired sigh. "I'll keep it to one drink."

"I have a meeting early in the morning tomorrow."

Taiga glanced down at Juri's phone, seeing the surprisingly full schedule on the screen.

It always seemed like Juri had the free time to just mess around at his home. Taiga hadn't expected that he had actually fine tuned his visits rather concisely.

He took out his own phone, fiddling with the deep scratch that had managed to raise the plastic on the corner of his phone case.

"That sucks… Is there something going on?"

"We're looking at new prospective authors again," Juri said, switching over to his email that always had at least one message unread. "Tons of manuscripts, so little time. Lots of rough to dig through to find the diamonds."

"Anything exciting?"

Juri hummed as he crossed his arms over the table. "A couple. There's a couple historical fantasy novels that look interesting and some good coming-of-age stories. But you know how it is, the deep melodramatic plots are popular right now."

"Ah."

"They're beautifully written and emotionally moving when you read them, but sometimes I wonder if some people like to buy them so they can look intelligent when they put them on their bookshelves."

Taiga chuckled, popping the corner of his case back onto his phone. "Maybe. But what makes money, makes money, right?"

"Right."

They both raised their heads when the waitress reappeared in front of them, both of them removing their elbows from the table to appear more orderly as she set down a tall glass with a smile.

"Red wine?"

Taiga nodded as she slid it over to him by the stem. "Yes. Thank you."

Juri grinned gratefully when she placed down his drink, but his thanks was disrupted by a quiet curse as his phone began to ring.

"Sorry, I have to get this." He gave an apologetic bow as he slipped past the waitress with his phone pressed to his ear.

Taiga watched Juri speed away to find a place to talk in private as the waitress chuckled warmly, melting the awkward energy left by Juri's sudden departure while she set down individual plates and silverware for two.

"Rather busy, isn't he?"

Taiga just reflected her laughter with a polite smile, making up for the small talk Juri left in his wake.

"Just a little."

"Let me know if you need anything."

Taiga thanked her again as she walked away, leaving him in the booth alone.

For a moment, he just stared at the deep ruby of his wine, sitting silently before reaching over and smoothing his fingers over the flat base to move it slowly closer to himself.

Somehow… It felt lonely.

Taiga was far from alone. The room was filled with the low humming of indiscernible conversation and distant laughter of customers while customers and staff alike passed before the front of his booth, but there was a certain solitude that sank into him as it only seemed to encircle him, leaving a void where he sat in silence with only his drink to keep him company.

Loneliness wasn't really a feeling Taiga was used to. As an only child of a busy family, he had grown accustomed to entertaining himself and being his own company and as he grew older, he often preferred to be alone.

But right now, there was an emptiness.

The wine glass touched his lip, but Taiga didn't drink. His eyes were set forward as the feeling in his stomach began to grow.

… Why?

He knew Juri would soon return, but the loneliness he felt was only medicated but not cured by his friendly chatter.

With Juri, he shouldn't feel alone. But yet, he still did.

Taiga glanced at his phone that laid quiet and undisturbed on the table as he finally took a sip, not wanting to acknowledge that it wasn't about whether someone sat beside him or not.

It was about who.

His fingers wrapped around his phone.

That person didn't owe him any more of his time. That person had his own life and what he chose to do with it, didn't involve him.

Taiga was just another in the swarm of people that requested his attention.

Whoever that person decided to spend his nights with, Taiga couldn't say anything, no matter how badly he wanted the hour hand to pass the 11th hour with him still there.

He couldn't.

The screen of his phone woke to an absence of messages as his hands moved by themselves, opening and swiping through the brief conversations he and Hokuto had exchanged before.

Hokuto's messages mostly said the same thing, but just in different ways.

I'm on my way.

Are you free?

I'm coming over.

Can I stop by?

Can I see you?

Taiga's were the same, saying the same thing with different words.

Yeah.

Okay.

Yes.

I'm open in an hour.

Sure.

But as Taiga scrolled down to the messages of the past weeks, Hokuto's messages had changed.

I can't come by.

I'm busy tonight.

I can't make it.

I'll be out this weekend.

I'm sorry.

All Taiga could say was that it was okay and that it was alright. He didn't even say anything like "maybe next time" or "hopefully next week" because he couldn't expect Hokuto to make time for him the way Juri did for him on his calendar.

But that didn't mean he didn't want him to.

Taiga's thumbs typed each letter slowly, the message growing character by character to say what he wanted to say, but knew he couldn't.

 

I want to see y

 

His thumbs hovered over the last two letters, the echoes of clattering plates and leisurely talk ringing in his ear before one finally moved.

It jammed itself into the backspace key.

He couldn't.

He can't.

The cursor swept over the incomplete message, erasing it to leave the textbox empty with only the all too familiar blinking bar waiting patiently for words.

He typed again.

Are you busy

Taiga didn't bother to punctuate before blindly hitting send and slapping it face down on the table to trade it for his wine, drinking it and already wanting to forget that he had sent it all.

Of course he was busy.

He said he was busy.

That's why he wasn't here.

That's why Taiga wasn't home. That's why Taiga wanted to leave.

What a stupid question to ask.

It was pathetic.

He was pathetic.

Taiga stared at the untouched food as he let his mind fill with only an empty haze.

He just didn't want to think about him anymore or the abandonment he felt in his leave as his ears heard a sound he believed his head had crafted from the blended noises around him.

How fucked up was he to be hearing sounds he only heard around Hokuto?

It was a sound he had only heard a few times before. It was only once or twice when Hokuto arrived at his door before he promptly muted his phone after the first chime and when it pinged in his pocket just before he left with his bags in his hands.

Both times, Hokuto had apologized.

If Hokuto had never drawn so much attention to the courtesy he gave him, the sound would have never made it into Taiga's memory, but Hokuto had shown he cared enough to mute his messages during the time he spent with him.

So Taiga remembered.

He wished he hadn't.

He wished it had just been his brain playing tricks on him, forcing him to hear Hokuto's message tone play in a buzzing crowd.

Because when he looked up to confirm whether he had gone crazy, he saw Hokuto in the booth that was once empty.

And that woman.

Hokuto looked just as shocked with his hand over his phone on his table and his arm draped around her shoulders, leaving no space between them as they sat close together at the center of their booth.

Hokuto was the first to break his eyes away as the woman laid her hand on his chest, smoothing over the black fabric of his button up shirt. He looked down at her, giving her a warm smile and a squeeze on her shoulder, flashing a glance back at Taiga before leaning his head down to whisper in her ear, causing her to giggle in his hold.

Taiga took his gaze away once he saw her fingers slip between the buttons on his shirt.

This.

Hokuto was busy.

And this was why.

The empty feeling in Taiga grew, swallowing him from the inside.

Juri returned, sighing while slipping his phone back into his pocket as Taiga quickly grabbed his phone to delete the message he had sent before.

"Whoof. Sorry about that," Juri said, exhaling as he sank into his seat. "The chief was asking about some of the references so I had to look up their contacts for him."

Taiga shoved his phone in his pocket, trying to ignore the way it vibrated against his leg.

"It's no problem. Work is work."

"Have you tried the food yet?" Juri asked, sipping his drink and swallowing hard as it burned his throat.

"No, not yet," Taiga said as he fought the urge to look across the room again.

"Just waiting for you."

Juri smiled and nudged Taiga's arm with his first.

"You didn't have to."

"It was too expensive to eat by myself…"

"Well if you're paying, then I have no complaints."

"You brought me here. You're paying."

"How about we agree on dutch?"

"Fine."

Juri chuckled before putting cuts of overpriced cured meats and cheeses onto Taiga's plate and pushed it in front of him.

"Thanks. Now eat already."

They talked. Juri complained about his job as he nibbled on his food, describing the worst of the manuscripts with lavish detail and the stifling politics of upper level work while Taiga drank, ate, and nodded while failing to restrain himself from glancing across the room.

Every time he did, the two were all over each other.

Hokuto always kept one arm around her, whether it was over her shoulders or around her waist as the woman leaned into it, looking satisfied and comfortable at his side. Taiga saw her feed him, touch every inch of his exposed skin from his neck to his chest as well as shamelessly stealing a kiss from his lips whenever the waiters and waitresses were cleared of the floor.

Each time, it made a weight in Taiga's core sink, watching her fingers over the collar he studied when he fell asleep and her lips over the ones that had kissed him last they met.

Only once, their eyes locked.

Taiga quickly tore his gaze away, not seeing how Hokuto took every second he had before the woman demanded his attention again, or how his eyes wavered before returning to the pull at his chin.

Taiga tried to focus on Juri's words as he crunched down on artisan crackers, but every time he looked away, his mind's eye showed him visions of when they were together last and how he didn't know when he'd see him next.

He had been with her for 5 years. She was the one that gave him the bracelet that never left his wrist. She was the one he could never tell "no".

She was the one who mattered more.

She was the one who Hokuto gave his time.

She was special.

Taiga was not.

Then why did Hokuto follow him out the door?

Why did Hokuto look so desperate to stop him as if anything Taiga thought truly mattered?

His head hurt. His chest felt heavy.

He didn't get it.

He didn't understand.

But he knew he wanted to see him.

That he missed him.

Even if he didn't mean anything, that was enough for Taiga to type on his phone.

Taiga:
Tomorrow, I'm free.

"Welcome back…" Taiga said, stepping back.

"... Why didn't you use your key?"

Hokuto just laughed and handed him groceries as they had grown accustomed to doing. "Ah… I just… They were too deep in my bag to get out this time."

He lied because he knew that saying he wanted to have Taiga open the door and hear him say 'welcome back' as if this was his home wasn't reason enough.

"... Is that weird?"

"It's not really a dinner food, but it doesn't really matter. As long as you're satisfied at the end, right?" Hokuto said as he removed his shoes.

Taiga's jaw tightened.

As long as he was satisfied.

Taiga blinked when Hokuto looked up after sliding on his slippers, catching Taiga's gaze he didn't know he had been giving him. Hokuto just smiled and brought over the rest of the bags as Taiga turned his attention back to the groceries.

As long as he was satisfied, then it was enough.

That was the mantra Taiga told himself over and over as they went through the same motions as they had any other day.

He just wanted everything to be normal.

He just wanted to have Hokuto's company as he had many times before. He didn't want to think about the day before or about Hokuto's girlfriend, or even about how much or how little he was worth.

He didn't want to think about how Hokuto looked at him.

He didn't want to feel the regret he had not knowing when Hokuto would see him next.

He just wanted to be as it was before.

It didn't have to mean anything.

All Taiga wanted was to feel warm.

"Yeah, of course. Was there something else you had questions about? I can always–"

"Just… a movie or something… Anything."

Anything was fine.

As long as it was long enough to keep Hokuto here.

Only that the run time was 112 minutes.

The animated movie featured a boy who runs away to the city and finds a girl with unusual powers. It played beautiful and colorful scenes that washed over them, illuminating the dimmed room with bright and flowing lights as they watched silently together.

Hokuto looked back, giving a shy smile.

"A little, but it's fine."

"Are you going to share with me?"

Hokuto regretted it the moment he said it, but before he could laugh and swallow his words back by saying it was just a joke, as he went to reach for his own, he felt the seat cushion beside him sink.

"No… This is fine."

He didn't have to be the one on Hokuto's mind.

He didn't even need to matter to him.

Hokuto knew.

They pulled apart, both exhaling their held breaths.

It told him nothing.

Taiga stared, his chest and heart collapsing and caving in as Hokuto started to gather his things.

Hokuto forced a failing smile as he slung his bag into his shoulder.

"I'm sorry."

Taiga stood up, the blanket falling to the floor as Hokuto went to put on his shoes.

It should have been enough.

Taiga told himself over and over again that this should have been enough. He was claiming shared time that wasn't solely reserved for him. He should have been happy that he had any at all.

Hokuto gave himself to anybody and anyone who asked and he couldn't selfishly ask for more. It had to be enough.

It had to be.

It had to be.

But it wasn't.

Taiga wanted more.

He wanted Hokuto to stay.

He wanted him to hold him at night.

For him to smile at him.

He didn't want him to see her.

He wanted to be selfish. To matter. To be special. To mean more.

He wanted Hokuto.

They only kissed.

They kissed after falling onto Taiga's bed until their lips were red and swollen as Taiga quietly suggested sleep, wishing to be held.

After changing with Taiga's insistence, they settled into bed with Taiga wrapped in Hokuto's arms before Taiga asked to be kissed again.

The kisses were soft and slow, their noses brushing and bumping until Taiga had enough, burying his face into Hokuto's chest, clutching his hands into the back of his own pajamas Hokuto wore.

Hokuto hugged him tight, gently cradling the back of Taiga's neck with his other arm wound around his shoulders as if to protect him from the invisible monsters that only came at night.

As Hokuto nuzzled his nose into Taiga's hair, he had a question at the of his tongue he couldn't ask because he was afraid to know the answer.

An answer Taiga knew, but didn't want to say.

Because if he did, then it would be the end.

Taiga had said "until" and "until" had come too soon.

For just a bit longer, even if it was a lie, he wanted to feel like he mattered.

Just like all the girls Hokuto had held before him, he wanted to play pretend and escape, believing just for now that he was special.

To him.

Taiga wasn't ready for it to be over.

Not yet.

Taiga closed his eyes, letting Hokuto's warm scent fill him for tonight.

He wasn't ready to let him go.
