Chapter Notes

Warning: Emotional Abuse.

See the end of the chapter for more notes

Matsumura Hokuto had only fallen in love twice in his life.

The first time was about 5 years ago.

He had moved out from his small town to the city, bright eyed and bushy tailed, ready to do what it took to pursue his culinary dreams.

But as everyone knows, the city is much crueler than it seems once seeing past the blinding and glimmering lights.

His first job was working as a line chef in a moderately reputable establishment. The pay was decent, but the hours and labor were grueling, both on the body and mind.

Day in, day out, Hokuto worked tirelessly until he only had enough energy for sleep at the end of the day.

Get yelled at.

Get scolded.

Yelled at again.

Forced to work through the endless aches and pain.

Exhausting.

His body was running on fumes with no days to relax as his days off from the restaurant were spent on side jobs.

This was the only way.

If he wanted to own his own restaurant, he had to have money, and if he wanted to escape, he had to work.

So work it was. Even if it meant running himself into the ground.

Through some trial and error with different additional jobs, he found a small but chic bar with a master kind enough to let him only work weekends.

For the first time in his life, Hokuto was happy to have someone tell him he was good looking, only because it helped convince the master that he was worth keeping around for even just part time.

This repeating pattern of his life went on for months.

During the weekdays, he cooked. During the weekends, he mixed drinks.

His hands and fingers were battered and bruised from the labor, thankful that the patrons turned a blind eye when he served them their drink.

Takeuchi Hinako was the first to mention it.

"Oh, you poor thing… It doesn't hurt too much, does it?"

She was sitting at the bar with her simple but expensive red dress with furs over her shoulders. Each and every piece of jewelry on her body looked like it could pay for more than a month of Hokuto's rent, but the way she was dressed wasn't necessarily out of place. Many customers came in well dressed to the dim bar, but it didn't take a genius to know that her clothes outpriced all and everyone that day.

Hokuto just smiled and gave her the dry old fashioned she had ordered.

"No, ma'am. I'm quite alright. I just happened to cut myself yesterday. I hope the unsightly appearance doesn't bother you."

He nearly flinched when Hinako took his hand just before it pulled away from her glass.

She turned his hand over and trailed a caress over the bandage on the side of his palm, chuckling at the way Hokuto's fingers twitched from the sensation in her hand.

"To be honest, I actually find it kind of attractive… It's rather manly to have such roughened hands," she said with a sly smile over her lips and a tease in her voice.

"They're almost as good as your face."

Hokuto chuckled politely before taking back his hand. "Why, thank you."

"Does that mean you'll order another drink?"

This was a line Hokuto had used often. He didn't really like doing it. It felt slimy to use someone's attraction to him for the bar's profit, but every sale was worth something, and the bonus the master gave him at the end of every month helped melt all his guilt away.

Hinako laughed lightly behind her glass as she took a sip.

"From the taste of this drink, I'd have to say yes."

The days that followed, Hinako became a regular, always wearing outfits of high value as she sat in the corner seat to talk to Hokuto.

For a while, it just felt like casual flirting with intentions no further than playful conversation, but slowly, she asked about him. She asked about his life, his dreams and hopes, all of which Hokuto told her with honesty. Maybe it was the sense of impermanence that made him feel he could open up to her, that one day she would just disappear with all of his stories with her.

But she came back.

And came again.

And again.

The first few times Hinako asked him out for dinner, he refused.

There was a line that had to be maintained between customers and staff that Hokuto held strongly too, but after a month of her persistence, he finally said yes.

Because he liked her.

At this point, Hinako knew more about him than his own parents.

The dinner went well. They laughed over food and drinks and at the end of the night, with the encouragement from both her and the glasses of wine in his veins, he took her home to his cramped apartment.

By morning, they were dating.

Hinako was a bit older, sweet, and came from a wealthy family.

As much as Hokuto didn't like to admit it, he liked to be spoiled.

And Hinako spoiled him sick.

She bought him endless amounts of priceless things. Clothes. Watches. Glasses. Jewelry. Shoes. Bags.

Anything and everything.

After the first year of them dating, she got him a golden bracelet.

"I want to see you wear it all the time," Hinako told him as they cuddled in the suite she had reserved for them to celebrate, closing the clasp of the chain around his wrist.

"I want it to always remind you of me."

After the second year, Hokuto was finally looking at buying a place for his own restaurant.

His relentless work schedule paid off, bringing his savings account to a sum he felt he could safely rely on to confidently begin his search. Hokuto toured vacancy by vacancy, diligently keeping notes of the pros and cons of each with the floor plan and layout, but the moment he stepped into the space surrounded by glass walls, the notes were all abandoned.

It was a wonderful ground level occupancy in the city filled with natural light that uplifted the cool earth toned interior. Just walking over the colored tile and through the glass alcove filled Hokuto's mind with the imaginary furniture that would suit the space perfectly to encourage the warm and welcoming air. The living space on the floor above would also let him move out of his cramped apartment.

Putting it simply, it was perfect. It was everything Hokuto wanted and dreamed of.

But the price was high.

For even just the bare bones, the rental cost was out of his pay range. Furnishing and completing the inside would already consume the majority of his savings, and with consumables and cost of operations, Hokuto could only reasonably keep the place up at running for a year if he was optimistic.

He sighed to himself and bowed to the owner.

His dream had to stay a dream for a bit longer.

"I can help pay for it."

Hokuto blinked as Hinako straddled his lap on the lavish couch of the hotel she chose for the night.

He had just finished lamenting his struggles before she climbed over him.

They always met in a hotel. Hokuto knew his apartment was too small for her tastes and her family home wasn't an option.

"No, no. I can't ask for that. That's way too much," Hokuto said, setting his hands on her hips as she undid the top button of his shirt she had bought for him.

She chuckled. "Do you know how much I've already spent on you?"

"I want to support your dream. The price is nothing."

He frowned, even as she kissed him. "That's exactly why I can't ask for more… I could never pay you back."

Hinako hooked her finger under the bracelet that never left Hokuto's wrist, lifting his hand to kiss the calluses and scars on his fingers.

"This is how I show my love. Are you saying you don't want it?"

"No! Not at all! I just–..."

She slipped the straps of her dress off her shoulders, letting the fabric drop to her waist as she looped her arms around his neck to kiss him again.

"Just promise you'll never leave me."

"That is enough."

Hinako wouldn't take any answer but yes.

Hokuto was happy.

It was thanks to Hinako that Hokuto was able to buy the place he dreamed of. She was there every second as the space transformed, becoming the restaurant he thought he’d only ever see from his sketches on paper.

The day after he signed the lease, Hokuto was able to call the best chef he knew from his previous job. Jesse was younger, but had years of valuable experience under his belt and Hokuto couldn't have trusted anyone more to be his lead chef. He knew that he was taking Jesse from a great position, but Jesse accepted without question, thankful for anything to get him out of the hell that was their last employer.

"No amount of money is worth my happiness," Jesse told him.

Their beginnings were slow. The customers in the first weeks consisted mostly of familiar faces and friends of friends who all kindly complimented and congratulated them on the place they could call their own. It humbled them the first few weeks, but the flow of patrons began to come in steadily after Jesse had shamelessly used his extensive list of contacts.

Eventually, the friends of friends who arrived at their door became friends of friends of those friends who told their family and loved ones of the small french restaurant encased in glass. Customers became returning customers, returning customers became regulars and Hokuto nearly cried when he saw the promises of breaking even in their earnings.

Salut was running smoothly.

It felt like everything in his life was perfect.

Hokuto had his restaurant, an amazing staff, a home, and a girlfriend who believed in him.

He was happy…

But perfect stories weren’t meant to last.

Everything started to crumble when Hinako arrived at his door with an engagement ring around her finger.

Hokuto was in so much shock, he forgot how to cry.

"What about me!? What have we been doing for the past 3 years!? Am I nothing to you!?!"

He felt like he couldn't breathe.

The weight of the world that had once felt so high came crashing down on him, his head dizzy with pain as Hinako stood before him, calm, like it had been any other day. "I've been arranged to marry him since I was 15. We just had to wait until he was 25…"

"Why!? Why did you talk to me if you knew!? Why did you make me think you loved me!?"

Hokuto clutched his hand over his mouth, struggling to steady his lungs as they fought for air.

"I do love you."

"What about him!?!" Hokuto pointed at the ring on her finger.

"I love him too."

"Then why!?! Why did you drag me in?!?!"

"Because I love you more!"

"No!! Fuck that!! Get out!!!" Hokuto shouted pointing at the door behind her. "Get the fuck out!!"

Hinako scrambled to him, grabbing his wrists and holding them to her chest as Hokuto fought back.

"Hokuto!!"

Now she had tears in her eyes.

"Hokuto, please–!! I promise, I love you!!"

"You can see any girl you want and I won't care-! Please, just stay with me, please!!" she pleaded as the tears fell from the lashes Hokuto had always found to be beautiful. "I love you!! I love you with my whole life!! Please!!! Please don't leave me!!!"

"Hokuto!! I'm begging you– Please!! Please!!!"

Hinako had given him everything. He owed her everything.

He knew he should have let go.

But how could he?

She was his world and the next world over.

Hokuto embraced her and held her as she cried, her chest heaving wrapped in his arms.

Over and over, Hokuto said he would stay. He swore. He promised. He vowed. "I'll stay…"

"Please… Don't cry… I'm sorry, I love you so much."

"I'll stay forever…"

But things wouldn't ever be the same.

Hokuto loved her, but his heart ached at the same time.

He knew that Hinako would return home to another man, telling another lie and another tale to erase the time they had spent together just before. He was a person who disappeared every night when she went to sleep beside her betrothed.

It was as if he didn't exist.

It was as if they didn't exist.

Hokuto's love slowly turned numb.

Hinako had told him he could be with anyone. Maybe she had only said it in the throes of her cries to make things feel fair, but it only managed to hurt him more.

All it told Hokuto was that she didn't care who she gave his love to. After all, he wasn't the one she was married to.

All he was, was a filthy side piece.

So Hokuto did.

Before, Hokuto would politely decline and reject anyone who tried to flirt or approach him saying kindy saying that he was taken, but on the day that Hinako texted him that she would be on an overseas vacation with her husband, when the woman who frequented Salut persistently flirted with him again, Hokuto gave his love away.

And flirted back.

He couldn't really say he enjoyed it.

It didn't take much to make a girl blush. Just a few kind words and a subtle touch was usually enough to make them avert their eyes and bite their lip. It was easy when he knew they were attracted to him, which Hokuto still couldn't understand as he teased every woman who showed interest.

But it made it easier.

It felt like payback.

Hokuto handed out his number. He accepted every date. He let women come and sleep in Hinako's spot beside him in bed. He gave away everything he once protected so preciously just for her. He gave and gave until it was worth so little that he could convince himself it never meant anything at all. That it wasn't something to be valued. To be cherished.

It was all just a cheap trick to have paying customers return.

Hokuto wanted to give his whole heart away to make the ache stop.

Jun was someone he thought he could give it to.

Jun was pretty, kind, and smart. She was maybe only a little unfamiliar with love, but that's what made her endearing. She only started to show interest in him once they talked at the bar after she came again with friends, and not simply because of his face.

When she asked him out, Hokuto agreed, and after it was over, for the first time ever, Hokuto asked for another.

It went well.

Time with her was fun and easy. It let him temporarily forget that his heart was broken and the pieces belonged to someone who didn't belong to him. He played love with her in hopes that one day it would help cure the numbness that has swallowed him from the inside.

Hokuto was ready to ask to see her again, but he couldn’t stop what Hinako told her.

Hokuto didn’t know what to think when he saw Hinako sitting beside Jun, her bar stool pushed up against hers as she whispered in her ear with her ruby lips. He tried not to listen to the anxiety pooling in his stomach, wanting to believe that, at most, all it was was playful gossip. He tried to convince himself that Hinako wouldn't try to hurt him as he pushed through his work day, until Jun asked to meet him outside.

"I'm sorry, Hokuto… I don't think we can see each other anymore," she told him at the front doors.

The numbness that barely had the chance to subside deepened as Hokuto tried to reach for her arm only to have Jun step back away from him.

"... Why?... Did Hinako say something? Jun, don't listen to her, she–"

"It wasn't Takeuchi… I already knew that you dated around and slept with other girls but…" Her grip tightened on her purse. "I just want to be with someone who will love me completely. I like you, Hokuto..."

"... But not enough to share you."

Hokuto couldn’t say anything.

He couldn't, because he wanted the same too.

That's why he let her walk away.

He wanted a complete love just as much as she did. He didn't want to share. He just wanted anything that would stop the emptiness that slowly sank deeper into his core.

When Hokuto opened the door to his room, Hinako was there, waiting on the bed.

"Hokuto…" Her voice started soft and slow as if to scold him. "I told you that I don't care if you see other women."

The door clicked behind him as Hokuto pushed it shut with his back, his eyes still trained on the floor with chest burning from within.

"... Then why did you say those things to her?"

Hinako's heels clashed against his wood floor when she shot to her feet.

"Because I have to be first!!"

Hokuto's back hit the door when she rushed him, taking his face into her hands to force their eyes to meet.

"You loved her, didn't you!? You were going to leave me for her!!"

Hokuto's eyes widened as he grabbed Hinako's hands that refused to let go. "No! Hinako, I–"

"You're lying!!! You're lying to me!! I know you are!!! You loved her!!"

"I would never lie to you!! Hinako, listen to me–!!"

"You're a liar!!!" Hinako screamed. "You promised me!!! You promised me!!! You said you would never leave me!! You lied to me- How could you lie to me!!!"

Hinako wouldn't listen. No matter what Hokuto said, none of it reached her as she pushed herself into Hokuto's arms, sobbing into his chest.

"Do you know how much I love you!?! How much I spent on you!?!? I'll take it all away!!!" Her nails dug into his clothes as her make up ran down her cheeks.

"I'll shut this place down!! I'll end all of it!!!"

Hokuto's body went dead cold.

He gripped Hinako's shoulders and tore her from his chest as he couldn't even hear his own voice over the ringing in his ears. His eyes were wide as his hands nearly shook.

"Hinako!!! Listen to me!! Please!!! I don't love her!!! She never meant anything!!!" His voice tore through his throat, nearly quivering as they passed his lips. "There's only you!!!"

"There will only ever be you!!!"

The words spilled from his mouth before he knew what he was saying. Out of the things that mattered to him most, he had already lost Hinako.

He couldn't bear the thought of losing Salut too.

Hokuto said words he didn't want to accept. Words that instilled the sinking numbness that would consume his heart. Words that promised the ache would never stop, that he couldn't escape, that he would never feel a love that was whole.

Words he had to force from his mouth to protect all he had left.

For the years that followed, Hokuto laughed and smiled with only an empty shell in his chest where his heart once was. He played love with the women that came and left his life as a reminder of what he would never truly have.

Hinako still bought him everything, but there wasn't a single luxury worth what they once had as he performed as the person he once was during their happiest of days to please her.

The numbness became a part of him as Hokuto surrendered to it, letting it consume him until he nearly convinced himself that this was what true love was.










Then Kyomoto Taiga crashed into him.

Though, it was more like Hokuto caught him.

It was rare for an independent man to dine at Salut. Most came by obligation to their female counterpart, be it a boyfriend or family member that was forced to come with them. There had been single men in the past who had come before to give Hokuto a solid look up and down as he served them, but that wasn't all that made Taiga pique his interest.

It was the animosity.

Taiga didn't try to hide that he didn't like him.

Even without reading the scribbled words in his notebook, Hokuto could tell from the way he averted his eyes, kept their exchanges short and physically repelled himself from him.

Hokuto had a rule to never flirt with anyone who wasn't interested, but there was something about Taiga that made him want to push himself closer no matter how much Taiga pushed away. He was like a skittish cat that hissed and bore its claws at him until someone reached out their hand, making it jump and bolt away.

There must have been something sick about Hokuto that made him enjoy Taiga's repulsion to him. Every time Taiga flinched or scowled from his advances, something stirred in him that Hokuto had never felt before.

The more and more Hokuto learned about him, the more and more he was fascinated by the man named Kyomoto Taiga.

Hokuto was amazed by how viscerally Taiga rejected romance and love to the point where it disgusted him and made him ill. He grimaced and soured at the mere mention of it, refusing to acknowledge and take part of any of it… Even though Taiga himself had admitted to not knowing what it really was.

It was impossible for Hokuto to keep himself from getting closer, poking and prodding– teasing and pushing to see at what point Taiga would cave and confess that all his hatred was all just wasted energy. Eventually, Hokuto got close enough to see the delicate face that only ever had a frown in his presence as he trapped him between his hands against the restaurant wall.

It really was a waste that it was always hidden behind heavy frames…

Taiga's eyes were beautiful underneath.

The way Taiga blushed and flustered was cute. There didn't have to be anything romantic about that. Hokuto had enough self-awareness to know the difference between a passing thought and attraction.

But the passing thought had become more and more frequent.

Each step he got closer, the closer Hokuto grew towards the edge.

At the theme park, even though they hardly knew each other, Taiga had seen right through the lie Hokuto convinced himself was true as Hokuto ignored the showers of lights in the night sky for another glimpse of his long lashes.

Another step.

During their date at home, Taiga invited him over again, giving him a payment of chocolate mousse from his own spoon, ignorant of the intimate gesture before he fell asleep with his head in his lap.

Closer.

Hokuto didn't know he could feel like this. His chest that had been so vacant felt the pricks of a sting when Taiga didn't flinch from Juri's touch before it melted away when he opened his hand to find a key. Back and forth, something inside him was pulled until he found himself cornering Taiga into his couch, asking him if he was in love with Juri.

It scared him how much he had reminded himself of Hinako, asking Taiga as if he had any reason to be upset.

Closer and closer. Stumbling. Sliding. The edge at his feet.

Hokuto couldn't get closer.

He knew he shouldn't.

He had promised. He swore. He vowed.

But when Taiga came to him at night, his anger and his rage all falling apart into tears, Hokuto slipped.

He took Taiga into his arms as his once abandoned heart started to pound, race, ache and sway. It burned, banging at his ribs as Taiga asked him to teach him what love was worth when he himself had forgotten so long ago.

He fell.

He kissed Taiga, unable to save himself from the ledge.

Hokuto fell. Completely and hopelessly in love with Taiga.

Hokuto woke up with Taiga in his arms.

The night before, Hinako had called him and demanded he meet her, but after Taiga kissed him and begged him to stay, he couldn't leave.

He couldn't bring himself to refuse the person he had become so desperately in love with.

Hokuto swallowed down the lump in his throat and gave himself a few more minutes, nuzzling his nose into Taiga's hair and pulling Taiga's back closer against his chest, trying to remember every detail and feeling of his skin.

It wasn't mutual… or maybe it was.

It was hard to tell with the doubts and denial stirring in his thoughts, but whatever it was, Hokuto took every moment believing, despite the pain in his chest telling him it wasn't.

"... Taiga."

Hokuto barely breathed the other's name into the back of his neck.

Yesterday was the first time he had heard his first name from Taiga's lips. Sure, it was stupid and only teenage boys ever got so excited hearing their name in their crush's voice, but Hokuto didn't care. He loved it and wanted to hear it again. Every morning and every night. Just like this.

With Taiga wrapped in his arms.

His hold tightened, wanting so badly to simply drift off again with the sounds of Taiga's steady breaths beside him, but his internal clock knew he couldn't stay any longer.

He still had to go to work.

Hokuto pressed his jaw into the curve of Taiga's shoulder, taking and treasuring every last second in Taiga's gentle warmth before finally bringing himself to slip away.

The moment Hokuto unwound his arms from around him, he wanted nothing more than to collect Taiga back in his arms and lose himself in his scent, forgetting about work and the unread messages on his phone, but he knew he couldn't. A quiet sigh left his chest as he sat up in bed, watching Taiga sleep for just a second longer before sitting at the side of the mattress and unbuttoning his shirt.

As the shirt fell from his shoulders and he went to get up, a tug on the collected fabric kept him from rising to his feet.

"... Are you leaving?..."

Hokuto didn't want to.

But he had to.

No matter how much he wished to stay after seeing Taiga's tired eyes peering past his gathered blanket and tousled bangs with his fist clenched into his shirt.

Hokuto's chest ached.

"... I'm sorry… I have work…"

There was a moment as Taiga's gaze fell from his, the tug tightening before it slacked with Taiga's hand retreating back under the covers. His blanket fell from over him as he pushed himself up from his side, blinking the sleep from his eyes through his mess of blonde hair.

"... Okay."

"... Let me get up with you at least…"

A chill already sank into Taiga's skin as he sat.

He gazed at their feet as Hokuto dressed himself in yesterday's clothes. He had folded them neatly after Taiga caught his breath from their kiss, whispering to Hokuto that he wanted to be in his arms for the night.

Taiga wished he could have rewound time back to then as he rose to his feet and followed Hokuto to the door as he always did, not noticing how Hokuto took and shoved his phone into his pocket without checking the screen.

His fingers dug into his own pajamas as he watched Hokuto slip on his shoes and take his previously abandoned bag from by the door, ready to leave.

Again.

"Um-..." Taiga choked out. "Did you want something to drink before you left? Like coffee or-..."

Hokuto smiled, but it was short lived as he glanced at the clock.

"Sorry, I don't really have the time. I'm already late."

"I have instant. Are you sure?"

Taiga wasn't ready for Hokuto to leave again.

There was no telling when he would return. For all Taiga knew, this could have been the last time. Once Hokuto stepped out his door, he would disappear for who knows how long. By the time they could see each other again, Taiga's deadline may be well over, with or without a manuscript. After that, Taiga wouldn't have any other excuse for wanting to see him.

But whether Taiga was ready or not, time wouldn't wait for him.

"I'm sorry… I really have to go…"

It took everything in Taiga to not pull Hokuto back when the door clicked open.

A dirty trick like that was certainly something that only worked once.

It was pathetic how desperate he was with his voice nearly cracking when Hokuto stepped into the hallway.

"... Tomorrow?..."

Hokuto turned to him as Taiga took the door, keeping it open as he spoke.

"Can you come tomorrow?..."

Taiga could see Hokuto's hand place over his phone in his pocket as Hokuto's words hesitated in his mouth.

"I–... Uh…"

The only thing more pathetic than begging for more time was being told he couldn't have it.

"... Not tomorrow… I can't…"

It already hurt.

Taiga might as well dig the knife in deeper, right?

"... Is it your girlfriend?..."

Hokuto laughed, trying to force his lips into a smile. "Well, it's um… She-"

Taiga cut him off.

"It's fine."

He had heard enough.

It almost hurt more that Taiga could still feel the lingering of Hokuto's embrace as he was reminded how it didn't belong to him, no matter how much he wished to be still wrapped safely within it. Hokuto would go back to her while all Taiga could do was wait until he could live in the brief illusion of Hokuto's affection again, whenever that was.

Hokuto watched as Taiga's eyes fell to the bracelet on his wrist.

"... Just–…" Taiga's hand tightened around the handle as he slowly began to push the door shut, severing them apart. "Just text me…"

"... Whenever it is that you can waste your time on me…"

Taiga was ready to close the door tight and throw the dead bolt locked, bottling up his rejection and shame with it before curling back into bed alone with an emptiness that would consume him.

But just before the door latched with Taiga behind it, Hokuto shoved his hand through the crack of the opening.

Taiga blinked, stepping back as the door swung back open.

"H-Hokut–"

Whenever they had kissed, Taiga had always asked first. As training, as practice, nothing else. Even when it was Hokuto leaning in, it was because it was Taiga who had sought it.

Taiga never could have imagined how different it was to have Hokuto kiss him simply because Hokuto wanted to.

He barely had a chance to breathe before Hokuto stole his lips. His eyes squeezed shut as Hokuto held their kiss with his hand grazing the back of his neck as Taiga shakily exhaled into it.

Before Taiga could roll his lips back into his, Hokuto pulled away, leaving him breathless.

"One week."

"H-… huh?" Taiga barely whispered, still recovering from his shock.

Taiga watched his eyes as Hokuto tucked his blonde hair behind his ear, the bracelet slipping down his wrist.

"Just give me one week."

Hokuto drew his hand back, already missing the feel of Taiga's skin.

"One week…"

"... Then all my time will be yours."

One week.

Hokuto had one week to pull his shit together.

In one week, Hokuto had to pull his life up by the bootstraps and figure out what the fuck actually mattered to him.

After being numb for so long, he finally started to understand what love was worth after it had become so mangled and manipulated. It wasn't about wanting, needing or claiming. It wasn't about give and take. It wasn't even about instinctual sexual attraction.

It was just a feeling.

There were no "and"s or "but"s. There were no boundaries or barriers.

Just a feeling.

There was no reason for it to be anything more than that.

Hokuto didn't truly need the whole week to figure himself out. He just needed a week to gather enough courage to do it.

Just a week.

One week.

For just one week, all Taiga had to do was wait, though sometimes, waiting was far worse than doing.

Waiting simply meant that there was nothing he could do. There was no control, no knowledge, no awareness of anything that would happen while he waited for time to slowly move by.

Taiga had no idea what Hokuto would be doing with the week he asked for. As far as he knew, Hokuto could have just fed him lies to give him enough time to disappear.

But Taiga wanted to trust him.

Hokuto said one week until… something happened.

Taiga wasn't actually sure what it really meant.

Hokuto had left him with a kiss and a promise of his time. It wasn't exactly an acknowledgement of mutual affection, it wasn't like Hokuto had dropped to his knees and asked Taiga to love him forever and always.

All it was was time.

But sometimes, that by itself meant more than a kiss.

For the week, Taiga tried his best to focus. There were only two months left on his deadline and at this point, all he could do was place his bets heavily on the chief's words of "anything will work as long as there's some promise".

It was certainly something, but if that something had promise, it was hard to say.

As supportive as he was, Juri didn't cushion his words with compliments before telling him that it wasn't exactly enough. He told him that maybe if the staff was in a good mood, they would consider taking it as a work in progress with promises of improvements in the future, but as it stood, there wasn't a good chance it would sell.

Juri had brought his last editor along with him to get a second opinion on Taiga's work. After reading, she gave him an encouraging smile and told him that it was at least interesting in concept, but Taiga remembered that she had made the same smile after he had killed off her favorite character from his last series.

"Ironically… for a story about language, I'm having a hard time understanding what you're trying to say," she told him.

Taiga knew what she meant because he didn't really know either, but time was running out. He had something and that something had to be finished, whether it was a masterpiece or not.

He tried to work, locking himself in his room with only himself and his document to write, but somehow, the one week Hokuto asked for weighed on him heavier than any of the days of his 8 month deadline.

As he stared at his screen, trying to digest the clutter of words he had put on his page, Taiga's mind always wandered.

What was Hokuto doing. What would come at the end of the week. What would happen. What it meant.

What it would mean.

What they would be.

What they could be.

For the days that passed, Taiga's phone stayed silent.

Seven. Six days.

Taiga typed, but the paragraph on his page never grew longer, writing and deleting as his mind was swarmed with doubts, hopes and regrets.

Five.

Finally, a decent amount of writing had been done, but it all felt disjointed. Juri had come to look over it and patched it up a bit, but without a complete rehaul overwrite, it was as good as it was going to get.

Juri ordered takeout from them that night.

Four.

Some authors liked to use alcohol to encourage their writing, calling it the social lubricant for their words. Taiga had tried it before and it didn't seem to help, but at this point, anything was worth another shot.

If anything, it would help keep his mind off of the number of days.

After a few glasses of whiskey, Taiga was able to write, but he had asked for just a little too much 'encouragement'. His fingers moved, though he wasn't sure if anything would make sense in the morning.

Eventually, instead of words, the alcohol brought sleep.

Taiga got into bed early and curled himself around his spare pillow, falling asleep with the wish that Hokuto was there to hold him.

Three…

The bottle of whiskey was returned to its place at the back of his shelf.

Two…

One.

One more day and it would be a week.

The previous 4 days felt like they lasted an eternity. The last 6 months of his deadline had seemed to disappear in a flash that Taiga didn't think time could have moved any slower.

Yet, on the last day, the seconds seemed to tick by like the gears of the clock were made from molasses.

Taiga glanced at the time after what had felt like hours was only 20 minutes.

It was about 9 pm.

Salut closed at 8.

He sighed as he leaned back in his chair, staring at the messily strewn together words he had tried to make sense of from the night before.

9:13 pm.

…

…..

……

9:14…

…………

…………..

9:15.

Taiga got to his feet, using a flimsy excuse to pull on his jacket as he went to the door.

"... Maybe fresh air will help."

"Are you okay?"

The chair screeched as Hokuto flinched, shoving it just a little too hard under the table.

Shintaro put a finger in his ear, wincing as Jesse peeked through the service window for a second before returning to his cleaning without worry.

Hokuto wiped his hands down his apron, acting as if he hadn't sent a piercing sound through the restaurant. "Um… Yeah. Why do you ask?"

Shintaro sighed, plunging the mop into its bucket cart.

"You act like you haven't been a space case all day. Do you really think your employees, also known as your friends," he inserted with emphasis, "wouldn't notice at all?"

"Even some of the customers noticed, it's not like you."

Hokuto gave him a half-hearted smile as Shintaro frowned, placing a hand on his hip with the other authoritatively gripping his mop.

"Sorry. I've just been a little distracted today."

When Shintaro didn't drop his act, Hokuto jabbed his finger into his side as he passed, making the other yelp and reflectively curl into himself from the sharp ticklish sensation. He huffed, hooking the mop into the bucket before quickly following behind Hokuto's footsteps.

"Is everything really okay?"

"I told you, Shintaro. Everything is fine."

Shintaro leaned over the bar as Hokuto began checking the register.

"Bullshit."

"Are you going to take any answer besides a no?"

"Not really… Well, I could if I'm truly convinced, but I mean– Okay, that's not really the point."

Hokuto just kept his eyes down on his work.

"Then what is it if it's not just to harass me?"

"Oh, I don't know… Just wanting to feel like my longtime friend trusts me enough to rely on me, maybe?"

Hokuto's hands paused before they dropped onto the register drawer with a sigh.

Why did Shintaro have to guilt him like this?...

Shintaro was a great friend and a great worker. More often than not, Hokuto would be happy spilling out all of his issues to him over some hard drinks.

But this was just something Hokuto really wasn't feeling vulnerable enough to talk about.

Not this time.

"Thank you, Shintaro… I really appreciate it." He pushed the drawer closed. "I'm not perfect, but I'm fine."

"... I'll be fine..." Hokuto corrected.

Shintaro pursed his lips, dissatisfied, but knew better than to push.

"Okay… Well, if you ever need a drinking buddy, you know who to call."

Hokuto laughed a little. "Trust me… I know."

"Thank you."

It was about time to close up.

Shintaro took his leave after he finished his mopping job he had momentarily abandoned, but not without making sure to take his revenge by jutting his finger into Hokuto's side with a loud laugh and a wave.

Hokuto waved back, rubbing at the aching spot as he went to the kitchen to help Jesse finish preparing for tomorrow's pastries.

As Jesse set down another bundle of chilled dough on the counter, he glanced at Hokuto next to him before pulling the cling wrap off from around it.

"... You know, you really did seem a little lost today."

Hokuto looked up from the tart tins he lined, wiping his mouth with the back of his hand as he gave a bitter smile.

"You too?"

Jesse chuckled as he floured his hands to roll out the dough. "Honestly, I couldn't have ignored it if I tried."

"What gave it away?"

"Hmm… Probably the blank look you had every time you came into the kitchen…"

"... It was that bad?"

"Well, it wasn't good."

Jesse's laughter somehow always got Hokuto to at least crack a smile.

It was a brief respite from the anxiety that was brewing in his head.

"I already heard what you said to Shintaro, so I don't think it needs repeating," Jesse said as he passed the flat spread of dough to Hokuto. "I'm sure you know. I've told you before and it hasn't changed."

Hokuto smiled as he let out a deep breath.

He held out and swung his hand just enough to tap his knuckles against the fist that Jesse held out to him. "I know. Thanks."

Jesse grinned as he returned to his work.

"Any and every day, Hokuto."

They finished up using idle chatter to pass the time, Hokuto noticing, but still thankful for the cheerful topics Jesse stuck to to keep the mood light. After cleaning the counters and storing the finished sweets, Hokuto went with Jesse to the door.

"I'll see you tom– oof-!"

Hokuto blinked as Jesse wrapped him in a big hug. He squeezed him tighter as Hokuto laughed against his shoulder and patted his back.

It was always strange when his large friend embraced him, but each one of them was warm and comforting.

"Don't stay too late. Get some sleep."

"Okay. I got it."

Hokuto reflected the smile Jesse gave him when he let go and raised a hand in goodbye as he watched Jesse walk down the alley.

And as soon as Jesse rounded the corner out of sight, Hokuto's smile faded as his mind began to buzz again with static.

He glanced at the clock behind the bar.

10:08 pm.

It was 1 hour and 42 minutes before it would be a week.

Hokuto exhaled a tired sigh as he took a glass to polish, pushing away the thoughts of running out the door at exactly 12 am.

Every day for the past week, all Hokuto could think about was how badly he wanted to see him. All he could hear were his pleas for him to stay and all he could feel were the lingerings of his kiss and his embrace.

It was like he was sick.

Whenever Hokuto told a lady she looked beautiful or that her hair looked nice, he could only think about him and the blonde strands he would tuck behind his own ear as he read and when a woman called his name, Hokuto could only think about how his name sounded from his lips.

Every laugh was his laugh.

Every smile was his smile.

Every voice was his voice.

Hokuto set down the glass, the crystal chiming a clear ring as he moved to the next.

Just one more day.

Just one more hour.

Then Hokuto would give everything he had to him and all he could hope was that Taiga would accept it.

The doorbell chimed.

Hokuto looked up, setting down his glass.

Salut was closed, but every so often someone would still walk in through the doors. Sometimes it was just someone who was dead drunk, asking for water or food, or even just a customer who misunderstood the time or was returning in hopes to find something they had lost.

Hokuto knew who it could be.

He also knew who he wanted it to be.

But it couldn't possibly have been, right?...

He called out as he put down his cloth.

"Hello?..."

When Hokuto stepped out from behind the bar and their eyes locked, he froze.

Immediately, his heart began to race.

"... Hokuto?..."

His chest felt tight as it ached, hearing his name said in a voice he loved and adored.

He hardly ever heard his first name from it. The first time he had heard it, it made his heart swell.

He loved it more than anything in the world.

He loved.

He did love.

He had loved.

Hokuto couldn't remember the last time she had said it without the teasing nickname.

"Hinako…"

Hinako dropped her purse to the ground, the gold chain raining to the floor as she ran to him, throwing herself into his chest.

She looked up at him, hands eyes wide and empty as she gave a hollow chuckle that echoed through the vacant restaurant.

"Y-you… you can't." Her hands clutched into his shirt. "You can't break up with me… You can't. This is all just a cute joke, right?"

"This is all just a silly little prank!"

Hokuto took her shoulders, panicked. Scared.

"Hinako, I–"

Her laughter grew louder as she took his face into her hands and pulled him down to her, not seeing the troubled look in his eyes.

"Of course you wouldn't mean that, right?? My Hokkun would never say something like that! Were you just getting jealous? Aww, are you trying to get my attention?"

Hokuto struggled to get his words out when they were face to face.

"N-No– Hinako– Please–"

She backed him into the bar, the chairs clattering from his body pushing them away from the counter as Hinako pressed herself into his chest, her laughter fading.

"It's just a prank, right?..." She smiled with no joy. "Tell me, Hokkun."

"Tell me all of this is just a joke."

"Tell. Me."

Hokuto couldn't.

Even when Hinako demanded it, hissing through her teeth as she pulled at his clothes, he couldn't.

But silence wasn't an answer Hinako would take.

"... Hokkun?..."

Her voice was drenched in her sweet tone, hiding the bite underneath.

"... Why aren't you saying anything?..."

"Why!?!"

Hokuto flinched when her voice rose, her desperation beginning to show through the crack of her mask.

"Why can't you tell me, Hokuto?!?!" She beat her hands on his chest, screaming as Hokuto's hands tightened around her arms. "Tell me!!! Please!!! Tell me it's a joke!!!"

He couldn't lie to her.

But he was just as afraid of what would happen if he told the truth.

"Didn't you say you love me?? You love me, don't you?? You love me!!"

"I- I do! But-"

"You said you love me!! You said you would never lie to me!! So then why!?" She shouted, shoving her fists balled with his shirt into his chest. "Did I do something?? Did I say something wrong??"

"Please, I'm sorry!! I'll do anything!!!" She began to beg.

"No! No, y-you didn't-"

"Then why??"

Hinako didn't listen. She wouldn't listen. No matter what Hokuto said or tried, none of it ever reached her.

This was exactly what Hokuto was afraid of. He knew it was cowardly, but deep down he hoped that his long message would be enough. When she didn't respond, he wanted to believe that she had finally woken up and finally saw how their love had become a horrible dependence instead of affection.

Hokuto wanted so badly to be free.

He was done being trapped in a love that would never be completely his. He just wanted it to be pure. He wanted to be in love because he wanted to be again. Not because he had to.

Hokuto wanted to have the love that Taiga had for Juri.

So simple that he didn't know it happened.

Hokuto shouted, trying anything he could. "I told you!! Don't you understand?? We–"

"No–!!! It can't be!!" Tears began to fall from Hinako's eyes as she shook her head, refusing to accept his words. "Is someone paying you to say this?? I'll pay you more!! I'll pay you ten times more!! Anything!!"

"Just don't leave me!!!" Hinako cried, her tears rolling down her cheeks past her pleading broken smile.

"No! Hinako!!! Please–!!! Just listen to me!!"

Hokuto's voice echoed through the room when Hinako's screaming stopped.

For a moment, Hokuto wanted to believe that he had finally reached her and that she would finally listen as she stared up at him, eyes wide and full of tears.

He spoke softly, pleading. "Hinako… Please listen to me just once… I–"

"It's him, isn't it?"

"... Huh?"

"It's him."

Hinako pushed him away, smiling as she began to laugh.

"That boy! The one who came here!! It's him, right???"

Hokuto's eyes followed her as she stumbled back, laughing as she fixed her cardigan that had fallen from her shoulders, completely bewildered by her sudden shift in mood.

"W-what–? Hinako, I–"

"I could tell he was absolutely in love with you!! It was him! Oh thank goodness it's just him!"

Hokuto could guess who she meant, but he couldn't understand her joy.

If anything, he thought she would be furious.

"What… What do you mean?"

Hinako chuckled, rubbing her tears away on her sleeve as she went back to him to fix his shirt. She smiled as she took his hand, cupping her own cheek in his palm with the gold bracelet falling down Hokuto's wrist.

"The 1,000,000 yen bet."

Hokuto's body went completely cold.

Every worry and concern vanished, leaving only shock and fear as he forced his lungs to work, making his voice crack through his throat to say the only thing he could possibly ask.

"How…"

"... How do you know about that?..."

Hinako giggled, pulling his arms around herself as she looped her arms around his neck.

"I saw you talking to him," she said with all the confidence she had lost returning to her speech. "What was his name again? The man in the suit that was with him?"

"Tanaka Juri, was it?"

"He promised you money."

Hokuto could only hear his heart pounding in his ears. He had to remember to breathe as his breath shook from his chest as he stared.

Not at the ground.

Not at Hinako.

The door.

The door that he hadn't noticed was cracked open.

And Taiga who stood behind it, staring back.

Listening.

Hokuto wanted to scream.

"That boy falls in love with you, he writes a romance novel, and you get the 1,000,000. You just sent me that text to make it all that more convincing."

Pain.

"All of this is fake."

Regret.

"Of course, you would never fall in love with a man!"

Ache.

"You would never fall in love with someone like him!"

Betrayal.

Hokuto's muscles only listened once the door had closed, nearly pushing Hinako to the floor as he ran to the entrance.

"Hokuto??" Hinako gasped as he caught herself on a chair. "Where are you going?!?"

"Stop!! Come back!!!" She screamed at Hokuto's back.

"Please!!!!"

Her voice didn't reach him as Hokuto was already out the door.

"Taiga!!"

"Taiga, wait!!"

"Just let me–!"

Hokuto wasn't sure what hurt more, the sting on his palm after he was swatted away from reaching Taiga's hand, or the cold empty tone.

"Don't follow me."

Hokuto tried again. He grabbed Taiga's shoulder, trying to stop his feet from taking another step further.

Further from him.

"Taiga," he begged as Taiga shrugged him off. "Please let me explain–"

He couldn't do anything but follow as Taiga refused to listen.

"Taiga… Please… Please stop… Let me explain. I'll explain everything. Just–... Just give me a chance."

"Please…"

"Please, Taiga…"

Hokuto hated how he was pleading just like Hinako had been just before.

"Please… Taiga, just talk to me!!"

But what other choice did he have?...

"Please!!"

Hokuto was ready to plead forever until Taiga snapped.

"Why should I?!"

His feet stuttered back when Taiga swung around, finally facing him as they stood at the center of the bridge by Salut.

Hokuto thought he would know what to say. He wouldn't have chased him if he hadn't, but the moment Taiga turned to him, every word from his mouth was lost.

He never wanted to see him make this kind of face.

He had said so before when no one could hear just how deeply he had fallen.

It hurt more knowing that he was the reason Taiga's eyes were filled with ire and regret.

"Why should I stand here and listen to you ?? Just so I can let you lie to me more??"

"What could you possibly tell me that makes it worth standing here one more second with you?? That you didn't make a bet with Juri?? That I wasn't all just a game this whole time???"

"What is it, Matsumura?..."

Hearing Taiga return to his last name stung.

It took so long for that distance to close. It was just a name. All it was, was a name, but it made Hokuto believe that there could have been something. That Taiga felt something for him.

Now, that was all gone.

Taiga's eyes blazed as his mouth snapped out his words.

"Tell me."

"Tell me Takeuchi was lying. Tell me that you didn't make that bet– Tell me with that fucking bracelet on your wrist that she was lying!!"

Hokuto wanted to. More than anything, he wanted to say that it all wasn't true. Just so he could return to holding Taiga in his arms for at least one more night.

But he couldn't.

He was sick of lying.

He wanted it to be real and he wanted to be himself. He wanted to be honest with his heart and know that the person who listened would accept it.

He was tired of bending the truth just to make things work.

Hokuto was done lying, even if it only made it worse.

"... I-... I can't…"

Taiga's fists clenched.

"Why…? Tell me."

"Ta– Kyomoto, just listen to me. I was never going to take the money, I–"

Hokuto tried to close the distance that seemed to grow with each passing second, reaching out to take Taiga's hand, but Taiga pushed his touch away from him, retreating back again.

"No!!"

"Fuck that!!!"

"Why should I believe you!? You lied to me!! This whole time you lied to me!!"

"No!! That's not true!! I meant everything!! Please, Kyomoto, just–!" Hokuto tried to reason, but Taiga only clutched his head as he yelled.

"Shut up!!!"

"Shut up!!!!!"

For a second, Taiga nearly fell for it.

For a second, he wanted to forgive everything and listen, taking and accepting Hokuto's sweetened words, just so he could go back to believing he had Hokuto's warm smile. That he could really have the time Hokuto promised him just a week before, but the pain in his chest still burned as he bit at his inner cheek, the anger flooding over his despair.

"It's just as she said, isn't it??"

"Everyone is the same!! No one matters!! We're all just plaything for you to fuck around with until you get bored!!"

"Except for her ."Taiga pointed past Hokuto towards Salut. "She's the one you can never say no to, right? She's the only one you really care about!"

"No one else matters."

Taiga had fought so hard to deny it. He wanted to believe in Hokuto. Even despite all of Hinako's words, he had tried so hard to believe that all of Hokuto's kind and comforting gestures and words all could have been real.

But as Taiga's words spilled from his lips, it was as if each of them became true.

It never mattered.

It never meant anything.

He never mattered.

He never meant anything.

To Hokuto, Taiga had always meant nothing.

Taiga let out a bitter laugh as Hokuto stared.

"... I just took more of your time because I came with a cash prize."

"No!!!"

Those words made Hokuto's heart sink enough to force his voice from his chest. "No!! It's not like that!!! Kyomoto, if you would just please let me speak–!!"

"Why should I?? Just so you can just pump me full of your lies!?! No!!! I won't listen!!"

It hurt.

All of it hurt.

Taiga wanted so badly to listen.

He wanted to listen to Hokuto tell him in his warm voice that it all wasn't true. That he was wrong. That he mattered. That he was worth something. That he meant something. That he was worth something to him. That all gentleness and care actually meant something.

That Hokuto loved him.

For a week, Taiga thought it was all true.

But how could he possibly believe in any of that anymore?

"I have you all figured out…" Taiga breathed, refusing to let the stinging in his eyes bring tears. "You're exactly the person I thought you were from the very beginning."

"You're just a lecherous piece of shit!!"

"Things like love don't mean anything to you!! You just use your looks to take advantage of women but so you can live as a self serving selfish bastard!!! It's not anything to you!!! It's just a tool for you!!! You don't care how it makes people feel!!! It's all about you! Only you!! You and her!!!"

"You don't know how it feels for it to hurt, do you!?!? No one has ever told you no, have they??? That's why you don't care!! You only care about yourself!!!"

The words burned in Taiga's throat. "I'm the same!! I'm just the same as everyone else!!! Money was all I was ever worth!!!! You just used me!!!!! You disgust me!!! I'm sick of you, you and your fucked up idea of—!!!"

"And what about you!?!!"

When Hokuto screamed back, Taiga's tongue tripped, cutting off his hateful speech.

Hokuto's voice felt like it pierced through him, making Taiga's head snap up to meet the eyes that had only watched him even now.

It had taken so long for Taiga to believe he could understand the messages in Hokuto's eyes, but now, when it mattered most, he couldn't read them at all.

The bite in Hokuto's voice sank into his heart, but then why did it look like tears could have built in his eyes?...

Taiga didn't understand.

He couldn't understand.

Hopelessness.

Remorse.

"You used me too!!!" Hokuto yelled, his speech nearly cracking in his throat. "You pulled me around and pushed me back and forth just because Juri never loved you!! You used me as a cheap replacement!!!"

"What could you ever understand about me!?! You don't know anything about me!! It was always about you!!!"

For years, Hokuto had held back his voice. For so long, he had kept his mouth shut because he was afraid of what would happen if he did. He had always kept his lips sealed, nodding and agreeing with Hinako because he believed he loved her and that his silence would bring him a 'Happily Ever After'.

For the first time, he had a reason to speak.

A reason to escape. A reason to finally do something for himself.

Taiga had shown him it could be different.

For Taiga, he wanted to speak.

Taiga made him feel free. Taiga made him feel as if he could finally understand why love could be worth so much.

Hokuto wanted to say he would be back at his door tomorrow. He wanted to say that Taiga had all his time.

He wanted to tell him just how much he loved him.

Yet, his anguish and anxiety of losing it all took control as he screamed.

What Taiga yelled at him made him feel like a stranger.

Those moments where Taiga seemed to understand everything about him felt so distant and foreign.

How could Taiga ever understand what he went through?

How could he ever understand the ache he felt watching Hinako return home to another man every morning?

How could he ever understand how long his heart had been battered and bruised?

How could Taiga ever know just how much he wanted to feel love again?...

"How could you possibly understand anything about me!?!!! How can you tell me how fucked up my perception of love is!?!!?"

"You don't even understand it!!!!!!"

Screaming back felt good.

For a moment.

To finally use his voice.

But as soon as his high faded, all the regret and guilt flooded back, dragging him back down.

As Hokuto regained his focus and caught his breath, Taiga didn't say anything.

He just stood there. Silent and wide eyed.




Shattered.




Hokuto's heart fell into his stomach when Taiga's feet began to turn.

Everything was falling apart.

"Wait–"

Hokuto tried to grab his arm, but Taiga tore himself out of his grip before striking his hand away from him.

Taiga didn't yell. He didn't scream.

He didn't have the energy to anymore.

Hokuto was right.

Taiga didn't understand.

Things like romance and love never made any sense to him. He didn't understand how someone could be so important or how teenagers cried over break-ups. He didn't get how someone could willingly give up half of their heart.

He couldn't understand how someone could always be on their mind. How someone could always want them beside them. How someone could simply just want to see their smile.

Taiga never understood.

But for the first time, he wanted to.

And for one week, Taiga thought he had.

His chest felt cold, surely only because he knew what it was like for it to be warm.

"Don't touch me."

Taiga looked at Hokuto one last time, the throbbing in his head too painful to bring tears as his speech barely came out with his breath.

He wouldn't let the way Hokuto looked at him sway his heart, no matter how desperately he called for him or how badly Taiga wished to run back.

He shook his head, eyes locked with Hokuto's.

"Don't come near me."

No more.

Enough of his sweet words.

"Don't call me. Don't text me."

He was done with the safety of his embrace.

"Don't touch me."

He wouldn't let Hokuto have any more of his heart.

No more.

"Don't ever show your face in front of me ever again."

He was done.

As Taiga walked away, all Hokuto could do was watch.

Not once did Taiga look back, no matter how much Hokuto wanted him to.

What could he do?... Nothing he could say would change anything.

He truly loved him, whether Taiga would have believed it or not.

He wanted Taiga to be the one to set him free. To teach him what love was really worth, what a true and pure love really felt like.

… It didn't matter now.

Taiga would never ask for him again.

Hokuto collapsed, dropping his back against the concrete barrier of the bridge as he curled into himself, grabbing at the back of his hair.

His lungs shook as he brought himself to breath before tears flooded his eyes.

It was over.

Hokuto turned when he heard footsteps behind him.

When he saw who it was, he turned back to the front door of Salut to unlock it, now knowing it was the absolute last person in the world he wanted to see.

“... What the hell are you here for?”

Juri watched Hokuto pull out his keys from his back pocket before letting out a quiet sigh.

He pointed at the collection of keys in Hokuto’s hand.

"That."

“I’m here for that.”

Hokuto didn’t need to know which key he was asking for because he already knew.

Deep inside, he wanted to keep it. He hoped that he could have, even if it would only hang there unused until it was lost as it was a memory of what once was.

But it was also a reminder of what would never be.

Hokuto scowled before prying open the ring and tugging off the one key that was added to the many he had had for years. His feet dragged as he stepped over to Juri and shoved it into the chest of his three-piece suit before returning to the door.

"There. Now get lost."

Juri sighed again, taking the key to grasp tightly in his hand as he watched Hokuto struggle for the first time with the front door, jamming the key into the lock.

“Hokuto.”

“Shut up. I don’t want to talk to you.”

This whole thing with Juri showing up at Salut alone was much too close of a reflection of that night for Hokuto to feel anything but bitterness. The only difference was that last time, he was closing instead of opening.

That night many months ago, Juri and Hokuto had made a deal.

Juri had shown up at the front door as an old friend wanting to reconnect after moving away to sit down for just a couple drinks.

"Hey Hokuto. You know a lot about romance and stuff, right? You're able to attract all these girls here," Juri had said then.

He had smiled as he set his chin in his palm, leaning over the bar and watching Hokuto polish the last few glasses. "I know a guy who could really need some help…"

"Do you mind giving me a hand?"

Hokuto wanted so badly to shut the door in Juri's face after slipping inside Salut, but his conscience got the better of him, choosing not to potentially injure his friend who followed in after by impulse. Even when he was pissed at him.

Hokuto walked to the register, not sparing Juri any courtesy or service as he didn't even face him to speak. "If you’re going to come in, you have to be a paying customer."

"Are you even ready to serve anything?"

"No. So, get out."

Juri frowned, crossing his arms with his briefcase still in hand as Hokuto tried not to take out his anger on the cash register.

"It won't be long. Just listen to me for a second."

Taiga didn't give him that grace. Hokuto didn't have to give it to Juri either, but Juri showed no signs of leaving and Hokuto didn't have the energy to physically carry him out the door, settling on the silent treatment instead. The idea was that if he just didn't respond, maybe Juri would just give up and leave, finally giving Hokuto some peace.

Unfortunately, Hokuto knew Juri well enough that it wouldn't work that easily.

That asshole was always so persistent.

"If you want to ignore me, that's fine," Juri said as Hokuto did his best to turn his voice into white noise. "I just want to make one thing very clear…"

"I never told you to fall in love with him."

Juri didn't flinch when Hokuto slammed the register drawer shut.

Hokuto wished he could have done the same with Juri's mouth, but all he could do was let it keep on running as he went to fix the tables, trying to find something to do besides listening.

He pulled the chairs off and shoved them under their tables as Juri just stood and watched.

"It's obvious you're mad at me. And that's fine, be pissed off all you want, but you can't pin this all on me. All I asked you was to teach him about love."

Hokuto jammed a chair in with a deafening screech on the floor, hating that he knew the sound nor the rage would stop Juri's words.

"I wanted to help you. You needed money, right? You weren't going to just take it. I gave it a reason. You accepted the bet on your own."

The crashing of the wood against the hard floor boomed through the room after Hokuto had planted his hand on the back of the seat and sent it flying under the table, not caring how it bashed into the furniture and fell to the floor.

"Why are you here?!"

Hokuto couldn't keep his blood from boiling.

Did Juri just come in here to make him more miserable? To tell him his one outlet to blame was invalid??

He knew he was putting it all on Juri. He knew Juri was right.

Hokuto just wasn't ready to accept that he was the only one to blame for why Taiga was gone.

His heart was already broken. Did he really have to carry the weight of the blame now too?

All he wanted was to make Juri the villain for just a bit longer. Just until he wouldn't be completely crushed by the responsibility.

It only pissed him off more seeing Juri standing there, calm and collected, like he had any right to feel that he was above him while every second that passed, Hokuto felt like he was going to fall apart.

"You're the other half of the deal! Why are you lecturing me like you're not just as fucked up as I am!!! Are you not also in deep shit??"

Hokuto barked at him, saying anything to make him feel better. Anything to alleviate the crushing weight on his chest.

"I am."

"Then why??"

Hokuto blinked, his chest still heaving, when Juri raised his hand from across his chest to show the key that was tucked between his fingers. "My payment."

"He told me if I brought him this, he would let me inside to state my case for 5 minutes."

Juri slipped the key into his breast pocket, adjusting his clothes as he spoke. "I'm planning on getting on my hands and knees and begging for forgiveness."

"If that doesn't work, then I'll do it again tomorrow. And the next day. And the next until he does."

"So, yes. I'm in deep shit. I could lose my job, but frankly, I'm more concerned about losing an important friend. He doesn't have to forgive me, but I'm going to try like hell to fix what I can."

"So." Juri exhaled as he dropped his briefcase back at his side. "What are you planning to do?"

Under Juri's focused eyes, even after all the yelling and cursing, Hokuto found himself speechless.

He didn't know. He honestly hadn't even considered it.

After what happened, he didn't even think that he could do anything.

His mouth opened as he stammered, lost for words.

"I-... I don't-"

The door rang as Jesse stepped inside, his usual direct line to the kitchen interrupted by Hokuto and an unfamiliar guest. He raised an eyebrow as he tugged at the strap of his bag on his shoulder.

"Oh. Uh, good morning?..."

Juri turned, presenting his usual business smile to him as if Hokuto hadn't been screaming at him just earlier.

"Good morning! Sorry for intruding."

Jesse glanced at the chair laying on its side on the floor before looking back to Juri who approached him, side stepping around him to reach the door. "Was there something you needed?"

"Nope! I got everything I need. Thank you for asking though," Juri smiled as he pushed at the handle for his exit before turning behind him one last time.

"Hokuto."

The gaze that Hokuto let fall to the ground jumped up to him when Juri's cheerful tone changed.

"Contact me if you need anything, okay?"

The smile on his face was gone, leaving only the concern in his eyes before he disappeared behind the door.

Both Hokuto and Jesse watched it close shut in silence before Jesse glanced over to Hokuto who was still frozen in place.

"... Hokuto?..."

"... Are you alright?..."

Hokuto finally breathed, his body reanimating as everything started to sink in.

"... No."

"I'm not."

What was there that could he possibly do?...

Taiga would surely forgive Juri. After all, he has loved him once. Or still did, for all Hokuto knew.

But even if he were to do the same thing, begging on his hands and knees with his forehead pressed to the floor, Taiga wouldn't forgive him.

He had said terrible things. He had done terrible things, but even still, Hokuto really truly loved him despite everything and that was what hurt the most.

From the beginning, the money was always meant to free him from his debt with Hinako. He accepted the deal without a second thought because he could already imagine himself pushing the cash into her hands and telling her that he was done, that he was done fooling himself into believing that he was fine having payments as her affection while she held the key to the financial shackles around his wrists.

But as the months went by, he never expected that he would have found more.

Taiga's love would have been enough.

At the beginning, the only reason why Hokuto pushed to know more about Taiga was for the 1,000,000 yen. Juri had described him and Hokuto recognized him from the month before when he came in for the company party. The cash was the goal, but as time went by, Hokuto had to remind himself where it all started as he kissed him.

He didn't need the money anymore. He didn't even want it, as long as he had Taiga. With Taiga, he could turn Juri down and endure saving coin by coin until he could set himself free. Until he could give Taiga his everything.

The money was worth nothing compared to Taiga's kiss.

But now he was left with nothing.

Nothing, as days, months and years blurred past with Hokuto never gaining the courage to call the number Shintaro eventually deleted from his phone for him.

No money. No Taiga.

Not even Hinako.

Just an image of a future that he had once hoped would come true.

One with Taiga beside him.

And a love worth everything.
