Wait

Chapter Notes

See the end of the chapter for notes

"Thank you, please come again."

The elderly woman smiled and thanked Hokuto, taking the plastic bag filled with her purchases from his hand before the tiring repeated jingle of the sliding doors played as she left.

Hokuto watched her leave, the doors coming to a close behind her as he sighed, listening to the quiet giggling of the teenage girls assigned as his coworkers softly echoing through the convenience store.

"The weather is warm again today. Be careful as the air is humid and will increase the feeling of today's heat. Make sure to use air conditioning as needed–"

The weather forecast played from the monitor mounted above the register, registering in Hokuto's ears as white noise as he took the broom and brush pan to sweep while the store was empty of customers.

It had been 3 years since he last saw Taiga. 

After going back to Salut that night, Hokuto finally unloaded his whole heart to Hinako, telling her he was done feeling like second best and nothing but a physical playtoy for her pleasure. No matter how much she cried, Hokuto wouldn't listen, his heart cold and numb after watching Taiga walk away.

A month or so after, Hinako arrived at his door with an apology.

The moment he saw her, he expected her to throw herself at him, crying and begging for him to stay with her as she did when he finally said they were over when he returned to Salut, but from the way she spoke, it was hard to turn her away.

It had been forever since Hokuto had heard her talk in a voice so soft and genuine, it almost felt like they had turned back time. 

"Hokuto… I'm so sorry… I've been horrible to you…" she said as she clutched her purse in her hands. "I was selfish and only did what and what I needed…"

"But this time, I promise I'll listen…"

"I love you, Hokuto… I can't imagine my world without you."

"Please… give me one more chance."

Any normal person would have said no.

By every means, Hokuto should have said no, but the emptiness and ache that had sunk deep into his chest over the months alone made his heart cling to anything that could possibly mend its broken pieces. 

Hinako had been his world before. Maybe she could be his world again.

Hokuto and Hinako tried to make things work. 

The Hinako that Hokuto had let into his home was different. She was sweet, kind and patient as she loved him sweetly. There were no gifts, expensive dinners or luxurious hotel rooms. It was just them. 

Again, Hinako spoiled him.

Just not with items of high price tags, but with her time and her care as they spent their quiet evenings at each other's side. Hinako still returned home to her husband every night, but not without first pressing a longing kiss to his lips before she left.

And as Hinako promised, she listened.

She listened, agreeing to a simple dinner at home, letting Hokuto serve and pamper her as he had wanted to for so long, knowing and feeling her affection in simple words.

It was everything Hokuto could have asked for.

Years ago, Hokuto had dreamed of nights like this, finally having Hinako curled into his side as the wasted daylight away watching TV as if they were the only two people in the world.

Years ago, Hokuto's heart would have soared.

But his heart had changed.

As Hinako kissed him, it yearned for a different kiss. As Hinako hugged him, it wished for a different embrace. A different scent. A different warmth.

A different love.

As much as Hokuto tried to drag back the love he had from years ago to the surface, he couldn't.

Hinako had noticed too.

"... Hokuto?..."

Hokuto's eyes fluttered, coming back to focus from Hinako calling his name as she was tucked against his side.

The movie that played before them was one that he had seen before, but back then, he hardly could hear any of the words. Back then, all he could hear was the heart beat of the man beside him as it played through its runtime of 112 minutes.

When Hinako had asked him if he had seen it before, he didn't exactly lie when he said no. 

After all, he never did end up watching the ending.

"Sorry… Did you say something?" Hokuto said, giving her shoulder a squeeze.

"... I did…"

"Oh… I'm sorry, I just–…" 

He couldn't admit that even with her at his side, his mind was with someone else.

"I was just thinking about work…" he lied. "What were you saying?..."

Hokuto blinked when Hinako pulled away from him and clicked off the TV.

For a moment, he thought she was mad. That maybe, that side of her that had laid dormant for the past weeks would resurface and return them to where they were before.

"I was just saying…"

But her voice was soft… though her words still stung more than Hokuto would have thought.

"You don't love me anymore… Do you?..."

"I'm making you miserable."

At first, Hokuto lurched forward, conditioned to shout and deny, to again, tell her over and over that his love was true. 

"No– Hinako, I'm sorry. I just–"

Hokuto would have never imagined that she would be the one to ask for the truth as she placed her hand on his chest, her eyes gently asking for earnesty.

"Hokuto… It's okay… you can be honest with me," she smiled gently.

"I'm ready to listen."

Hokuto hadn't realized tears had fallen from his eyes until Hinako leaned in to brush them from his cheek.

"I'm sorry, Hinako…" His voice came out only as a whisper as she held his cheek. 

"I'm sorry…"

Once his tears had stopped, they quietly agreed to part.

Hinako collected her things, placing them into the large designer purse Hokuto hadn't realized she had brought with her.

She must have arrived knowing how the night would end.

Hinako never carried more than she needed.

"Will you be okay?" Hokuto asked as she threw away her spare toothbrush and folded her scarf into her bag. 

"Don't worry, Hokuto… I'm a big girl now. I can handle it." Hinako chuckled, standing with the straps grasped in her hands.

"I decided to tell my husband that I want to be closer to him." She wore a big smile as she turned to him, brushing down his collar for him one last time. "I've been reading a lot lately. It's been comforting and it gave me a little push I needed to move in the right direction."

Hokuto's brow pinched, watching her turn towards the door. He knew that she used to love reading once, but he had thought it was a hobby long gone.

"I'm happy to hear that it's been helping you… Was there a book that caught your interest?"

"No, not particularly."

"Then what–"

"Let's just say it's a secret," she laughed, unlatching the door as Hokuto decided to let his curiosity go. 

Before she stepped out, Hinako perked up as she turned on her heels. "Oh! As for Salut's rent, I can still–"

"No." 

She blinked as her hand paused on the all too familiar envelope in her bag. As she looked up at him, Hokuto suddenly felt awkward, but he smiled to push the feeling away.

"I-… I won't take money from you anymore…"

"I won't rely on you anymore… or I'll never move on."

There was a certain somberness that washed over them as they fell silent.

Even though they no longer had any love between them, it didn't change the fact that there was once a love that was now coming to an end. No matter how mangled and twisted it was, both of them had once cherished it and treasured it dearly.

Hinako sighed with a smile on her pink tinted lips, letting her mourning disappear with her breath before she shoved the envelope into his chest, making Hokuto stumble back.

"Hinako–"

"Just take this last one." She took Hokuto's hand to place it over the white parcel on his chest. "As my apology… for everything…"

As she stepped out the door, Hinako stole one last kiss from his cheek.

"And thank you for loving me."

The envelope only held enough to pay rent for one more month.

Maybe Hokuto should have just let her continue to pay as a way to make up for the years of emotional battering, but couldn't bring himself to accept it, not if he wanted to set both her and himself free. 

Salut was doing well and was better equipped to support itself since its hard beginnings, but it was still far from being able to pay its own rental fees without Hinako's support. 

Hokuto couldn't bring himself to cut Jesse or Shintaro's pay, they already worked for less than what Hokuto wished he could pay them and it wasn't their fault for the choices he selfishly made himself. He tried to run the costs of selecting cheaper vendors or buying in bulk, but nothing would save enough spendings without hindering the business or sacrificing its quality.

All Hokuto could do was take loans and offer his physical labor to make ends meet.

The master at the bar he used to work at was more than excited to hire him during weekend evenings again while Hokuto was able to work out a schedule with a nearby convenience store during the day.

If it sounds tiring, it's because it was.

Hokuto barely had the time to rest, working 7 days a week, mornings, days, and evenings to earn as much as he possibly could before all his free time was spent on sleep. Even then, only after Jesse and Shintaro cornered him and argued with him on cutting their own pay, Hokuto was able to pull together enough to afford their rent.

It was exhausting and ran him down to the bone, but in a way, it made the last 3 years easier to handle. 

Just as Taiga told him that last day, Hokuto never called or messaged. 

He didn't even ask Juri about him, despite his well intended offer. There was no point. There was nothing that could change anything. 

Not once did Hokuto ever doubt his words. 

Taiga said he never wanted anything to do with him again.

Hokuto had no reason not to believe him.

So Hokuto let himself be consumed by his work until Taiga became a blur in his past that came as quickly as it disappeared. Whatever Hokuto had hoped they would be or wished they would have been slowly died and faded with time as he sold himself to his work. 

Slowly, the sound of the smooth tenor of his voice became tarnished and distant. The rich color of his eyes became dull and hazed.

The gentle hesitance of his touch.

His warmth.

His care.

His sweetness.

His love.

It all blended and melted into a bitter and painful memory of something he wanted more than anything, slowly forgetting as time flew by.

The first few months, Hokuto had wondered about Taiga's deadline and if he ended up meeting it, but when he checked the future release list ST Publishing put on their website, none of the novels ever had the name Kyomoto Taiga attached to it.

It was hard for Hokuto not to feel that he was to blame, but even so, all it did was add to the list of things Hokuto already blamed himself for, alongside items such as "ruining Taiga's ability to ever trust in love" and "destroying every last chance for Taiga to believe in love". The thought sank the heavy weight of guilt on his shoulders, but what more could it do when Hokuto was already completely crushed by it? 

Just one more reason for Taiga to hate him could only add so much to make Hokuto hate himself even more.

The plastic dustpan clattered as Hokuto finished gathering what he could from the linoleum floors, glancing up at the click.

Another 4 hours, then he would work at the bar until 2 in the morning. Tomorrow, he had to wake at 6 to open Salut.

Hokuto could already feel his fatigue sink into his frame. 

The store jingle played again as the doors gilded open, Hokuto forcing a grin as he bowed, fighting against his overworked body.

"Welcome in!"

Once the 4 hours of meticulous busy work was over, Hokuto scarfed down a discounted bento from the store before driving to the bar to work the evening shift.

"Your Manhattan, miss."

Hokuto spoke in a low tone, allowing himself to lean towards the woman as he smoothly placed the martini glass on the bar counter.

She was into him. He could tell. Out of all the seats at the bar she could have chosen, she selected the one right in front of where he worked.

As expected, the master wanted Hokuto to lay his charm on thick just as he did before, wooing and swaying customers with his words to drain as many drinks into them as he could. With the bonus attached, Hokuto had no reason not to…

"Thank you… It looks beautiful." She smiled, looking through her long lashes as took her drink. "Can I assume it would taste just as good as you?"

Hokuto stopped himself from flinching when she tapped her nails over his fingers, forcing sweet words from his lips with a smile. "... Maybe… What about sticking around to find out?"

… But after Taiga left, Hokuto could never quite do it the same.

Each time he told a woman she was beautiful or was lovely to speak with, it felt like a bold faced lie. It didn't matter if she was beautiful or not, all the words his tongue could form felt empty and heartless. 

Maybe it was because he was finally tired of his sweetened lies, but maybe, it was because there was still the faded image of a person he truly found to be beautiful in his mind as he spoke. Even a small caress made his skin crawl, serving as a reminder of the touch that had once made his nerves spark and his heart race.

It was like he was cheating, though he was devoted to no one.

Well, maybe he was.

But that person didn't want him to be.

Hokuto wanted to collapse to the floor as soon as he reached his apartment after finally returning home at 2:21 am. His body was sore and tired and his clothes reeked of sweat and bourbon as he tore them off to stumble into the shower, but not without taking the bottle of whiskey he stole from the restaurant with him.

He was the one who ordered it. So he should be allowed to drink it.

The shower scalded his back and his scalp as he drank from the bottle, burning his insides at the same time and hoping it would swiftly bring him a rest that wouldn't last long enough.

And by the time he shut the water off, it was half empty.

His feet dragged as he ruffled his towel through his hair, eyes glazed and blurred as he tore open his bedside drawer for a box holding only scraps he had fished out from the garbage forever ago.

He emptied the contents onto his kitchen table, his fingers fumbling as pushed the pieces together to reform a word he would never hear from its writer's voice ever again.

The droplets from Hokuto's hair fell around it as his vision came to focus as the last two letters came together.

Thanks.

Somehow, even the period at the end charmed him.

Hokuto stared, hands planted on the table as he read the one word note over and over and over until it sounded like nothing.

"... I want to hear you…"

"I want to see you…"

The pieces crumpled as he clutched them in his hand as if they were him.

"I want to hold you……"

Touch him.

Love him.

But Taiga told him not to.

All Hokuto could do was comply and only dream of a person who slowly disappeared from his life.

 

 

"Hokuto."

"What."

"Hokuto!!"

"What!?!"

Hokuto swung around, hands still fumbling with the ever growing amount of order slips he tried to organize in the service window. "What is it, Shintaro?? Can't you see I'm trying to do something here??"

He didn't mean to snap at him, but no matter how many plates he delivered, the number of orders never seemed to shrink in size.

"I know, I know!! But listen to me–!!"

"Just say it already!!"

"I don't think we have enough stock to feed everyone!"

Hokuto froze, the issue with the order slips becoming microscopic in comparison as they nearly fell from his hands.

Salut had never seen so many customers.

No one in the staff had any clue or any time to find out the reason why.

It started around Wednesday when there seemed to be an unusual influx of customers. It was a pleasant surprise as it brought it more earnings, but by Friday, it had become unmanageable.

It wasn't extremely uncommon to see a line out the alley, but around the front and almost to the end of the block was completely unheard of. 

They had already hesitantly increased stock Thursday night, unsure if it was just some fluke and that maybe other restaurants in the area had been closed, but by 4 pm today, it had become gravely apparent that it wasn't nearly enough. They had already tried their best, sending Shintaro to buy what he could find locally while Hokuto and Jesse tried to manage the floor and kitchen on their own, but the efforts were fruitless. As much as they wanted to serve all the customers who were willing to wait, their staff that worked perfectly for a small bistro was simply not strong enough to handle the rush of people who had hoped to have a meal before returning to work. 

Hokuto slapped down the slips, speaking quickly as he hastily rummaged through the bar drawers to find a notepad and paper. "Start going down the line and asking if they want reservations for Monday. Only accept phone numbers, not emails." 

As he shoved them into Shintaro's hands, he could already see the panic in the boy's eyes worsen.

"B-but, we've never done reservations before–!"

"We are now."

"What do I even–"

Before Shintaro could fully express his hesitation, knowing full well that reservations took much more than just a phone number, Hokuto was turning him and pushing out from behind the bar. 

"Just do it! Don't make any promises! Apologize first and tell them we're working on it!!"

The additional stress was taking a toll on Hokuto's already overworked body. If he had been working on fumes before, now he was barely functioning on the wheezing gasps of what his energy bank had left. 

He was barely able to give any time to the customers as he usually liked. As soon as an order was taken or a dish was delivered, he had to speed off to refill water or to seat another party. Deep inside, he was incredibly thankful as he was too physically and mentally drained to even try to make any flirtatious small talk, but he couldn't deny that he was surprised that none of the women who sat down didn't seem to mind.

Hokuto wasn't stupid enough to know that before today, besides the food, he was the main attraction.

But now, the women promptly made their order before returning to whispering between themselves, hardly paying him any mind.

"It really is exactly like it!"

"Besides the crowd, the atmosphere is really nice."

"The food is almost perfectly described! Hey, do you want to come back next week? I want to try the creme brulee!"

"What about the cherry clafoutis? There's no way it's as delicious as it sounded, right?"

Hokuto didn't have the time to process the gossip stirring around him as he weaved table to table, trying to finish the last of the orders they were able to fulfill while bowing and apologizing for unavailable dishes before tempting them with what they could provide. With the combined efforts of his quick work and Shintaro turning away customers at the door, what was left of the crowd was worked away, filling their stomachs as they left happily, regardless of if it was full of what they came for.

Jesse threw himself over the bar, dirtied with food and utterly exhausted after Shintaro locked the door and flipped the closed sign over with a handwritten note hanging from the bottom. 

Due to shortage of stock. 

Please return tomorrow.

"... If this happens again next week, I might just die," Jesse groaned into the wooden counter.

"You can't die," Hokuto replied tersely, his mind busied with trying to comprehend just how much their income had spiked the last few days. "You'll make Kochi cry."

Jesse responded with another tired groan as he sank into his stool.

The loud clang of Shintaro's just emptied and oversized water bottle made both of them flinch as he slammed the metal bottom into the table with an exaggerated sigh from draining its contents into his stomach.

Hokuto and Jesse had expected a joke.

But Shintaro had always been surprisingly serious when it came to work.

"Seriously." He huffed.

"We need more staff."

Both Hokuto and Jesse agreed, Hokuto giving a nod as Jesse's shoulders slumped in defeat, pulling his phone from his pocket.

Jesse flicked his thumb, scrolling through his contacts with his head still resting against the table top. "I'll see if I can find someone for next week. Even if it's just temporary."

"Thanks, Jess." Hokuto sighed as he closed the register. "I think I'm going to go get some rest before work tomorrow."

"Huh??"

Shintaro leaned over the counter, his brow furrowed and mouth open in disgruntled shock. "Are you seriously going to still work part time tomorrow!?! You'll turn to dust if you go in!! If Jesse gets one more body and you're nothing but sand, we'll be back at a body count of 3! And if I know math, that's not an improvement!"

Hokuto let himself laugh a little, though even the bit of joy made his body ache. 

"With the extra sleep, I should be able to do just fine by Monday. The extra hands will be a huge help as well," he said as he rubbed his sore neck. "It would also be great if you could call back those numbers." 

As much as Shintaro wanted to complain and say no, he wasn't ignorant enough to know just how hard Hokuto had been working. The most he could do was give up part of his pay without prying into Hokuto's private life.

If calling numbers all weekend could help to alleviate Hokuto's stress just the barest bit, then Shintaro would do it.

"... Okay."

Hokuto sighed, knowing that Shintaro was accepting it begrudgingly. Shintaro was always easy to read, no matter how much he tried to hide it.

"I really appreciate it."

"Yeah yeah." Shintaro waved his hand as he took and chuckled the number filled notebook on top of his bag. 

"Just seeing you smile a little makes it worth it."

Hokuto blinked as Shintaro stretched and Jesse sat up, propping himself up with his elbows.

"Before you ask," Jesse cut in with a smile, looking a little revived after his break over the bar counter. "No, you haven't been smiling as much. And yes, we care."

"Just take care of yourself, Hokuto." Jesse chuckled, still cheerful though his body was beaten and tried. "We're just happy to have you lean on us a little."

Hokuto just stared at them, a lump nearly growing in his throat before he swallowed it down.

Jeez…

… Since when did he have such great friends?

As he smiled, Hokuto realized how long it had been since he had used those muscles. Even the service smile he gave when he worked didn't feel the same as when his teeth showed as he laughed.

"Thanks, you two…"

"Now let's clean up so we can get out of here."

The first thing Hokuto did when he got back to his room was eat.

Because only God knew just how much he needed it.

He hadn't been able to cook himself a proper meal in ages instead of swallowing down what scraps there were from the bar or Salut. Not even the discounted meals from the convenience store could compare to finally sitting down and taking time to eat.

He prepared his food like a ritual, carefully cleaning and washing fresh produce then cutting and chopping them steadily before listening to his stove flicker and come to life.

All he prepared was a simple stir-fry with white rice, but the grain had never tasted so good.

Hokuto ate, crunching down on a bell pepper, finally having the time to appreciate and enjoy its sweetness and the taste of sesame oil before washing it down with the round and full taste of rice as he filled his own stomach for once. 

For the first time since that night, the weight on his chest seemed to lighten, if not only for a moment as he ate in silence.

It felt great.

It felt like… he could finally take the first step towards moving on.

It was like the world was giving him a chance to turn everything around, that he could finally enjoy himself again. He had a business that was growing and friends who cared about him. 

It had been 3 years… 

It was about time to finally forgive himself.

To finally forget.

To finally let go.

Hokuto cleared his plate, the scraps of the note still laid out on his table across from him, as if Taiga was there himself, smiling as he ate his food, humming in glee from their shared meal.

"It tastes good."

Hokuto could barely remember how his voice sounded when he had said it, but he would always remember the words said after he had carefully cooked and crafted the dish for him.

His chopsticks clicked against his plate as he ate the last broccoli.




… Maybe it was time to let the words go too.




The image of Taiga began to disappear as Hokuto finished every last grain from his bowl, standing up and setting his dishes away to be handled tomorrow. After a shower and clearing the table, he laid down for a sleep that would only last for a couple hours. 

In the night's silence, Hokuto gazed at his dark ceiling before closing his eyes.

The torn up pieces of Taiga's note lay scattered at the bottom of his trash.

This was the first of many.

The first of many steps to finally forgetting Kyomoto Taiga.

 

 

"It's almost the end of August. We expect to see heavy rains across the Tokyo area this evening. It is advised to stay inside this afternoon or be prepared to dress appropriately for the upcoming weather."

"Aww shoot!"

"Hmm? What's wrong?"

"I didn't bring my umbrella…"

The girl giggled alongside her coworker as they restocked the magazines on the shelf.

"Just buy one from here, silly. Or I can go with you to Donki later."

"Really??" The other smiled with glee, throwing her arms around her friend. "Thank you!! This is why you're the best!!"

Hokuto glanced over to see the two girls cuddling up together, laughing and not really getting their work done.

He wasn't surprised. 

This is how most days went at the convenience store. 

It wasn't like the company was really paying him enough to care if one or two idol magazines didn't make it on the shelf in time for their fan to pick it up at that very moment. He wasn't the manager and he wasn't willing to do anything that was outside of his pay range.

His gaze fell back down to the sketch of Salut's floor plan he had drawn into the notebook laid out on the checkout counter. 

He was considering reorganizing the seating layout. 

With the expectations of reservation, Hokuto pondered whether it would help to reorient the tables to distinguish which were saved seats and which were open seating to keep them from accidentally overlapping. 

He had jotted down the number of tables of chairs as he drew lines and boxes to mimic their placement, running mental scenarios to find what would best maintain their organization and efficiency.

It was nice to have a focus. 

With his work, there was a particular haze that began to dissipate from his mind as he let himself bring his attention back to what mattered in his life. His work and his craft.

That's what he came to the city for in the first place. 

It wasn't to find someone or to find love. 

His passion was what mattered the most.

He couldn't waste his life away.

He couldn't burn his days away thinking and wondering, wishing for and dreaming of what he could have had with–

"Kyomoto Taiga?..."

"Ah! He's the one with the new book last week, right?"

Despite his own words, just his name took out all the air from Hokuto's chest.

Immediately, his head snapped up, his eyes looking at his coworkers who mentioned that name before jumping to the TV above him that they were watching.

Hokuto could feel his mouth go dry.

… How?...

How was it when he was just ready to forget him, he appeared before him like a vision that didn't feel real?...

He felt so far, but so close as even the outdated TV projected his image over the tiny screen.

Despite all of that, Taiga was as beautiful as ever...

… No, he took that back.

Taiga was more stunning than Hokuto could have ever imagined.

Hokuto had already fallen in love with the disheveled Taiga that only ever wore t-shirts and athletic pants that emerged from his nights writing, but with his blonde hair swept back neatly into place and a perfectly fitted suit that framed and accentuated his slender figure, Hokuto found himself breathless.

Every detail Hokuto could see made his chest tighten, from the dark fade that peeked out from under his smooth hair to the silver watch placed on his wrist, and as Taiga raised his head after bowing graciously to the interviewer across from him, accepting the seat offered to him, Hokuto wasn't even aware of his own words that slipped from his lips.

"... He's not wearing his glasses…"

Thank God, no one came into the store at this time, because all Hokuto could do was stare as his heart raced. 

Pounding and throbbing, already falling in love with him again.

"Is this your first time appearing on our show?"

Taiga laughed, bowing his head again. "Yes, my first time on TV actually, so please excuse me for being a little nervous."

"No, not at all! We're just thankful that you agreed to speak with us."

"Of course, thank you for inviting me."

"So, your book 'Silent Conversation'. It was released last week after your extended hiatus."

"Yes, I–"

As the interview went on, Hokuto stared as every blurred and faded memory of Taiga came flooding back with a clarity as clear as the day Hokuto had tried to engrain them into his mind.

He stared, reminded, remembering, every single thing that made his pulse rush and his heart ache.

His gentle voice.

His clear eyes.

His small smile. 

Hokuto remembered everything, from the way he cried in his arms to the way Taiga gazed at him after their kiss broke before he had promised him his everything.

His sadness.

His happiness.

His love.

Hokuto's fingers tightened, not realizing how they creased the pages in his notebook as he watched.

"At the end of your book…" the interviewer asked as she flipped through her cards, "I don't want to spoil it, but readers have been saying there isn't quite an ending."

Taiga smiled politely. "Is there not?... I thought I had ended it quite well."

The interviewer waved her hands in panic. "No! My apologies, I don't mean an ending. I guess it would be better said that there wasn't much clarity with the relationship. Your book isn't labeled as a romance, but many others with me included, found it to be rather romantic."

Taiga laughed.

Hokuto hadn't realized how much he had missed the sound of it.

"... Well… I didn't label it as a romance for a reason."

The interviewer tilted her head questioningly. "Could you explain?"

"I didn't label it as a romance because I don't think it needs to be."

Taiga leaned back in his chair, smiling once seeing his interviewer's confused expression.

Even if the woman across from Taiga didn't notice, Hokuto immediately saw how Taiga's folded hands tightened in his lap.

"That's not to say that those who believe it to be romantic are wrong, they're allowed to read it that way, but that is precisely the reason why. I left the relationship in the book open because I want it to resonate with people whichever way they wish to read it, romantic or not."

"What the characters do and how they act are led by how they feel, whether it's romantic or platonic doesn't matter. It could even be a mix of both, but what matters is that it's understood that there is an affection between them beyond vocalized words."

The interviewer perked up as she shifted in her seat. "Is this also why you made both of the characters men?"

"Well, wouldn't it be strange for a man to be writing about the experience of two women?" Taiga chuckled, crossing his legs. "I don't mean to invalidate your question. I understand why there's some curiosity in the gender choice and it relates back to what I mentioned before."

"Oftentimes in media and entertainment, regardless of the intention, any sort of attention or care between opposite genders is perceived as romantic. I wanted to eliminate those presumptions and have the focus be on their actions and not on whether they're a man or a woman."

The interviewer smiled, immersed in Taiga's words. "... That's wonderful. You mentioned action over words… Could I ask you about that?"

"Of course."

"There isn't much dialogue in your book… and as you had mentioned yourself, it's what the characters do that speaks for them. Could I ask you what inspired you to write with this focus?"

There was a second of hesitation where Taiga looked as if he was lost in thought, but it was quickly covered by a smile and a nod.

"Um… Yes."

His lips parted, closed, before opening again as Taiga carefully selected which words to say. 

As his voice came through the tinny TV speakers, Hokuto forgot how to breathe.

"Someone… once told me that food speaks…"

Taiga looked down at his lap, laughing to himself before he raised his head to continue. "After years of writer's block, that was the first thing that intrigued me. A language I wanted to know, but didn't understand."

"Is this why one of the characters cooks?" She asked.

Taiga nodded. "That's correct. That's where it started, but it grew from there."

"Language and meanings that live beyond words… just because words like 'I love you' aren't said, it doesn't mean that they aren't felt." 

"A mother doesn't have to tell her child everyday that she loves them for him to know. From the way she packs his meals or the way she makes his bed before he returns home can mean plenty enough on its own."

"Things like remembering someone's birthday or noticing their hobbies can speak a thousand words by itself. Supporting their passions, taking time to learn about them. To understand them."

"Cooking for them. Making them laugh when they cry."

"Talking. Being there."

"Giving them your time..."

Taiga paused as he inhaled.

"... I think… these kinds of things can speak louder than words…" 

He blinked, his eyes that had begun to wander refocusing on his talk partner as he laughed. 

"... Don't you think so?..."

She chuckled and nodded. "If I didn't agree before, you've certainly convinced me." 

Taiga chuckled with her. "I got carried away, but in short, it was from a conversation I had with someone once."

The interviewer crossed her arms, her notes abandoned. 

"It sounds like they were quite fascinating to have inspired you so much after such a long block."

Hokuto's fists clenched against the counter before they could begin to tremble, remembering the way Taiga had shoved his spoon into his mousse, demanding him to teach him to cook as Hokuto watched his eyes soften from the screen.

"... Yes…"

"They certainly were interesting."

The interviewer placed down the notes in her lap as she glanced at the queue card behind the camera. "We're about out of time, but before we end, do you mind if I ask one more thing?"

"Sure."

"Have you been able to thank that person?"

All Taiga did was laugh, the airy sweet laugh Hokuto had forgotten just how much he loved. 

"No…"

"I'm not sure if they would even speak to me."

When the door chime sang, piercing through Hokuto's mind as it greeted a customer, Hokuto nearly gasped as he was shaken back to reality.

He tore his eyes from the screen to bow with a smile, welcoming the man in as his heart pounded in his chest before clasping a hand over his mouth as soon as his back was turned.

He tried to steady his hands as his head spun and his stomach churned, sucking air back into his starved lungs.

He wanted to throw up. 

He felt sick.

Just last night, he was ready. He was ready to let it all go, to let all of Taiga go. 

He was ready to let it all disappear as nothing, just a blip in his life's timeline as he finally continued forward, never again thinking again of the person who had changed his life's course, who made him want to change its course.

Time could make his voice and his eyes fade away, even his touch, his kiss and his embrace.

But time could never let him forget how they made Hokuto feel.

Hokuto could never forget how his words overwhelmed him or how his eyes entranced him, or the way his heart sank when he was with Juri and how it sang when they kissed. How blissful it was to hold him in his arms, perfectly curled against his chest as treasured every second with his warmth, yearning for the day that maybe, Taiga would tell him that his kiss meant something .

He could never forget him. He would never forget him.

It was foolish to think he ever could.

Hokuto plastered on a smile as the man came to the counter with an energy drink and a packaged sandwich. He tried to keep his hands from stumbling over the items as he scanned them, forcing his mind to have enough clarity to count and sort the man's change, and as soon as the door jingle played again as it shut, Hokuto breathed, closing his notebook and its plans. 

He paused, staring at the cream colored floors before raising his head back up to the TV where Taiga was now gone from the midday reports and replaced by the news, but his words still lingered in Hokuto's mind. 

… Taiga had said that he wasn't sure if that person would even speak to him… It wasn't wrong to think that he spoke of him, was it?

Unless there was some other person who had taught him about food in the last 3 years, which wasn't entirely impossible, because it didn't make sense.

Taiga was the one who had told him to never see him again. Why would Taiga think that he wouldn't want to speak to him? 

Of course, he wanted to speak to him.

He wanted so much more than just to speak with him.

Hokuto wanted everything…. As long as it was Taiga.

Hokuto's jaw clenched as his gaze dropped to the store shelves, filled with the stale white light.

It wasn't like he could do anything anyways. 

All he could do was wonder.

"Have you read his book?" One of the girls whispered, flipping through a magazine as the other shook her head.

"No, but my mom bought it. She said she couldn't put it down, my dad almost got mad," she laughed.

"I think my sister said he's having a book signing today… I think she's already–"

Both of them jumped when the broom and the dustpan behind the counter clattered to the floor.

But what scared them more was the intensity in Hokuto's eyes as he spoke, leaning over the counter and anxious for their answer.

"Where?"

"When?"

One of them stammered, finding it hard to look Hokuto in the eye as she answered.

"U-um… I didn't ask, so I'm not sure… I-it's probably sometime around now–"

Hokuto was already unbuttoning his uniform.

"That's good enough. Thanks."

They just stared in shock as Hokuto disappeared into the backroom to return with his bag.

"Can you two do me a huge favor?" He asked as he threw it over his shoulder, typing rapidly into his phone. 

The two glanced at each other, the still yet to be sorted magazines clutched in their hands. 

"It depends," one replied, building enough bravery to answer for the both of them. "What's in it for us?"

"Just cover my shift and I'll give you my week's salary. If anything comes up, just call the supervisor." Hokuto said, his eyes still down on his phone.

"Deal."

"Um… Matsumura?..."

When Hokuto looked up, he saw the other girl hiding behind her friend's shoulder as she peered at him with worried and scared eyes. 

He apologized internally as he felt his phone vibrate in his hand, giving a reassuring smile as he opened the counter panel to step out.

"Yes?..."

"Are you a fan of Kyomoto's books?"

Hokuto glanced down at his phone, seeing he got the reply he wanted.

Juri:
J District. Ends in 30 minutes.

Juri:
Unless you're a block away

Juri:
Run.

"... I am…" Hokuto replied.

"I love them a lot."

 

 

The pen squeaked as it drew its tip over the inner cover, leaving curls and curves over the paper before it pulled away with a sharp line.

"Thank you for coming," Taiga said with a smile as the woman nodded, hiding her rosy cheeks behind the newly signed book.

"Um… Kyomoto? Can I ask something?"

Taiga raised his head as he capped his pen. "Sure."

"H-how many times have you… been in love?"

"Huh?"

He blinked as his smile turned crooked, shocked at the question while she bowed in apology. "Uh... Why do you ask?..."

The book moved higher over her face. "I-I was just– um–..."

"... Once."

The cover moved down just enough for her to peek over the top as Taiga repeated his answer with a soft laugh.

"Just once… Is that all?"

She nodded, thanking him profusely before scurrying off as security directed another person to approach his table. 

Hokuto couldn't really hear the conversation, but even if he could, he was too busy trying to pretend that he wasn't even there.

It wasn't that there were no other men in line, it was fairly well mixed, but there were few enough for Hokuto to receive glances from around him. It didn't exactly help that as soon as he tried to run into the line, he was pulled out by security who told him he needed to have a book with him.

He stood out like a sore thumb.

He really wished he could disappear.

Over the years, Hokuto had been able to build a false wall of confidence when it came to service, but when it came to him participating in the general public, he never wanted to attract more eyes than a normal person should. He even frequently wore masks and hats to cover himself when it came to shopping by himself or just taking a stroll.

But unfortunately, as things were, it was rather hard for him to blend in. 

He was happy to finally be close to the front of the line, but just the split second view of Taiga's blonde hair over the shifting of moving heads made Hokuto's blood rush with anxiety and doubt.

What if Taiga didn't mean him?

What if Taiga was speaking of someone else?

What if in the past 3 years, he had someone else?

What would Taiga say?

What would Taiga do?

Would Taiga even let him speak to him, or even come near him?

What would Hokuto say?

What could he say?

The sick feeling came back as his throat grew tight.

Hokuto didn't know.

He had no idea.

But as soon as Taiga's eyes met his as Hokuto soon just before the front of the line, it didn't matter. 

Taiga stared, locked in disbelief before his eyes stuttered over to the woman that approached him as he smiled and apologized. Once she was finished, Taiga glanced at him again as the pair in front of Hokuto went to the table, leaving him at the front of the line.

As long as Taiga didn't call security to throw him out, Hokuto had to at least try.

The staff directed Hokuto to walk forward.

A language beyond words…

… Hokuto just hoped Taiga would understand.

"... Your name?"

Hokuto placed the book he had never opened in Taiga's outstretched hand.

"... Matsumura Hokuto."

The untouched cover creaked as Taiga opened it and uncapped his pen. "... Pardon me for asking but…" 

The dark ink sank into the fresh page as Taiga drew his signature.

"... Have you read my book yet?..."

Hokuto couldn't lie.

He swore he wouldn't, after all.

"... No."

"Then, can I ask why you're here?"

When Taiga looked up at him, Hokuto lost every word he could have prepared from his lips.

Years of flirting and weighted compliments were reduced to nothing when Hokuto was once again faced with Kyomoto Taiga.

Because Kyomoto Taiga was never just someone to play with.

Kyomoto Taiga had always meant something.

Everything .

Hokuto's throat grew dry as he finally got himself to speak.

"... I…"

"... I was wondering if I could make you dinner."

Taiga handed him back the book, a new crease pressed into its spine as Hokuto smoothly pulled it from his grip.

"... Why?"

Neither of them heard the staff telling them it was time to move on to the next person.

As the corner left his fingers, Taiga looked up to meet Hokuto's eyes. "... What will happen if I go?" 

"... I don't know…"

Taiga wasn't wearing his glasses.

Even after 3 years, his eyes were just as breathtaking as the day Hokuto first saw them over those thick frames.

Hokuto forced his tongue to work, his heart pounding in his ears as he nearly saw his reflection in Taiga's clear eyes.




"... I was hoping you would be my boyfriend after."




Taiga blinked.

"... Hoku–"

"I'm sorry, sir. There's a line that we need to finish at the top of the hour, so if you could-"

A staff member gently pushed Hokuto's shoulder, attempting to encourage the moment of his feet towards the exit, but Hokuto's eyes didn't leave Taiga's and Taiga's didn't leave his.

"I'll wait. At the restaurant." 

Hokuto spoke, the staff pushing him again. 

"Sir–"

His feet stumbled as he was pulled away.

"I'll wait."

"I'll wait– I promise-"

It had been so long since Hokuto had felt so lost when Taiga's eyes left his to the new person standing before his table.

He'd wait.

And wait.

Hoping that Taiga would come and give him a chance he didn't deserve.

 

 

It was pouring.

Hokuto had remembered to ask the bar for the day off, but he had forgotten about the weather report from the morning as he did exactly what he said he would do once he returned home.

He waited.

Salut was closed and Hokuto waited outside, not wanting to take a chance on missing the unlikely possibility that Taiga would arrive.

It didn't matter if it was unlikely or not. He had said he would wait and he intended to keep that promise, whether it mattered to Taiga or not.

So he waited.

Even as the rain started and even as people stared at him as they passed, he waited. The ledge of the building kept him dry for a while, but the rain soon over took his shelter, soaking his shoes and below his knees. Still, Hokuto waited, scared that Taiga would come and turn away the moment he went inside for an umbrella.

The hot summer rain slowly drenched his clothes.

The sky grew dark and the sun fell beneath the horizon.

Hokuto stood, waiting, powered only by the glimmer of a hope that Taiga would come.

He checked his phone.

8:21 pm.

It had been about 6 hours since Taiga left his sight… but 6 hours felt like nothing compared to 3 years. 

If Taiga arrived, then it would make it all worth it.

Just for a chance.

A chance that he could hold him again, protect his heart, and finally have a chance to tell him he loves him, even if Taiga was just

going to tell him he couldn't love him back.

The day wasn't over. There were still 3 and half hours left. It was 3 and half more hours Taiga could still come to him.

People stopped passing by and the street grew quiet. Not too long after, there was only the flow of the street lights that flickered on and the storefront signs to keep him company.

Hokuto's foot slipped as he sank to the ground.

He was already almost completely soaked. There was no reason for him to not let the rain have the rest.

The rain soaked into his hair and fell against his cheek as he took out his phone to tap the screen, droplets collecting on the glass.

10:34 pm.

He stared at the number as the rain rolled down along his chin before he wrapped his arms around his knees, dropping his head into his lap.

He hated how he knew there was a limit.

If he could, he would wait forever, but he had to accept he was only human. His body could only last for so long before he would collapse.

He watched the silver of the view of his phone from between his knees where he had placed it on the concrete pavement.

10:35 pm.

Hokuto ignored the whine of his stomach and the shiver down his spine.

He wanted so badly to go back to the time when he was warm with Taiga in his arms.

11:12 pm.

The rain started to let up, but that was the only grace Hokuto was given.

11:56 pm.

If it weren't for the cold and horrible weight of his soaked clothes, Hokuto could have easily fallen asleep.

While the rest he had the night before was plentiful respite, it wasn't nearly enough to keep him awake for much longer.

Hokuto closed his eyes.

When they opened, the time on his phone seemed to mock him.




00:04 flipped to 00:05 am.




Hokuto's mind was blank.

… Three years.

After 3 years, Hokuto saw him again. He had even spoken to him.

… And for what?...

Just a reminder that he could never move on?...

Sick.

The world was twisted and sick.

Hokuto closed his eyes, his head heavy and his body and fingers ice cold.

But maybe this was his bliss.

To see Taiga just one last time.

To be in love with him one last time.

Hokuto could feel his consciousness slipping as his head lulled.

He felt the rain stop.

Maybe that was a sign.

Hokuto looked up, expecting to be blinded by the street light that had always been there to greet him, but he only saw black.

An umbrella.

Hokuto felt like he was hallucinating.


















He had his glasses again.





















"... Didn't you say you would make me dinner?..."
