Chapter Notes

See the end of the chapter for notes

It wasn't going well.

Of course, it wasn't going well.

No one could write when they were in complete emotional turmoil. Only freaks and insane people could manage to bring themselves to be creative.

Even if Taiga were to admit that he was a bit out of his mind, there was simply no way he could bring himself to write.

After he had walked away from that bridge, away from Hokuto, he completely broke down.

The tears hadn't come immediately. He could only assume that it was because the shock hadn't settled as a rage still stirred in his stomach, but after making it 4 blocks down the street, reality came, hitting him like a truck.

Hot angry tears had instantly flooded his eyes, blinding him and forcing his feet to come to a stop.

"Fuck…"

Taiga gritted his teeth, his curse hissing through them as he shoved his sleeved palms against his eyes.

He couldn't stop crying.

"Fuck –...!!!"

Fuck him.

Fuck Hokuto.

Fuck this.

Fuck love.

Fuck romance.

Fuck all of it.

He didn't need it.

It was worthless.

He hated it.

If he hated it before, he hated it even more now.

Love was worth nothing.

Taiga was right all along.

Love was just a cheap trick.

Cheap words. Meaningless action. Just a manipulative tool and empty promises of devotion to make someone believe that another could actually tear themselves apart just so that they would stay beside them. Thinking that they cared. That they loved them. That they were worth something.

It was never anything.

And Hokuto was the same.

Taiga choked on his tears, doubling over in the empty street as his hands clutched into his clothes, wishing it could ease the anger that burned in his throat.

Hokuto lied.

He used him.

He pushed himself into his life and spoke to him about the bullshit called romance.

Hokuto acted like he cared. Like Taiga was different.

He chased him. He held him.

He promised.

The worst part wasn't that all Hokuto wanted was money or even that one of his best friends was in on the bet as well.

The worst part of all of it was that Taiga believed him. That he wanted to believe him. That he even convinced himself to believe him.

That he had fallen, only to be told that he never understood and that he never would understand.

That it would always be nothing.

If Kochi had never miraculously texted him to ask about a reference, Taiga wasn't sure how he would have made it home.

Kochi couldn't bring himself to say no when he had heard the shaking in Taiga's voice, asking to be picked up.

When Taiga got in the car, his face was stained with tears, eyes and nose swollen from abuse. Tears still fell, but everything had turned numb, both his body and his mind, tired of painstakingly repeating words and memories that only wallowed him in despair and regrets.

Kochi only snuck glances as Taiga just let the spare tears roll down his cheeks.

"... I… I'm assuming you don't want to talk about it," Kochi said once he had convinced himself it was at least worth asking.

"... No... I don't."

Kochi focused back on the road. "... I didn't think so…"

Taiga wiped off the tears that fell from the bottom of his chin.

"... Just never talk to me about Matsumura Hokuto ever again."

Once Taiga got home, all he could bring himself to do was sleep.

He didn't eat or shower or work. He just slept since sleeping was the only thing that would make his brain shut the hell up. All his waking moments were only flooded with thoughts that only made him hate himself more than he already did.

The drifting images of Hokuto's ghost in his home only made the hatred sink deeper.

He needed to despise him.

Not wish that he was there.

The first time Taiga had gotten up to do anything more than swallow down an instant noodle to appease his whining stomach, was to answer the knocking on the door that wouldn't stop. All the other knocks were stopped with a text of "leave me alone", "I'm fine. Just go home", or "I don't care. Let them fire me", but this one persisted.

Wishing only to be allowed to sleep again, Taiga took his covers with him to unlock the door to peek through the crack.

He immediately slammed it back shut once seeing who was behind it.

"Kyomo..." Juri tried to call through the door with his forehead pressed against the smooth surface. "I read your text, but you know I can't just leave you alone. Not even because of work…"

"... As a friend."

He knocked again.

"Please let me explain."

"I never meant to hurt you. You know I would never try to hurt you."

"Please. Just 5 minutes. That's all I ask."

Taiga wanted so badly to just curl back in his bed.

He clutched his head, trying to keep Juri's voice from blurring into Hokuto's from that night.

He wasn't ready to forgive him. He didn't want to forgive him.

… But Taiga wanted to burn bridges and there was still one last rope that needed to be cut.

Taiga grimaced as he tightened his blanket around himself before knocking on the other side of the door, bringing Juri to press an ear against the wood.

"... Matsumura has my key…"

Juri heard Taiga's voice from the other side.

"... Bring it back."

"Then I'll give you 5."

It only took 2 hours for Juri to return, the key gleaming in the hallway lights as he held it up to the peephole for Taiga to see his payment.

Taiga begrudgingly opened the door, pushing it open and ready to snap at him that he wouldn't be taking any of his shit excuses, but before he could even begin to speak, Juri's forehead was to the floor before his feet in dogeza.

"Juri-"

"Kyomoto Taiga," Juri spoke into Taiga's entryway. "In my most deepest and sincere apology, I am sorry for what I have done."

Taiga pulled his blanket around himself as he watched Juri at his feet.

… While he felt he deserved it, seeing him like this felt shameful.

"What I did was wrong," Juri continued. "What I did was terrible and I cannot bear to face you and lie to you that I was not responsible. I take complete and utter responsibility for what I have done and I cannot blame anyone for my actions except myself."

"You deserve better."

"You deserve someone you can trust and believe only has your best intentions in mind. I believed myself to be that person, but I had crossed a line I should have never considered."

"I confess that I had made a deal with Matsumura Hokuto regarding the completion of a romance novel for monetary value. While this is true, in my deepest sincerity, all I ever hoped for him to do was to share his insight as a way to help you. I would have never expected for him to behave this way. The intention of the bet was never made on your feelings, only as a way for you to learn. It is your own will whether you choose to believe me or not or to ever trust me again, but I only wish to be truthful with you from now and from now on."

"Again, it is my heaviest of regrets that my actions caused you pain. I will understand if you never wish to speak to me again. I will personally discuss with the company about my work with you and will bear all blame."

"Kyomoto Taiga, I am deeply, deeply and incredibly-"

Juri nearly bit his tongue when Taiga's foot was suddenly shoved at his shoulder. He grunted as he was toppled over before the same foot planted into his stomach, forcing the wind out from his lungs.

He coughed but smiled as Taiga dropped down beside him.

"..... Do you forgive me?"

"... Let me hit you."

"As you wish. Just not the face."

Taiga reeled back his fist, his blanket slipping from his shoulders before dropping the flat of it hard into Juri's suit-covered core, making him clench his teeth and lurch in pain.

"Oof! Wait–! Kyomo! Ow–"

He did it again and again, whacking his first into Juri's stomach and sides, enough to hurt, but not enough to damage muscle.

Punching Juri's soft spots, that were actually only skin and bones, was cathartic. It let Taiga take his anger and frustration out on him as he watched Juri lurch and curl in pain.

It felt good to hurt him.

But at the same time, as his anger was released, it only dragged back up the numbed ache with it.

"Ow–!! Wait, Kyomo! That one actually really hurt!!"

Taiga had dug both of his fists into Juri's flat stomach, crushing his insides. Juri tapped at his shoulder, asking for an out, before coughing as Taiga's weight fell over him.

The punishment stopped, but only because it no longer made Taiga feel any better.

The room fell silent as Taiga pulled his blanket over himself, curling into the rise and fall of Juri's center, letting Juri lay his hand over where he presumed Taiga's head to be under the blanketed lump.

"Kyomo…" he said softly as he watched the white ceiling.

"I really am sorry…"

A quiet muffled voice spoke back.

"... I know..."

"Will you forgive me?..."

"... Not yet... but eventually..."

"I'll wait as long as it takes…"

The two of them stayed like this, both on the floor just feet away from the entryway as Juri gently patted and rubbed Taiga's head and back in silence.

Taiga didn't know at what point he had fallen asleep, but when he raised his head from his nest over Juri's middle, he found his pillow to be dead asleep.

Juri had always been able to fall asleep in the strangest places. Even on a cold hardwood floor wearing a full three piece suit…

Taiga sighed, wrapping his blanket back around himself before laying down beside him to watch the sleeping profile of the man who used to make his heart race.

Used to.

Taiga had loved him…

Maybe…

When Taiga had slept in a cramped bed next to Juri before, without knowing it, there was something about it that had calmed him. There was a comforting warmth that he had never felt before, and at the time, Taiga wanted nothing more than to stay in it. Just being beside Juri gave him a certain bliss he didn't comprehend and an ache he didn't notice until the warmth was gone.

There was a time when Taiga had thought that maybe this was love.

But now, Taiga knew what it was like to be folded in someone's arms.

Now, he knew what it was like to be held against someone's chest and have their voice reverberate within it against his ear. To hear their heartbeat and to feel their heat until the morning came.

To be held by Hokuto.

To have Hokuto.

Even from just his brief slumber over Juri's body, Taiga could tell that with Hokuto, it was different…

The blanket fell to the floor as Taiga's fingers spread over the floor, placing on the space above Juri's shoulders.

…… Hokuto was much warmer.

The blonde strands of his hair slipped from behind his ear as he moved over him, hovering over the man who remained asleep beneath him.

Taiga watched the gentle breaths that left Juri's softly parted lips.




And as he leaned in, he apologized.




To whoever was Juri's girlfriend and was his to be wife, Taiga was sorry.

It would only be once.

Maybe it was wrong for him to steal something so cherished, but Taiga felt that it was only fair.

With this, he would take as the last payment for his forgiveness.

It was only a touch, a simple brush, but months ago, Taiga would have believed this would have made his heart burst. He would have thought he had cursed himself with knowing the feel of Juri's lips, only to know that he wouldn't ever have them again. That he would have made himself watch Juri kiss his bride, knowing that it was something that had only stolen once, but would never belong to him.

It was still true that Taiga would never feel this again and he would still watch Juri say his vows to the mother of his child at the end of the aisle, but the person on Taiga's mind as he kissed Juri wasn't the groom soon to be.

All Taiga could think about was how it was nothing like his last.

His last kiss had been firm, but gentle.

It had a sweet bitterness that made his heart throb during and after they had parted.

It was a kiss that had given Taiga a hope that another would eventually follow, whenever it would be, a week, a month, the next day. Whenever. It carried a promise that he wanted to believe in, that it meant Hokuto would only think of him and he would be the only one…

But maybe some promises were just meant to be broken.

Taiga pulled away, tasting the cigarettes at the end of Juri's breath as he sat back, the other unaware of Taiga's theft in his sleep.

… He thought he would have at least felt something… Or anything at all… Even lingering old feelings that Taiga could cling to as an attempt to dampen the ache that wouldn't settle, but there was nothing.

Just the thoughts of someone else.

It was like a cruel comedy of errors that Taiga would fall out of love with someone he had thought had loved him to only have his heart broken by someone who made him believe it was all real.

Perhaps this was Taiga's curse for mocking and slandering love for so long, and whether it was or wasn't, Taiga wasn't eager to find out what his next punishment would be. The last two were painful enough.

Taiga rose to his feet.

Love just didn't come in a shape that was meant for him.

 

 

When Juri finally woke, he was covered by Taiga's discarded blanket as he was pulled from his sleep by the deep scent of fresh coffee and the variety of missed calls vibrating against his chest.

The first thing he saw when he sat up with his phone still buzzing in his breast pocket, was Taiga standing in the kitchen, hair wet with a towel around his neck and in a set of clothes that were different from when he had opened the door.

Juri's phone continued to rattle as he watched what almost looked like a completely different person pouring water in a glass coffee press.

When Taiga caught his gaze, Juri nearly flinched as the other raised his mug to his lips and spoke into it.

"... Are you going to get that?"

Juri blinked before finally slapping his hand over his phone against his chest.

"Oh. Uh- yes. Sorry," he said, ruffling his sleep tousled hair as he got to his feet and fished it out from his pocket. "Can I borrow your room to take this?"

"Sure. As long as you don't mind the mess."

"I'll take it."

"Hey, Juri?"

"Hmm?"

Juri looked up from the screen as his hand set on the handle to Taiga's room.

It didn't take words for Juri to know that the smile Taiga wore wasn't from joy.

"... I don't think I can write anymore."

Taiga wasn't sure how Juri would respond as the persistent buzzing of his phone filled the silent air between them. For a moment, he thought Juri's quiet stare was of defeat or disappointment.

But the moment Juri smiled back with his phone against his ear as he unlatched the door, Taiga knew he should have known better to have ever thought that Juri would have been anything short of understanding.

"Alright… We'll figure it out…"

"I promise."

 

 

As the days of the last month of his deadline passed by, Taiga could only stare at the white blank page.

He and Juri had given up on the idea of a full and complete manuscript heaping with beautiful imagery and a wonderful storyline for the chopped up scraps of what Taiga could manage to write in hopes that at least someone could see it's potential, even if Taiga wasn't sure himself of what it's potential was.

Juri was doing his best to make something out of nothing, but Taiga could only think of his resignation.

He had checked his bank account to see how long his royalties could hold him up for until he could eventually bring himself to write something or find another publisher that would give him enough pity. He thanked his past self for writing decent enough books in the past because at the moment, there was no chance that the chief editor would be taking what they had. Juri tried to stay positive and encourage him that there was still something that could be done, but the overflowing ashtray betrayed his words.

There was no doubt that Juri was just as stressed as he was because even Juri knew there was a slim to nothing chance of their botched up sorry excuse for a story making it through.

… Well, whatever.

What was another 10 pounds on top of the walls that already were crashing down on him?

Taiga poured himself a drink as he walked over to his neglected calendar.

The red cross marks had stopped after Taiga had torn the page off from the previous month, not wanting a reminder of how many days had passed since his fight with Hokuto, but after staring at the clean empty page, he figured he might as well fill it in.

He popped the cap off the felt pen and dragged a dark thick winding line down all the days to the last week where at the end, the last day was marked with a circle he had drawn 8 months ago.

In hindsight, drawing that circle was pointless.

From the very beginning, Taiga never really had any confidence that he'd make it. The last couple months had only set it in stone.

He looked up to read the ever steady ticking clock.

8:07 pm.

Juri was going to show the slapped together manuscript to some of his coworkers to get an idea of what others would think. There wouldn't be much time, but maybe they could use their feedback to fix it up before the end of the week.

Juri had said they would be meeting at 7. It was only about time he–

Taiga's phone pinged as if Juri had read his mind.

He slipped his phone from his pocket and tapped it to waken the screen.

One new message.

Juri:
No good.

Ah.

Taiga stared at his phone until the screen went dark, taking the message away with it.

Well…

It wasn't like Taiga wasn't expecting something like this, but he would have been lying if he said he hadn't been a little hopeful that his successful record would at least grant him a little grace…

Taiga held up his glass of highball to no one, to the absence of a presence across the table from what had become what he called his seat .

"... Cheers...To unemployment."

He kicked the glass back, draining his drink until all that was left was the ice that clattered at the bottom of his glass.

Thank God he had made the choice to pick up a 6-pack at the convenience store.

He would absolutely be drinking all 6 tonight.

The ring of his doorbell overlapped with the snap of the opening of his second can.

It has to be Juri.

No one came over this late unannounced.

Not anymore anyways.

Taiga took another big gulp before setting the can down to answer the door.

Misery loved company, at least.

"Juri, do-"





"You."





That certainly wasn't Juri's voice.

And the person at the door certainly wasn't Juri's height.

But before any of it could begin to register, a seathing sting exploded across his face.

All Taiga could do was hold his burning cheek while hands shoved him back into his own home as the voice spat again with a familiar poison.

"You."

"You!!"

"This is your fault!!!"

The woman introduced to Juri as Takeuchi Hinako slammed his door shut before his shirt was clutched in her manicured nails as she screamed at his face.

"You did this!!!!"

"You made Hokuto leave me!!!!!"

"You fucking bitch!!!!"

Taiga clenched his eyes shut when her hand reeled back, but it didn't save him from the burn that bloomed over his skin when she struck him again. He tried to pull her off of him by her shoulders, but Hinako was persistent, stretching his clothes and pulling at him relentlessly.

"This is all your fault!!! You made him leave me!!!!!! You ruined me!!!!! You ruined my fucking life–!! How dare you!!?!!"

"Wait-!"

"You're just a slut !!! How much did you open your legs for him to make him leave me, huh?!?!!!?"

"I-!"

"You ruined everything!!!"

Before Hinako could strike him again, Taiga caught and gripped her wrist which only managed to infuriate her more. She gritted her teeth, yanking her hand back as she yelled at him to let go, lurching Taiga's grip on her wrist back and pulling him into her.

Taiga's feet stumbled as he tried to catch himself, but he could do nothing when Hinako shoved at his chest, toppling him backwards and allowing her to sit on and pin him down by his chest after he hit the floor.

Her nails raked red marks across his cheek when she swung her hand at him again.

"You took him from me!!!" Hinako screamed, her voice tearing through her throat.

"You stole him!!!"

With the next hit, Taiga's glasses went skating across the floor.

"Why couldn't you just let me be happy!?!!?!"

Taiga tried to hold up his arms over his face to protect himself, but they only took the brunt of her abuse as she pulled and tugged at them, trying to reach him again by digging her nails into his skin.

He didn't know what to do.

There was no way of reaching her.

No matter what Taiga said, he didn't think she would listen.

The only thing he could do was lay there and be her punching bag as she blamed him for things he didn't understand, saying Taiga had "taken", "stolen" and even "seduced."

If she spoke of Hokuto, it made no sense.

Hokuto was far from his.

But she said his name.

It didn't make sense.

"You!!" She gasped for breath as she pulled Taiga's arm back enough to sink her fingers into his hair to yank at it.

"You ruined my whole life!!!"

"You took everything from me!!!!"

"All-!! All I ever wanted was him!!!"

Taiga winced, grabbing at her wrist to keep her from tugging any harder.

He said all he knew he could say, whether she would listen or not.

"I'm sorry!!"

"I'm sorry!!!! I'm sorry–!!!!! Please–!!!"

"Sorry isn't good enough!!!!"

A throb of pain washed through the back of his head when she lifted and shoved it back into the floor, cracking his skull against the hardwood.

"If you're sorry then give him back!!!"

"I- I can't-!!"

"Give him back!!!"

"I don't–!"

"Please!!!"

Taiga flinched, tightening his arm over his already battered face, defending himself from what her rath would inflict against him next as Hinako's voice started to form cracks.

But instead of hateful words and nails scratching into his arms, there was only the sound of hiccups and the feeling of droplets falling and rolling down his wrist.

When Taiga cracked open his eyes, he saw Hinako leaned over him, fists full of his shirt and eyes full of tears falling from her long lashes with her voice quivering as she begged again.

"Please–…. Give him back…"

"I-I'll do anything–…."

"I love him…."

"You have no idea how much I love him–… Please– …"

Her tears dropped onto Taiga's cheeks, rolling and trailing down his reddened skin as he listened quietly as she cried and begged, over and over.

It stung Taiga's heart to watch her cry.

It hurt and it hurt for her only because he knew exactly what she felt. To love someone so desperately to be brought to tears.

He stayed silent as her hands released from his shirt to clutch in front of her face, her breath growing ragged and her tears refusing to stop.

"H–he gave me everything–. I j-just wanted– wanted t-to love someone one-" Hinako sobbed, her speech broken by the shaking in her chest. "All… A-all my life i-it was- just deal- I was just a t-token but h-he-... He–!"

"I'm sorry…"

Taiga's voice was soft and low as she cried, her tears wetting his skin and his clothes as they fell one after another.

He said it again.

"I'm sorry…"

"... I'm so sorry…"

Taiga wasn't sure what to do.

Hinako had struck and beat him, but he couldn't help but feel her agony.

Even if it was a different monster, the squeeze in their chests and the ache in their hearts were the same.

Taiga may have suffered.

But what reason was there to add one more miserable person to this shit place called Earth?

Taiga reached out.

His hand and his heart.

If Hinako hit away his hand, he wouldn't have been surprised, but it was worth trying as his hand slowly went to set on her shoulder. He flinched back when she hiccuped, but continued, placing his hand on her arm, trying to give a comforting squeeze.

"... T-Takeuchi… was it?...."

She didn't respond, but she didn't deny it either as she continued to sob in her hands.

"... Before I say anything else… I want you to know that there is nothing between me and Matsumura. I swear over my own grave."

At least not anymore. If there ever was.

"So please…"

"... Can we just… talk?..."

At first it seemed like a miracle that Taiga had gotten Hinako to agree, but Hinako wasn't a bad person.

She was just broken.

The world had broken her with its crushing fist until all she had left was to comply with Hokuto as her only escape.

Taiga put a blanket over her shoulders after asking to take her uncomfortable but expensive coat.

"... Would you like water?... Or maybe coffee?"

Her small nod didn't tell him much, but Taiga went to prepare both.

The kettle clattered lightly on the stovetop, the fire coming to life below it. As the water boiled for the coffee press, Taiga snuck glances over to her in the living area, seeing how all she did was soak her last few tears into her hand cloth with an empty gaze in her eyes.

Taiga couldn't help but think of himself in Kochi's car on the way home.

As complicated as hearts were, the pain they felt was surprisingly simple.

The first thing she said to him after the crying stopped was "Your coffee tastes like his…"

Taiga peeked over his mug at her before looking down into the deep colored brew.

It tasted like his because it was his…

He was the one who taught him, after all.

"... Does it bother you?..."

She shook her head.

"Honestly?… A little… but you swore, right?...... That there's nothing."

Taiga swallowed as he set down his mug on the coffee table.

"Yes… I promise."

"Then I'll enjoy it…" She brought the cup back to her lips.

"... It might be the last I'll ever have anyways…"

Taiga looked back down at the piece of Hokuto he wasn't aware he had, the foam from the milk swirling in the center.

"... Do you mind telling me how you met him?..."

Hinako told him everything.

The beginning, the middle, chapter 5, chapter 8. Everything.

Hokuto was her everything, but somewhere along their story, something went wrong.

Her family, her arranged marriage, how every part of her being was decided for her, it all broke her as Hokuto was the only person who saw her for who she was, and not the person her family made her to be. Her time with him was the best she ever had, but she couldn't stop the arrangement.

Hinako knew she couldn't have Hokuto as she wanted, so she didn't care how she kept him, as long as she had him at all, she didn't care.

It was only when Taiga entered the picture that everything started to crumble apart, and from how Hinako told her story, Taiga couldn't even bring himself to blame her for how she felt towards him.

If someone had taken the only person he had ever chosen for himself, he would have been angry at himself too.

"I did everything to keep women away," Hinako explained with a soft hiccup in her voice. "I spread rumors and said terrible things to anyone who got too close."

"It was only because you were a boy that I didn't notice."

"It was only until Hokuto didn't let me inside that I realized… He had always let me in… Even when girls had slept over, he would kick them so I could come in."

"But for you–... He said no."

Somehow Taiga felt ashamed. He knew there was no reason he should be, but it didn't change the guilt that sank in his stomach.

"... How did you know it was me?..."

Hinako squeezed her eyes shut, another tear escaping from her lashes. "Because I waited!... I saw you leave that morning! You were wearing that suit-..."

Taiga had no idea that Hinako had come over that day. There was no way he could have. His mind was wrecked and distraught with learning who he had thought to be his first love had gotten engaged.

He hadn't known that as he laid asleep in Hokuto's bed, when Hinako arrived at his door asking to be let inside, Hokuto had turned her away.

For him, Hokuto told Hinako no, the person Hokuto said he could never tell no, before returning to lay beside him and fall asleep next to him in the same bed.

Before he held him as he cried.

Before they kissed for the first time.

Taiga felt as if he had been caught doing the walk of shame.

"... I-... I'm sorry…"

"It's too late now…" Hinako murmured into her blanket. "I tried so hard to think it was nothing… but I couldn't take it. I used up all his free time on me because I couldn't fall asleep thinking that he was with you… I made him use all his time on me but–..."

Her tears came flooding back.

"I-... I thought I could leave him for just one day… but I couldn't stop the horrible feeling in my chest so I called him and asked him to come back to me."

"He said yes–! He t-told me over the phone that he would but he n-never–" The shake in her voice worsened.

"I knew something had to be wrong– I thought he would never leave me but then he-! He–!!"

As Hinako began to sob again, Taiga went to refill her glass of water before coming back to rub her back and offer her another tissue as his mind began to stir.

… There was so much he didn't know…

After that last night, Taiga had convinced himself that Hokuto had returned to her, disappointed by how his plan didn't work out and the bet was ruined, not to break up with Hinako and tell her that it was all over.

Yet, life was full of surprises, even if he didn't really understand what they meant.

Hokuto had left her.

Taiga had thought everything he did was for her.

… So what did it all mean?...

It couldn't have meant that Hokuto wasn't lying, right?...

As much as he wanted to forget, Taiga could still see the glimpse of pain that was deep in Hokuto's eyes as he screamed at him, telling him that he would never understand him. The desperation. The ache.

Taiga's eyes fluttered for a moment from the image that played from his memory.

… It wasn't that Hokuto really, truly –...







… It didn't really matter.

Regardless of whoever actually occupied Hokuto's mind… He was all Hinako had.

Hinako needed him. Even with him, she was already falling apart at the seams. She needed Hokuto to put her back together.

And Hokuto loved, if not, had at least loved her once before.

Taiga was just some pitiful idiot who didn't understand romance.

He would live, whether or not Hokuto was there to hold him at night.

Taiga exhaled softly as he drew his hand away.

"... Have you told him? That you really love him?"

"Of course, I have!" She cried, defeated as she curled into the blanket. "I told him over and over again. I told him thousands of times…"

"... Have you… um…" Taiga held his mug that now held tea, not wanting to stay up all night from the caffeine. "Showed him?... That you love him?..."

Hinako raised her eyes from her lap to see Taiga staring into his drink.

"Of course, I did..."

"I bought him everything… I paid for everything… Is that not enough?..."

Taiga shook his head, tracing his thumb along the ceramic handle of his cup.

"No, sorry. That's not what I meant… There's no doubt you gave him plenty, I just–..."

"... What I mean was… Did you think about how Matsumura wants to be loved?"

Hinako blinked, her perfectly shaped brows furrowing as she clutched her cup.

"... What do you mean?....."

Taiga wasn't completely sure.

He just knew the moments that made him think Hokuto had cared. He hadn't fallen in love enough times to know any other way.

Taiga only knew how Hokuto made him feel.

"I don't mean to say I know any better… You know him way better than I do, but umm…"

"Have you ever just… let him spoil you?..."

The food. The service. The work. The time. The care.

Hokuto had given so much.

He cooked with him, taught him, ate with him as he smiled every time Taiga said it was delicious.

He stayed up, working. Writing. Taking notes when Taiga never asked. Even after Taiga told him to stop, he sat by him after working tirelessly at his own job to help any way he could.

Hokuto held him when he cried.

He arrived in a flash after a text.

He kissed him.

He embraced him.

His actions spoke more than words.

Hokuto had told him he loved him over and over without saying a word.

Maybe.

Perhaps…

… But this wasn't about him.

It should have never been about him.

"Maybe you gave so much you never let him share the burden…"

"He likes to-... I-I think-..." Taiga stammered, not wanting to claim any knowledge over someone who has known him for years. "He likes to have you depend on him…"

"You like to give… but let him give something back. A relationship shouldn't be one-sided, right?..."

Hinako pulled her knees to her chest. "But I can't give him everything… I'm married… Don't I have to make up for that?"

"I don't think so…" Taiga said quietly. "Just letting him know you love him and being there should be enough."

If Hokuto loved her deeply enough to stay with her for 5 years without asking for anything else, it should certainly be enough.

Just having Hokuto there had been enough for him.

Hinako sniffled. "You really think so?..."

"... I don't know… but I think so…" Taiga said, handing her another tissue.

"... Isn't that enough to try?"

They talked for a while longer.

Hinako talked about her worries and insecurities as Taiga comforted her the best he could. They talked or simply stayed quiet as Hinako cried until she couldn't bring herself to cry anymore.

The day had turned late before they knew it, and as Hinako traded the blanket for her coat, Taiga pulled a few books from his shelf to hand to her by the door.

"Here. If you just want an escape."

Her eyes traveled over the cover as she took them from his hands.

"... What are these?..."

"Just some modern fantasy… They're good to escape with so… if things ever get hard, maybe try to read these."

The front was covered in washes of colors depicting a complicated but simple world that was much like their own, but was different.

She held them to her chest.

"How much are these worth?... Let me pay you –" she said as she began to look through her purse.

Taiga waved his hands as she looked back up at him. "No, it's okay. I get a lot of them for free anyways. Just take them."

"... But promise me one thing in exchange."

"... Sure."

"Talk to him."

Her lips pressed together.

"But… what if-"

"Just try…"

Taiga placed his hand over hers on the books. "He loves you… If anything… he'll listen… and listen to him too."

"Thank you… I'll try," Hinako barely nodded.

"I'm… I'm sorry I hit you…"

Taiga had honestly forgotten about the burning lines on his skin, but his cheek would recover.

Broken hearts were much harder to mend.

"It's alright. I'll be fine."

He opened the door for her as a thought came to his mind. "Um… Do you mind me asking something?"

"Hmm?" Hinako turned back to him after stepping out.

"... How did you know where I live?..."

Hinako almost looked embarrassed or even a little ashamed as her eyes broke away from his with a timid smile.

"... Let's just say my husband knows people. And I knew your name and your company…"

"You can learn anything by saying the right thing and talking to the right people…"

Ah.

"I see…"

Scary.

Hokuto was with someone much scarier that Taiga could ever imagine handling.

"Have a good night, Kyomoto..."

"... You too, Takeuchi…"

Taiga hoped to never see her again after closing the door. Not that he disliked her, just that with this, he wanted it to all be over.

Hinako would go back to Hokuto to make things work and Hokuto would take her back. They would have their happily ever after now that the plot point of their story named "Kyomoto Taiga" was now done.

So where did that leave him?... The Kyomoto Taiga that was still in love with Matsumura Hokuto?...

Who cares.

Taiga just knew that all he wanted to do right now was write.

A language beyond language.

A feeling beyond speech.

An affection without words.

 

 

"... Should I ask what happened?"

Taiga just shoved his laptop into Juri's hands, making no further mention of the bandage over his cheek the other stared at.

"No. Just read."

"Kyomo, as much as I love your determination, there's only 2 days left. I really don't think-"

Taiga pushed down at Juri's shoulders, forcing him onto his couch.

"Sure, whatever. I don't care. Just read it."

Juri sighed, placing a fresh cigarette between his lips as he scrolled past the pages.

He had thought there would only be one or two of them, but as the words and pages just kept going and going, his cigarette nearly fell from his mouth as it widened.

"Christ–! Just how much did you write? Were you hiding all of this from me??"

Taiga rolled his sore neck and wrist as he sat. "No, I only started writing it a couple days ago."

Juri swiped his fingers on the touchpad, the pages flying past again to return to the top. "A couple-... What?! A couple days ago?!"

"What the hell happened?? Did you lose your mind???"

"Kind of– Juri, just read it already."

Juri sighed as he sat back, looking over the first sentence.

"Alright, fine," he said as he pulled his glasses from his briefcase. "Can you make me a drink then?"

Taiga got back onto his feet to immediately go to the kitchen.

Whatever it took for Juri to just shut up and read.

"What do you want? Coffee? Tea? Alcohol?"

"Whatever you think suits whatever this is best."

"Then tea."

After 5 cups of tea, a few bathroom breaks and a snack, Juri was reaching the end of the text with his fingers covering his mouth that had been hanging open, enthralled as he read.

Taiga was preparing dinner when he nearly choked from the whack that landed on his back, not expecting Juri to shove the laptop into the couch and run into the kitchen just to hit him with childlike excitement.

"Kyomo!!!" He shouted as he looped his arms around Taiga's shoulders, shaking him.

"God damnit!! Kyomo!!" He shouted with his huge wide grin as Taiga quickly placed down his knife safely.

"It's good!!!"

"It's really fucking good!!! What the hell happened to you!?!"

"It's a long— story-" Taiga struggled to respond as Juri continued to squeeze and rattle him like a large toy.

"Well, fuck it!! It doesn't matter!! It's good, Kyomo!! It's really really good!!"

Taiga pushed back up his glasses that had been jostled down his nose.

"But it's not long enough–"

It was only enough to cover the first and a half of the second chapter.

It was nowhere near the full manuscript that was requested in two days.

"You're right!!" Juri's volume was the same, but the enthusiasm was dampened by the truth. "... It's not!... But it's better than before."

"With this, it's worth a shot. If it takes all night for me to edit, then I'll do it. This is worth it."

Taiga gripped Juri's arms that had ceased their shaking.

"... So you are having dinner here?"

Juri laughed, letting go to squeeze the top of Taiga's shoulders. "If you'll have me. And for tonight."

"... And probably tomorrow. And the next morning..."

"Okay, Juri, I get the point."

Juri grinned as Taiga pushed him back.

Taiga had forgotten how nice it felt to smile as he returned one to his friend.

"So!" Juri said with a deep breath to prepare himself for the hours ahead. "We eat and then try to make magic happen?"

"Sure," Taiga laughed.

"Whatever that magic is."

Magic is what Juri called it.

But it was more like they needed a miracle.

For the next two days, all that they did was work.

Taiga wrote. Juri read and made comments.

Taiga wrote again. Juri read again.

Rinse and repeat until the morning of their deadline where Taiga quickly made final edits and touch ups while he listened to Juri beg for an unscheduled meeting, bowing to nothing but the wall in front of him.

After Juri told him they got a yes, everything was a blur.

Juri shoving him in the shower.

Getting dressed.

Getting in the car.

Going into the office.

Sitting in front of the chief editor holding what looked more like a college pamphlet than a manuscript.

Taiga stared down at the white table as Juri did his best to sell it, emphasizing its creativity and the results of their determined effort.

Juri was good with his words, explaining with dramatized detail just how hard Taiga worked and how wonderful and successful his previous book had been, but the chief editor only held a frown as he thumbed through the pages.

"Please, Matsumoto…" Juri pleaded again with his head bowed.

"We know it isn't much, but please understand that Kyomoto has the potential… It's not long, but it has life. I have read many lengths of manuscripts in my career and just that alone has so much more than many of the hundreds of pages we get from prospective writers."

"So please, if you would even just take another day to consider…"

The chief sighed, setting down the incomplete story down on the table. "... It's good… I won't lie about that… but it's a hard sell to the publishers to ask for more time again… Just one chapter doesn't give promise."

Juri's shoulders deflated, but was still nowhere near ready to give in. "I understand, but I swear. I'll do whatever it takes to make sure that it comes out great. We'll even work on a tightened deadline. I promise to take full responsibility."

If Juri had bowed any deeper, his forehead would have collided with the top of the table.

Taiga only raised his head when the chief said his name.

"Kyomoto."

"Yes."

"I just have one question."

"... Yes."

Juri glanced back and forth between the two of them as neither of their gazes relented to the thickening pressure.

"Is this a romance?"

Taiga wanted to laugh.

It was incredible how circular life was…

Juri looked back to Taiga as the silence grew longer, growing anxious by the absence of his response as he began to beg in his head for Taiga to give a reply that didn't backtrack all his efforts.

Taiga did finally answer, but what came from his mouth made Juri cringe.

"... Why don't you let me write the rest so you can find out?"

It came out in a huff and was blazé as he said it, but Taiga didn't know how to say it any other way as he ignored the sharp bump Juri gave his foot with his own from under the table.

Taiga just didn't like all the groveling.

If the company wanted to take his story, then they would take it, if they didn't then they wouldn't.

That was life and that's how life went.

All the pleading and pleasing could sway a person if they were soft, but more often than not, a person will have already made up their mind. The formalities and pleasantries were all just fillers for what was already decided.

In Juri's opinion, it was his typical businessman persuasion that got the chief to accept their deal and that's what he insisted the whole way home, but Taiga couldn't help but believe it was because the chief editor was impressed that he had enough balls to stand up to the reputation of Matsumoto Jun.

In the end, it didn't matter who was right or wrong and they could have argued about it all night. All it truly meant was now there were many more tireless nights ahead of them.

Now, they had to make the product.

 

 

3 years ago, Taiga didn't care about clothes.

3 years later, he still really didn't care.

Also, since when did his company care so much about PR?...

For his last several books, he hardly did anything besides one or two short inserts for a publication announcement or even just a signature for a bookstore display. It was the responsibility of the sellers and the stores to create enough promotion for their units to sell.

So why was it that he now had to stand around while Juri found an outfit that "most suited his image"?

What image???

He didn't have an image.

All he did was write books for people to read and maybe even enjoy their time reading it. Why did he have to have an image?

Usually after a book went on sale, Taiga just slept and ordered expensive take out for himself. Maybe he would even enjoy the wine he got gifted as a congratulations.

So why did he have to do interviews and appearances now??

The "grand return" of his books, he guessed, from how many times Juri had mentioned it.

Juri stepped back to look at his work, grinning pridefully about his own personal choices even if the suit was slightly soured by Taiga's frown.

"Perfect."

"Is it? You said that 8 ties ago."

"No, I'm settled with this one. This one is perfect," he smiled as he waved down a clerk to make last adjustments before they checked out.

"So we can go home after this, right?"

"Nope."

Taiga wanted to groan like a spoiled child, but he kept it in his chest as the tailor cuffed and marked where to adjust the length of his pants.

"... What else, Juri?"

"This."

His eyes nearly crossed when Juri brushed at his bangs where the dark color of his hair had long replaced the bright blonde that had been cut and left on a salon floor before pulling off Taiga's glasses from his nose.

"And this."

3 years of work and it all came down to this… Getting his hair bleached again and learning how to place contact lenses in his eyes.

The last years had been endless amounts of work as it always was, but Taiga's bold shot in the dark wouldn't go unpunished.

The company made sure that they would be made to work on a short schedule.

Taiga didn't remember how many times he apologized to both Juri and his girlfriend about how the work would postpone their wedding and how many nights Juri was made to sleep on his couch. His guilt was only made worse when Juri's child was born to the point where Taiga asked again and again to help pay for her childcare, but Juri always refused. He only ever asked for Taiga to let him bring his baby over during their work so his girlfriend could have a break.

Aside from the crying, it never became a problem, even if some of his books had become play toys. It was manageable, but Taiga was still endlessly grateful when Juri's girlfriend had taken herself and their child to spend time with her parents back in Osaka.

Taiga had asked Juri if he should be going with them, but he told him no, saying that once he was done babysitting him, he would have all the time in the world to spend with his new born.

… Though, somehow, even after the book was done, Juri managed to waste his time making sure Taiga looked nothing like himself for his interviews.

It wasn't at all part of Juri's job description. He just wanted to.

Taiga barely recognized himself in the mirror after Juri stilled a smooth sweep in his hair for his interview the next day.

The blonde he had seen before, but the contacts and the fitted suit really made it something else. He looked good… probably?... But all Taiga wanted was just to return to his large t-shirt and shorts in the comfort of his own home.

He had completed his magazine interview weeks ago and all that was left was the TV appearance and a book signing.

Comparatively, the magazine interview was painless, quick and concise. It was simple and he also didn't have to wear a tie.

There wasn't much he could have said. It wasn't like there was exactly a plethora of creative ways to describe the growing relationship between a blind man and his mute caretaker who cooked for him and how they learned to share their feelings and thoughts without relying on words.

The questions were straightforward, as expected for a literary publication. The readers weren't really there for all the fluff.

Just what, when, where and why.

Taiga answered them as honestly and as directly as the questions themselves. There was no gain in lying in the same fashion that there was no loss in telling the truth, so he answered with the whole truth… Minus the personal details.

What was the book? A book about growth.

When did you think of the book? Years ago.

Where do you imagine this book? Salut.

Why did you write it? He had to and it was all he had on his mind.

In hindsight, maybe he shouldn't have mentioned Salut by name, but he said it before Juri could stop him.

"You know, you've just about exiled yourself from ever going back there. People are going to look for you," is what Juri told him afterwards in their elevator ride down.

Taiga just responded with a sigh as he leaned against the wall, knocking his head back onto the cold metal surface.

"It's fine…"

"I wasn't planning on going back any time soon anyways."

The magazine had been fine with just him, Juri and the man with thick glasses across from him in a small room, but in the space rushed with people and large TV cameras, Taiga was far more overwhelmed.

The constant stage directions Juri rambled to him didn't make his nerves any better either.

"Smile." Juri whispered to him quickly as a stage hand waved them over.

"Don't forget to smile."

"Laugh if you're nervous."

"Be friendly."

"Don't act like you don't want to be here."

The last one was the hardest out of all of them because he didn't want to be there and it very obviously showed on his face, but Taiga did the best he could to be charming as he took a deep breath.

Hokuto did it for years.

How bad could 15 minutes really be?

For 15 minutes, Taiga acted like Hokuto when his character was on, doing the best he could to follow Juri's directions as he smiled and laughed for the pre-filmed show.

He should have guessed that the TV interview would be different. Unlike the literary interview a week ago, the questions were less about the book and were more about him.

The magazine was selling his book.

This was selling the author.

Even so, Taiga answered honestly because honesty was the easiest to say as he told the woman across from him why the book was the way he had written it and what had inspired him.

Who inspired him.

Taiga didn't lie about what he said about Hokuto either.

He really didn't think Hokuto would ever want to speak to him again.

Taiga had said horrible things and called petty names before walking away because he couldn't tell him that he was wrong.

Hokuto was right. Taiga had used him. He was just too busy wallowing in his own self-pity to see it. He had asked Hokuto for selfish things, pulling him and dragging him along by his own self-will because Hokuto let him and Taiga was shallow enough to believe it wouldn't hurt him.

Taiga knew better now.

Hokuto had given him so much and Taiga had the audacity to ever call him selfish.

Taiga denied all of it when Hokuto truly did-...




He had–…

………




Well, it was too far too late to apologize now.

Forgive and forget, though he couldn't do the former.

If everything had gone as Taiga had thought, Hinako was surely at his side, happy and peaceful in their repaired love.

Not even for a second had Taiga ever imagined that he would see Hokuto waiting in the line of his signing, clutching his book in his hands.

Taiga nearly let the book he was handed slip from his fingers as he dragged his eyes away from Hokuto's.

It had been so long since he had seen that gaze.

He had seen it so many times before, when they cooked, when they shopped, when they kissed, when Taiga had said his last words before swearing to never see him again.

Yet, it still managed to shake him as much as the day he could see the red lipstick stains smudged across his lips.

Taiga tried to stay focused on the person in front of him, to keep a smile and write his name cleanly into the paper of the book, but he couldn't help his eyes from being pulled back to him.

It was only once Hokuto approached the table when Taiga was able to keep his gaze down, watching the wrist that was no longer encircled by a gold chain.

It almost felt like something was missing from it when it reached out with his unchristened book in its hands.

As Taiga took the book and creased the cover as he opened it, he didn't understand.

Even now, he still didn't understand.

So he asked.

Why was he here?

What was he here for?

What did his invite mean?...

"... I was hoping you would be my boyfriend after."

Taiga didn't understand as the name he had removed from his vocabulary nearly slipped from his lips, watching wordlessly as Hokuto told him he would wait for him.

He said he would wait.

The words replayed in Taiga's mind during and after the signing was over. Even as Juri led him to his car to the restaurant he had booked, the words stayed in Taiga's ears.

… There was just simply no way he would… right?...

Taiga couldn't enjoy the drinks that were given to him at his celebration party as all he could do was watch the clock as time passed.

6:42 pm.

Kochi arrived with a smile and a congratulations, giving Taiga his gift of a new journal and a pen that wrote beautifully. Taiga thanked him as Kochi gave his side a hug, saying "I knew you could do it."

7:54 pm.

Juri slung his arm over his shoulder, shoving a beer into his hand that Taiga would nurse slowly, only so that the glass wouldn't be filled again.

9:19 pm.

The party was slowing down, some had left, but others were still ready to move to the next bar. Juri was far gone, but still energetic as ever.

10:48 pm.

Kochi had only stayed so long because Juri wouldn't let him leave. Taiga finally convinced Juri to use the bathroom so that Kochi could escape.

11:37 pm.

Taiga told everyone he would walk home.

Thankfully, everyone was either too drunk or too tired to question it.

It was pouring.

He bowed to the restaurant owner who offered him an umbrella left behind by a previous customer, thanking him and wishing him a goodnight.

And as soon as the door closed, Taiga's dress shoes splashed lightly into the shallow puddles of the sidewalk as his legs began to move on their own with the question that had been reeling in his mind all night repeating again.

He couldn't be.

He couldn't.

Not with the rain.

It was impossible.

But his feet still moved and his legs still walked.

It would take while, but Taiga was already in the city and he knew the way.

Taiga truly didn't think that Hokuto would wait for so long.

He didn't deserve to be waited for.

… But Hokuto told him he would wait.

Taiga had doubted his words before and he was wrong back then… So what reason did he have to believe that he couldn't be wrong again?...

His feet quickened.

The words replayed again in his mind, but maybe only to save himself from ache if they were true.

He couldn't be waiting.

If he wasn't there, then it was over. Taiga would be right.

There was just simply no way that Hokuto would have waited for him this whole time.

And if he was there?...





Then…






Taiga's feet stopped as he reached the corner, his breath coming out in huffs in the humid air.

A lump formed in his throat as he looked at the front of Salut.

And the figure curled up beside it.





Waiting.






Still.






Taiga didn't understand.

He didn't understand romance.

None of it made any sense.

Why would anyone sit in the rain and wait for someone to show up after not speaking to each other for 3 years?...

It was ridiculous.

… But then why would someone come to check to see if they were still there even after the time had passed midnight in the middle of the pouring rain?...

Taiga's hand tightened around the smooth handle of the umbrella.

Romance.

Care.

Affection.

Love.

He held the umbrella out, sheltering Hokuto from the rain as he gazed up at him with glazed eyes.





… It couldn't hurt to find out...












 

 

"... Didn't you say you would make me dinner?..."
