Chapter Notes

See the end of the chapter for notes

"... Kyomoto?..."

"... Matsumura, I–"

Hokuto still couldn't believe it.

It still didn't feel real.

Before Taiga could say anything, Hokuto pulled him into his arms.

Hokuto's body was cold, his wet clothes seeping into Taiga's tailored suit as the umbrella was knocked out from Taiga's hand, submitting them both back under the rain.

Taiga was speechless as Hokuto's hold tightened.

He just let Hokuto cling to him, his arms around his shoulders and his fingers clutched into his suit as he buried his face into the curve of his neck.

Hokuto might have been cold, but his breath was warm against Taiga's skin as the rain slowly drenched him.

"... You came…"

"... You actually came…."

Maybe Taiga could have said something snarky or sharp to lighten the mood that was slowly becoming overbearing, but when Taiga tried to speak, his words got stuck in his throat.

All he could do was nod and hold Hokuto back.

"... You're real, right?..." Hokuto spoke into Taiga collar, his voice shaking. "I'm not just dreaming?..."

Taiga shook his head, finally managing to make his speech croak from his throat. 

"I'm here… I'm real…"

"... You waited…"

Hokuto's arms squeezed around him.

"I told you I would wait… I would have waited for you forever…"

Taiga's chest gave a weak laugh as his hands gripped what he could of the back of Hokuto's soaked shirt. "You're an idiot… You would have died."

"That's fine…" Hokuto muttered into Taiga's collar.

"... As long as it meant seeing you."

Taiga hit his fist into Hokuto's back.

He wished he could have sounded more cool, but the crack in his voice ruined everything.

"Just take me inside already…"

"Before you freeze to death."

Hokuto only let go once Taiga pushed him off of him.

As they went towards Hokuto's door, Hokuto made Taiga walk before him, afraid that if he were to leave his sight, Taiga would disappear. Even as he undid the lock to his flat, he had Taiga stand between him and the door as he leaned in, encircling himself around him with his chest pressed against his back while he turned the key.

Once the door swung open and they both stumbled in, Hokuto immediately looped Taiga back into his hold.

As it closed, the steady sigh of the falling showers outside were muted as neither of them spoke, leaving only the sound of the scattered pattering of the rain dripping from their clothes onto the hardwood floor and the quiet breaths that escaped their lips.

In the silence, Taiga could hear and feel Hokuto's heart pounding against his back as he placed his hands over the ones clasped tightly around his waist, gazing into the dimly lit room through his water-stained glasses. 

There was no doubt that his was pounding too. 

The rain in their hair blended together as Hokuto nudged his head against Taiga's from over his shoulder with Taiga leaning his temple onto his. Droplets rolled and fell from their chins in the quiet while Taiga smoothly threaded his fingers between Hokuto's over the back of his hands. 




… Did they really need to say it?...




Both of them knew.

Both of them had known for forever.

They didn't have to.

This was enough.

Taiga buried his nose into Hokuto's damp hair before whispering softly into his hairline, gently pulling his hands loose from around his waist.

"... You should change your clothes…"

Hokuto stayed silent as Taiga turned to him, only watching how Taiga's eyes lowered to his chest.

"... I should too."

… It still felt like a dream.

Even after Taiga told him in his own voice it was real and after he felt warm in his arms, Hokuto still couldn't bring himself to believe this was all more than a vivid dream. 

Taiga was here.

With him.

It was unbelievable.

… But even if it was all just a dream, Hokuto would take and value every second of it.

All of it could just be delusions as his body gave into the heavy rain outside the front of Salut, but he didn't really care.

Just having Taiga in his dreams was more than Hokuto could have ever wished for.

He pressed his jaw against Taiga's crown as Taiga's hands smoothed down his chest, his fingers undoing each button on his shirt one by one, loosening the damp fabric that stuck to Hokuto's skin. After the sleeves fell free from his arms, Hokuto cupped the sides of Taiga's neck, not wasting a second on his shirt that dropped heavily to the floor.

The only thing that mattered to him was the feel of Taiga's skin.

For years he had yearned for it after having a taste of it, holding Taiga in his sleep and exchanging meaningless kisses, but now he couldn't resist as it was a completely different heat. 

Because now, Taiga looked at him. 

Taiga didn't accept his touch because he mourned over Juri or just because he wanted to know what it felt like.

Taiga came for him. 

And Hokuto clung to that with his whole life.

Hokuto threaded his fingers into the ends of Taiga's pale hair, the rain that was caught in strands collecting along them, trailing and rolling down along his wrists. 

As Taiga placed his hands over Hokuto's, spreading the droplets between their hold, he lifted his chin to bump the bridge of his nose against Hokuto's, the frames of his glasses softly clattering between them.

"... Hey…"

His breath was hot against Hokuto's lips as he led Hokuto's wide palm down over his collar to the tie around his neck.

"... Me too…"

There were many nights Taiga imagined Hokuto doing something like this with someone else, removing each other's clothes piece by piece as the rush and heat of desire raced through their veins. Maybe there had even been one or two alcohol-imbibed nights where Taiga had dreamed it was himself, waking with his body hot and swimming with shame before forcing himself back to sleep without another thought.

But Taiga never imagined it would be like this.

Whether in his mind's eye or in his dreams, there was an impatient haste.

He never imagined that Hokuto would bury his face in his neck as he carefully pulled his tie loose before slowly pushing his suit jacket from his shoulders.

The process of undressing often meant sex, especially when another person was there to do it for them, leaving themselves bare for the other to possess for pleasure.

But this was nothing like that.

For a long time, Taiga didn't understand. Hokuto confused him time and time again, unsure of what he meant or felt or wanted.

Now, it was all so clear. 

Now, Hokuto was a glass case and Taiga could see right into his heart. 

After all, it was Hokuto who taught him.

Hokuto told him he was scared when he hid himself in his neck.

He whispered just how much he missed him through his hesitant hands that took their time smoothing down his bare arms, leaving the damp dress shirt to join the discarded clothes on the floor.

Even just the beating of his heart sang songs of how much he wanted to see him.

All of which spoke love.

… It was about time for Taiga to say it too.

He had waited too long before.

He wasn't going to lose his chance now.

"... Matsumura..."

Taiga whispered into his hair, placing his hand on his cheek and leading him away from his shoulder.

Hokuto's eyes wandered over Taiga's features as he drew away from Taiga's skin, his voice still uneasy.

"... Taiga?..."

Taiga would apologize a million times over later.

He would apologize for not believing. For not trusting. For making him hurt over and over. For using him. For loving him. For scaring him, even now as they stood nearly bare with each other.

But it would be for later.

For now, Taiga wanted to love him.

Nothing else.

"Hokuto."

Taiga's eyes lowered as Hokuto grew close, their noses brushing.

There were some things that 3 years couldn't change.

Taiga watching his lips as an ask for a kiss was just the first Hokuto would learn.

"... Will you kiss me?...." 

Taiga's fingers began to trail along Hokuto's jaw, catching the drops that tempted to fall from his chin as his voice carried on his breath.

"... As training?....." Hokuto barely whispered, his breath warming Taiga's lips.

Taiga hoped Hokuto would understand his answer when he closed the space between them, pressing his lips into his.

No.

He dug his fingers into Hokuto's hair, pulling him closer as Hokuto looped his arms around his waist.

Never.

Hokuto only managed to release a sigh and catch a glimpse of Taiga's half-lidded eyes before Taiga tilted his head, capturing his lips again.

Never again.

Taiga moved Hokuto's lips apart with his, asking for Hokuto to taste him, which Hokuto eagerly received.

He wanted him.

He wanted Hokuto.

He wanted to love him and take him and never let him go.

No more games or hidden messages. No more regretful goodbyes and painful gazes.

No more.

No more or his heart might just fall apart.

Hokuto wiped away the tears Taiga didn't know fell from his closed eyes.

I love you.

I love you with all my heart.

Taiga told him with every kiss, clash of their teeth and whisper of his name.

I love you.

I love you.

Please never leave me again.

Hokuto said the same, rocking his lips into each kiss and swallowing Taiga's breath before taking it again.

It had been so long since a kiss had made him feel so alive.

Hokuto had pointlessly given it to so many, hoping it would numb the ache in his chest and cheapen it's worth so that when the person he wanted to value it most treated it like nothing, he would be able to believe the same.

But Taiga took each like it would be their last, breathing and gasping, refusing to patiently wait for the next.

It made his heart sore.

Even if Taiga's tongue was clumsy and his lips would fumble as Hokuto dragged his hand up his smooth back, Hokuto wouldn't trade it for the world and the world next.

Because it was him.

And Taiga was his everything.

Before, then and now.

Forever.

Taiga gasped as Hokuto placed kisses under his ear and down his neck, shuddering and dragging his nails through Hokuto's hair.

"H-Hoku-"

Hokuto took his lips again, sealing them and claiming his mouth as they stumbled until the back of Taiga's legs hit the side of Hokuto's bed, bringing them both down on top of Hokuto's soft covers.

Their kiss broke when they fell, Hokuto's hand sinking into his plush blankets, catching himself over Taiga's shoulder. Their chests heaved as their eyes met in the midst of their paused affection, becoming breathless in the wash of golden light from Hokuto's bedside lamp.

They were still the same people.

They were just the same as they were when Hokuto had come to Taiga's table earlier today.

But somehow, it was all different.

It all felt different knowing the other felt the same.

They could only guess that's just what love does.

How strange the thing called love was…

Taiga closed his eyes as Hokuto gently slipped off his glasses from his nose, blindly placing them safely on the sill above them to not spare a moment to miss how Taiga's lashes fluttered open for his eyes to meet his again.

The drops of rain that fell from their hair and skin seeped into the light fabric of Hokuto's bed, staining it dark as Taiga slowly reached up to touch Hokuto's lips. He barely touched the tips of his fingers to the reddened and swollen skin that had grown warm, his heart racing knowing that it was because of his kiss.

Years ago, the idea of this scene would have been Taiga's worst nightmare.

If he had ever told his younger self that he would one day be laying under another man shirtless, he would have surely laughed in his face.

He would have said that it was impossible. That there was no way in hell. That just the simple thought of it made him sick and it all had to be just a horrible joke.

Well, the one thing Taiga was sure of, was that people change.

Sometimes it just takes something or someone to wander into a person's life to tear it apart before they're pieced together in a different shape.

Hokuto had certainly shattered him.

But Hokuto also assembled the shards.

And Taiga would let him do it again and again.

"Hokuto…"

Taiga breathed his name as he reached up, slipping his fingers behind Hokuto's neck to lead him down, whispering against the lips he had admired and the moles that seemed to perfectly decorate them.

"I want you to hold me…"

Hokuto's breath hitched, his blood raced through his veins.

"A-are you sure–? You haven't-… before. I haven't–" Hokuto stumbled on his words while Taiga pressed warm kisses to the corners of his lips.

Hokuto thought his heart would explode.

It felt like their roles had suddenly reversed. Out of either of them to be charging forward, Hokuto would have thought it would be himself.

He guessed he should have known that if anyone were to break the outlines of what he had refined for years, Taiga would be the one to do it.

Hokuto closed his eyes as Taiga shook his head, taking Hokuto's face into his hands.

"It's okay…" he breathed into their kiss.

"Break me…"

"Just promise me you'll put me back together when we're done."

… Amazing…

It was amazing how much better sex was when it was with someone he loved and they loved him too…

The whole time, Hokuto thought his heart would burst. 

And it did. Over and over again as he drank from Taiga's heat.

Taiga clung to him, sweat beading on his skin with his nails digging into Hokuto's back as his name spilled from his lips and his voice sang. Tears fell from his eyes as he gasped and begged for Hokuto's kiss. 

"I love you–" he panted between their lips.

"Hokuto– I love you so much–"

Hokuto's heart was overflowing.

He never knew he could ever love so deeply.

"I love you." 

Hokuto's voice almost shook, his words nearly desperate as his chest burst, clutching Taiga in his hold. 

"I love you more than anything."

He repeated, tears stinging his eyes as he swallowed Taiga's breath.

"I love you."

"I love you…"

Hokuto could say it thousands of times and it would never be enough. Every kiss they had and would have would never come close. 

He hoped he had his whole life to show him.

After their heavy breaths had calmed and their heated skin had cooled, they entangled themselves with each other, taking the embrace they could only dream of during their years apart, when all they could do was deny, regret, and give up on ever feeling that warmth again, but knowing it would be a memory that would never escape them.

Hokuto pulled his covers over them before wrapping Taiga in his arms, burying his nose into his soft hair with his lips brushed against the back of Taiga's neck as he whispered words he wished he could have said sooner into his skin. 

Taiga took a hand from his waist, folding his fingers with it before setting them against his chest and feeling the heat from Hokuto’s skin set into his heart. 

There were many things that were left to be said and to be spoken. About Hinako and their relationship. The rain. The book. Their future. Their present. 

Three years was a long time and the stories they could tell were endless, but as they fell asleep with their hearts in sync for the first time, they both knew that they had each other for tomorrow.

 







There were only the soft sounds of shifting sheets and fabric in response to the beeping alarm as Taiga began to stir. 

His squinting eyes cracked open, regretting the morning while the beeping persisted. 

It was 6:00 am. 

It had to be. 

He knew, because it was the time Hokuto's alarm always went off in the morning.

"... Hokuto…" Taiga muttered, his vocals cracking from the early morning. "... Wake up…"

"... Hey."

Hokuto was awake. 

Taiga could tell by the squeeze that tightened around his middle. 

He reached behind him to tap the back of his fingers against the warm cheek that was set in the crook of his neck. 

"At least turn off your alarm…"

As Hokuto rolled back to stretch his arm out behind him to tap at the screen of his phone set on Taiga's bedside table, Taiga couldn't keep back the smile that cracked at the corner of his lips at the other arm that refused to unhook itself from under his waist. 

When Hokuto returned to curl back into his boyfriend, he found himself meeting Taiga's chest as Taiga turned himself to face him, slipping his arm under Hokuto's head while the other laid across Hokuto's shoulder to thread its hand into his dark waved hair. 

This is why Hokuto refused to leave Taiga’s side in the mornings. 

Even after weeks of dating, Taiga wasn’t really one for public displays of affection, or even displays of affection in private. Either of them were rare and far between, but every morning and night Taiga did all and more, making sure the moment they were ready to rest, their limbs were tangled with each other’s before sleep. 

It didn’t matter whether Taiga woke him up with an "I love you" or a kiss, these mornings were more than enough. 

"Good morning," Hokuto whispered, smiling into Taiga’s collar. 

Taiga just replied with a soft hum, hooking Hokuto’s head under his chin. 

"Taiga?..."

Another questioning hum vibrated in Taiga’s throat.

"... I love you."

Hokuto knew to not expect a mirrored response as he rarely got one, usually only ever receiving silence or a just a tightened hold, but that just made the small replies feel like a blessing as Taiga nuzzled himself into the mess of his hair and muttered back.

"Y' too…"

Hokuto didn’t need the full words to know. 

This was just how Kyomoto Taiga said "I love you too."

Taiga’s language wasn’t one that was hard to learn, it just took a little time to understand. 

Hokuto smiled and pressed a kiss against the base of Taiga's neck, waiting for Taiga's breath to even again as he got his fill of the scent of his skin before carefully untangling himself from him to stop his next alarm from disrupting Taiga's peaceful sleep again.

6 am was when Hokuto usually rose, but besides a morning rinse and preparing breakfast, there was something else he wanted to be ready to disrupt in the early morning.

… Well, someone. 

At around 8 am, Taiga’s doorbell would ring. 

Today was no exception.

"Oh! Hey! Good morning! I wasn't expecting to see you again, Hokuto."

Hokuto hoped that the other wouldn't recognize his forced smile.

"... Good morning, Juri."

He stepped back as Juri beamed before yawning, giving Hokuto's shoulder a hefty pat as he came in. 

"Is Kyomo awake?"

Maybe if Juri didn't arrive so early, he wouldn't have to ask this question.

"No, he's–"

"I'm awake."

They both turned to the voice behind Hokuto to see the sleep-disheveled Taiga entering the bathroom to wash up as quickly as he left his room, giving no mind to the extra person in his home. 

They watched the bathroom door close before Juri only laughed, throwing his coat over the back of Taiga's couch, showing he wasn't here to just drop something off.

"So you're making breakfast?"

Unfortunately.

Hokuto had gotten to know this pattern well enough to make enough for breakfast for 3.

At least today he was able to get Juri up on his feet to prepare the rice for their meal instead of just sitting on the couch and simply waiting for his fresh coffee as he often did.

When Taiga stepped out of the bathroom, he saw the two of them already well into their morning conversation which somehow became relatively routine.

"She's not mad?" Hokuto asked as he filled Juri's mug.

"Nah, we've just about got it figured out. Work already wakes me up early but the little one is the only reason why I'm able to stay awake. I'm with her in the morning and then we trade off before I leave."

"You don't need to stick around longer to help?..."

"Ahh well, I pay the rest of my dues at night."

"Do you really?..."

"... As much as I can–"

"Good morning."

The two of them looked over to the now completely awake Taiga entering the kitchen, Juri giving a bright grin and Hokuto giving his own warm smile as he turned back to the stove.

"Good morning, Kyomo. Are you ready to eat?"

Hokuto felt as if his line was stolen as Taiga nodded, sitting in his chair beside Juri.

"So, how is the writing going?" Juri said, setting his chin in his palm while sliding Taiga's serving of rice over to him.

"It's a slow start but I have plenty of ideas." Taiga took it before Hokuto handed him his bowl and plate with his breakfast. "At this point, it's just getting it on paper, but I know where it's going."

Juri didn't notice how Hokuto's fingers lingered over Taiga's as Hokuto passed him his bowl.

Frankly, Taiga didn't notice either, but Hokuto had grown used to it, keeping those moments to himself even if they weren't completely reciprocated.

The clock caught the corner of Taiga's eye as he brought his bowl up to his lips. 

"Ah. Hokuto, it's already 8:26. Don't you have to get going?"

Hokuto blinked, checking his watch while he pulled his apron from his neck.

"Shit. You're right," Hokuto said, quickly making his way back to the bedroom to collect his things, but not without tapping his hand on Taiga's back as he passed by. "Thank you."

Taiga didn't bother responding to Hokuto's gratitude considering Hokuto was already long gone before he has a chance, but when he set his bowl down, he felt a set of staring eyes boring into his side. 

He sighed, he swatting away Juri's nudging elbow.

"You guys have only been together for a few weeks and you're already in some kind of domestic bliss?" Juri chuckled, withdrawing his arm to himself.

Well, with the emotional rollercoaster it took to get here, things had better be going well or Taiga may have gone insane, but calling it something so cheesy as 'domestic bliss' made shivers crawl up his spine. 

Taiga was happy, but he wasn't ready to admit that these were some of the happiest days of his life. 

"Shut it. Just eat the breakfast Hokuto went through the trouble of making you," he said, shoveling a large bite of rice into his mouth and ignoring Juri's question.

Juri just smiled and ate some of his fish before responding with one last tease.

"Yes, sir."

A few bites later, the sound of the bedroom door closing got Taiga onto his feet to help lock the door behind Hokuto.

"How late do you work tonight?" Taiga asked with his cheeks still full of his food.

Hokuto threw his bag across his body before he leaned over to fasten his shoes. "We're doing some prep tonight so it may be late. I'll probably be back before you sleep, but will it be okay if I use your shower that late? Will it wake you up?"

Taiga frowned as he crossed his arms. "Why don't you just stay at your own place if you're going to be so late?"

"Is wanting to see you good enough of a reason?"

Deep inside Taiga knew the real answer to Hokuto's question, but his impulse replied first. Sure, they were happily dating, but people could only change so fast and Hokuto's words were still just as embarrassing as they had been nearly a month ago. 

"No." Taiga answered quickly to save himself from the flush that wanted to settle in his cheeks. "Just get out of here already."

Hokuto just smiled, letting Taiga push him out the front door before turning to face him through the frame. 

"Will you come for lunch today? Jesse made creme brulee for this week. I'll save you one if you are."

Taiga hated how Hokuto knew sweets were his weakness, especially when they were filled with cream.

He pulled the door half closed. "... I'll think about it."

Despite his deflecting words, Hokuto watched Taiga's eyes lower to his lips, making him unable to hold back a smile. 

Hokuto placed his hand on the handle on the other side of the door to lean in. 

"Just text me, okay?"

Even with his disapproving frown, Taiga still raised his chin to catch Hokuto's cheek and accept his wordlessly requested kiss.

"I'm leaving now."

Taiga dropped his hand to Hokuto's chest to push him away, sending him off to work with the words he told him each morning he left, ensuring Hokuto that he expected his return.

"Have a safe trip."

The door clicked shut and Taiga sighed, going back to his breakfast next to Juri who was unfortunately watching the whole time.

As much as Taiga wished to wipe the teasing grin Juri had off of his face, nothing could stop what would eventually spill from his lip. 

"How long is it going to take you to get used to him saying stuff like that? It's already been more than a month," Juri laughed, pushing his last abandoned rolls of tamagoyaki over to Taiga.

Taiga just plucked one off of Juri's plate and chomped down on it with his teeth, cutting the expertly crafted fluffy texture.

"Forever, probably."

It wasn't the flirting that bothered him.

It was the fact that it wasn't flirting that bothered him.

Everything that Hokuto said was completely genuine and that only embarrassed him more.

Juri propped his elbow up on the counter and drank from his mug. "Does he flirt like that at work still? You don't mind at all?"

Taiga pulled the spine out of his fish.

"No, it doesn't. He doesn't do that anymore, anyway."

Juri blinked, leaning his chin against his knuckles. "He's not?"

"He works in the kitchen now. One cook wasn't enough and since he knows the menu better than anyone, decided they hired new waiters. 

"I see," Juri smiled, warming his hands on his coffee before sighing. "It's kind of a shame that they don't have someone charming the customers any more. It sort of feels like an end of an era."

"Don't worry. There is."

When Juri looked over to Taiga, he was eating the last of his breakfast, finishing it off with the handmade pickled vegetables Hokuto served with the eggs.

"There is?..."

"They're people that Hokuto used to work with at his previous job. Apparently, they were about ready to quit anyway."

Juri hummed, fiddling with the spoon he used to mix the sugar into his coffee. "I see…"

Taiga glanced over at him, pulling his chopsticks from his lips

"... Are you curious?..."

Juri laughed, setting down his mug.

"... So… what are your lunch plans?"



"Welcome to Salut. How many people are in your party today?"

Juri almost had to squint as soon as he stepped into the restaurant behind Taiga.

The man before him was blinding.

If the world had been a cartoon, roses and sparkles would have bloomed around the man's image.

"I believe I've seen you before. You must have enjoyed the food, or maybe did you enjoy me?" the man said smoothly, his smile glimmering at the end of his sentence.

Taiga was already recoiling into himself as the man bowed to him.

"Uhh no. I–"

Juri could see Taiga's shoulders relax once Shintaro's voice boomed from the other side of the dining room.

"Kento!!"

"How many times do I have to tell you this isn't a host club!!!" Shintaro huffed, speeding over to him before shoving at Kento's shoulders, making Kento laugh. "You're lucky I don't tell Hokuto about this!" 

Kento just chuckled, letting Shintaro yank the menus from his hands.

"Go ahead, tell him! It's all in good fun, right Kyomoto?"

Taiga gave a polite smile, unsure of how to respond to Kento's playful wink. "Yeah… sure."

"Go refill some waters or something! Jeezus!!"

Juri just stood in shock, watching Shintaro briskly wave off Kento back into the restaurant while Taiga offered him a pitying smile when he turned back to them. 

"... Things are going well, I see."

Shintaro let out a heavy sigh as he crossed his arms with menus still grasped in his hand. 

"Too well, if you ask me. Kento and Fuma have a lot of experience and do a great job, but they're worse than Hokuto ever was! I get Hokuto was just trying to keep a customer base but our main attraction is still our food!"

"But business is good?" Taiga asked, following Shintaro's directing hand to the table that was set out for Taiga long ago, but was never taken out.

It was repurposed for a random overflow for many years, but when Taiga came back, it was cleared off for him again.

Taiga didn't really like how the designated spot drew attention and stirred up the whispers from the other guests about the author of Silent Conversation in his favorite restaurant, but it meant there was a table always waiting for him. 

There was no amount of care he could have had for Hokuto or his food that would convince Taiga to stand in the line outside while others stared and gawked at him. 

"Business is great! But my stress levels are higher than ever," Shintaro frowned, the wooden clipboard menu he set before Taiga clattering lightly against the tablecloth. "Our efficiency is fantastic and Kento and Fuma fit right in, but it feels like I'm spending all my time chasing them around, trying them to do work instead of playing 'who gets to have their ear whispered in by Kenty'. I just— Oh."

When Shintaro placed down Juri's menu, he looked up at him, only just then logging in his brain that there was another person besides Taiga who had heard him whining about his job. 

He quickly flipped his casual switch to professional, grinning and laughing to cover for his preciously exerted frustrations.

"I'm so sorry, sir! I didn't mean for you to hear all of that! I can assure you this is a wonderful establishment with wonderful people who are all very happy to work here and have no complaints about their work or colleagues at all! Could you be a friend of Kyomoto's?"

Shintaro straightened out, giving a polite bow, making Juri laugh and wave his hand, excusing Shintaro's unserviceable behavior. 

"It's okay, you can relax, I'm a friend of Hokuto and Kyomo, it's fine," Juri said while Shintaro's relief showed in his posture. "I can perfectly understand changes in work can be annoying sometimes."

Shintaro bowed again with his usual grin. "Thank you for being understanding, my good customer! Is there anything at all I can bring for you to drink?"

Juri shook his head and took the menu into his hands. "No, thank you, water is fine."

"Kyomoto?"

"Just water. Thanks, Shintaro." Taiga smiled as he pulled his phone out from his pocket. 

"Oh, also congratulations on the full-time position."

Shintaro beamed. "Thanks! It was about time! Though it was really about when I finished school," he chuckled. "And thank you for the signed book, my mom was thrilled."

"It's nothing at all."

It really wasn't.

The hard part was done.

Drawing some scribbles that somehow resembled a name was easier than falling asleep, especially when all he had to do was pass it to Hokuto.

After Shintaro scurried away, Juri went to study the menu. His eyes nearly crossed trying to interpret the French named items before squinting to read the small words written underneath.

The menu was longer than he remembered. 

Guess that's what happens when the staff is expanded.

The limited amount of refined dishes had expanded as well as including items considering dietary restrictions. 

"Hey, Kyomo, what are you-"

"Hmm?"

He had fully expected Taiga to be looking over the list as intently as he was, but his friend's hands were occupied with his phone rather than the clipboard menu before him. 

"... Do you not want to eat?"

Taiga didn't bother looking up.

"I do."

"Do you know what you want to eat?"

"No."

"Then why aren't you looking at the menu."

Taiga just tucked his hair behind his ear and kept his smile to himself as he swiped his thumb over his screen. 

"Don't worry about it, Juri."

When Shintaro returned, Juri was only confused more when Shintaro took Taiga's untouched menu without question after setting a creme brulee before him.

"So, do you know what you would like to order?"

Juri was so baffled that he had already forgotten what he was contemplating.

He chuckled awkwardly, handing Shintaro the clipboard. "Uhh… I'll just have the same thing as Kyomo, thanks."

"Sure!" Shintaro grinned, shoving his blank order sheet into his apron pocket. "Holler if you need anything!"

Juri's smile dropped as soon as Shintaro turned his back, turning to see Taiga already breaking into the sugar crust of the brulee.

"Are you seriously eating dessert before dinner?"

Taiga scooped the brulee into his mouth, licking the sweet creme from his lips. "Yeah, why not?"

"Didn't your parents say that it ruins your appetite?" 

"Yeah?" Taiga said, taking a spoonful and holding it out for Juri. "And aren't you the one who lived off of instant and convenient store food through college?"

Juri furrowed his brow, leaning forward and taking the spoon offered to him into his mouth, watching Taiga as he pulled it from his lips.

It was delicious and it nearly made Juri forget his argument, but he gratefully spread the cream over his tongue to savor the flavor before swallowing to speak and defend himself.

"I didn't have money then. That's called eating on a budget."

"No, that's called being lazy. You could have easily used your cafeteria credits or gone to a cheaper restaurant."

"Just give me another spoon."

Juri went through his bag, looking for Taiga's notebook before turning back, taking his second bite from Taiga's held-out spoon and placing the book on the table.

Just seeing the new notebook was refreshing for the both of them. 

The last had been battered to bits with the corners of the binding and pages softened from being carelessly tossed from place to place. Even the brand name printed and embossed in gold paint had been worn away and smoothed to the point it was hard to tell it was ever there in the first place.

The new notebook felt like a new mindset, a clean slate that didn't carry the stress and anxiety from the last, filled with scribbled-out words and scratched-out ideas. Instead, each page was fresh and crisp, unmarked and unused for endless potential.

"So, I know you're gonna hate this, but Matsumoto did want me to ask if you were willing to write a romance novel again…" Juri said, clicking the end of the pen and handing it to Taiga.

Taiga opened the notebook, pleased by its neat notes that were written smoothly with Kochi's congratulatory pen. "From your tone, it sounds like you already know the answer."

Juri smiled, stealing the spoon to take a shard of the sugar crust. "I do, but I still have to do my job."

"Then you know it will be another 10 years before I consider it again."

Juri laughed, setting the spoon down on the saucer. "I'll let him know."

Taiga's new idea was a mystery again.

Honestly, after working on Silent Conversation for so long, he started to miss his previous genre. Writing exciting moments and pressured meetings was enticing and he always loved hearing his editors gasp as they were reading. 

This time, it was just going to be less dark. He had to change it up somehow. If he wrote a mirror of his first series, it'd never sell.

Right now, his idea was to have the mystery plot hidden under the main character's occupation of painting family portraits of those with recently deceased to aid their grief.

Maybe it needed some adjustment, but for now, Taiga just wrote what came to mind.

It felt amazing to have the words flow back to him with ease again. 

"How's this?" Taiga asked, turning the notebook towards Juri who tilted his head to match the angle of the pages.

He put his hand over Taiga's to turn it towards him a little more, holding it as he read the neat bullet points Taiga wrote on the page.

"Hmm… Ohh… Very interesting. I think that's a great idea," Juri mused, tapping his chin with his free hand. "I feel like this would be more suited for later in the story, don't you think? You don't want to build up being too hasty."

"Oh, maybe. Let me-"

Taiga began to reach over to write a side note in the margins, but a plate intercepted their view, bringing them both to raise their heads to the person who held it.

"Pardon me, sirs. Here is your lunch."

Taiga withdrew his pen.

"... Ah. Hokuto."

Hokuto just smiled at Taiga, waiting for the both of them to remove Taiga's notes and their hands from the center of the table.

"Two tomato a la provencale, correct?"

Juri had no idea what he had ordered, but he could only assume it was correct by the fact that there were two of the same, so he just nodded.

He should have known it would have tomatoes, but he couldn't say he remembered anything primarily featuring tomatoes on the menu.

"I thought you were done with the waiting, Hokuto," Juri smiled as his lunch was set in front of him. "That's what Kyomo told me this morning."

"No, that's still correct," Hokuto said, putting down Taiga's plate in its place. "I don't serve anymore."

Juri laughed, trying to make fun of the situation. "But here you are, still bringing us our food."

"That's because I got word that our esteemed patron Kyomoto Taiga was here. I had to come by and give my greeting and thanks for what you've done for our restaurant," Hokuto smiled as he stepped back, giving them both a polite bow while Taiga cut into his food, not paying much mind to Hokuto's sudden formality.

"It's nothing at all," Taiga responded anyway.

"My staff also informed me that there were whispers about his boyfriend arriving with him today."

Ah. Juri understood now.

Hokuto was pissed.

"With all due respect, sir, I can assure you that my friend and I are nothing but friends," Juri explained with the same polite smile.

He was telling Hokuto what he already knew, but it didn't manage to make Hokuto relax as Hokuto crossed his arm, straightening his back and gave a laugh they both knew was fake.

"I see. Then what the other customers believed was flirting were just things friends do? The feeding each other and such?"

"Well, I–"

Juri paused.

Honestly, he had never thought about it. 

He guessed maybe the things he did with Taiga were a little more intimate than what two male friends usually did, but was there anything wrong with that? He was only a few months away from finally getting married and Taiga was currently in an unexpectedly stable relationship. There shouldn't be any misunderstanding. 

Also, it wasn't like Taiga wasn't encouraging it.

"Come on, Hokuto. You know I'm engaged."

"That doesn't matter."

"I just want to let you know that Kyomo was the one who held out the spoon. I didn't ask for it." Juri held out his hand, presenting the man in question who was eating peacefully across from him.

Hokuto's service smile fell before he sighed.

"You know he doesn't know any better. And you still accept the spoon."

"Okay, sure but–"

They both bit their tongues when the clink of Taiga's silverware cut into their trivial argument, pulling them both to look over to him and watch him wipe his mouth on his napkin. 

"Hokuto?"

Juri and Hokuto froze like children getting caught by their teacher before Hokuto spoke up.

"... Yes?"

Taiga stood from his chair. "Will you come with me for a moment?"

"To where?... Wait, Taiga. Where are you–"

Taiga didn't wait to answer Hokuto's question as he walked past him towards the back of the restaurant, Hokuto following quickly after him and leaving Juri alone with his vegetable-heavy dish.

Juri stared down at it, contemplating the rich deep reds of the roasted fruit-vegetables before remembering the words of his dear mother.

She was right…

Eating dessert beforehand did ruin his appetite.

Juri stood up, seeing the eyes of other customers hiding away as he looked over the other tables that must have been watching this whole time.

He guessed there was no better time to have a smoke. It was better than sitting alone with the curious eyes that peeked over at him.

As he sat down in the small garden at the end of the alley, lighting his cigarette alone, he laughed to himself as the burn at the end bloomed. 

"... I guess that could have been me, huh?"

He filled his lungs with smoke.

No.

It had to be Hokuto.

The only person who could ever truly teach Taiga was always going to be Hokuto.

Just as the only person who could save Hokuto was always going to be Taiga.

While the end of Juri's cigarette burned between his lips, the "where" Taiga took Hokuto was the backroom storage to which he closed the door to after Hokuto walked in. 

Taiga sighed, shutting the door with his back by leaning against it.

"What's going on between you and Juri? Every time you guys are together, things seem to get tense."

"I'm just telling him what I heard," Hokuto said with his back turned to him as he busied himself with aimlessly pushing boxes of produce around the small steel table. "Fuma came in laughing so hard that the women Kento was serving were so distracted by the two of you they wouldn't even look up at him. Do you understand what that means?"

"No. I don't." Taiga's eyebrows furrowed. "What we do is none of their business. Isn't it their fault for gawking at other people? How is it my or Juri's fault?"

"Do you not understand why they were watching you two?"

"Not really. We were just acting as we always do."

That was a problem in itself, but Hokuto stayed on topic.

"Taiga, you were feeding him."

"I was just sharing."

"That's not what normal people do when they share food."

"Is it not? Don't you do that with me all the time?"

Taiga wasn't getting it.

Taiga's cluelessness was part of what made him adorable, but when it came to Juri, Hokuto couldn't help but feel an irritation flare up in his stomach. 

"It's not about that," Hokuto sighed heavily as he dropped his weight onto the side of the table.

"Taiga, how many times have you done something like that with me?"

Taiga's brow raised, his head tilting slightly in confusion. "Did I just say that you-"

"Not me, Taiga. You."

Taiga blinked.

Hokuto swore he could see the gears turning in Taiga's head. 

He wasn't really sure what was going to come next. 

He mostly expected Taiga to apologize to end the argument without really knowing why he was apologizing, but it was possible Taiga would fight back, refusing to believe he did anything wrong.

Hokuto understood a lot more about Taiga since they started dating, but no one could truly ever understand everything about someone without being inside their mind.

"Hokuto?..."

Whichever way Taiga reacted, he could handle it, right?

"Are you-…"

"... Are you jealous?..."

Apparently not.

Hokuto felt his face instantly begin to burn. 

Even though that wasn't the point Hokuto was trying to make, he cheeks turned visibly red in the dimly lit storage room. He just was trying to make Taiga realize what these gestures could be perceived while in public, but somehow, Taiga had seen deeper into his own heart that Hokuto had even realized himself. 

As Taiga watched Hokuto cover his face with his hand and wrist, his heart squeezed. 

It was hard to believe that this was the same man from all those years ago. 

So long ago, this man had pulled him in by the waist and challenged his doubts about love without hesitation, the same one who followed him and insisted that love was all worth something.

Somehow, that same man who flirted with every woman in his own restaurant was now jealous over his boyfriend just because of some stupid gossip between friends.

Taiga couldn't help but smile, his chest heating with a mix of embarrassment and adoration.

It was incredible how much things could change.

But Hokuto wasn't the only one who had changed.

Taiga was different too.

It might have been slow, but he was learning.

He sat next to Hokuto on the table, leaning over to see him turn his face away from him as he slid closer, just until their shoulders bumped.

"... Do you want me to start feeding you too-?"

"No, it's not about that."

"Then what can I do?..."

It was hard to stay mad when Taiga was so earnestly trying.

Hokuto dropped his hands into his lap, sighing. 

"Can you just… not do these things with Juri?"

"Only Juri?

"Only because I know you were in love with him once…"

That wasn't really true, but this wasn't exactly the appropriate time to try to clarify exactly what Juri was to Taiga back then. 

"... You know he's getting married next month, right?"

"I know but you can do all these things with him that you don't even do with me. It's sometimes hard to believe that I'm the one you're actually with…"

Taiga laughed. "I can try to do it if you want–"

"No, I told you. That's not the point…" Hokuto said, using the excuse of pushing his fingers into his temple to hide his face. 

"... Just promise me you won't fall in love with him again…"

Taiga smiled a little to himself as he looked at their feet.

"... No, that's impossible."

He knew it was impossible.

When Taiga had stolen a kiss from Juri for the first and last time, the only thing it told him was that he was completely in love with Hokuto. There was no spark or ache for a lost love, just a regret and realization that Hokuto's kiss was the only one that mattered, and that fact would never change. 

Taiga had learned more at that moment from what he didn't feel more than anything else.

"... You know, I can do those things with Juri because it doesn't mean anything."

"But with you, it's embarrassing."

Hokuto looked over at Taiga beside him, seeing his timid smile and staying silent for him to continue.

"If it's with you, I just imagine how you would look straight at me and not at the food. You would look at me like– you know." Taiga waved his hands, making some nebulas form of what he was trying to describe.

"It's embarrassing."

"But if it really bothers you, I can try to do more stuff like that or I don't know, I can–"

Taiga stopped when he felt Hokuto's head on his shoulder and his nose bury into his clothes. He let the rest of his words release as a breath while Hokuto slipped his hand under his to threaded their fingers loosely together.

He stayed quiet for a moment, letting the smell of his own shampoo in Hokuto's hair fill his nose before muttering into his dark hair.

"... Juri isn't the one who sleeps next to me at night."

"Juri doesn't cook for me every morning."

"Juri doesn't say 'I'm home' or 'I'm leaving' when he comes and goes."

"Only you."

Hokuto's fingers tightened around Taiga's as the room fell silent aside from the distant humming of chatter and the clatter and clink of plates and silverware behind the door.

Without words, they knew their hearts were in the same place. 

"Taiga?..."

"Hmm?"

"Can I kiss you?"

Taiga couldn't help but laugh, bumping his temple against Hokuto's head before Hokuto moved away to stand before him, cupping his cheek to lift his chin up towards him. 

"You already know the answer without me saying, don't you?"

Hokuto mirrored his smile as Taiga slipped his fingers under the tie of Hokuto's apron to pull him closer.

"I do."

Taiga let out an airy chuckle while Hokuto lowered his head to press his lips against his to feel the touch that set his heart ablaze time and time again, and when Hokuto began to pull back, Taiga craned his neck, chasing for another to which Hokuto happily surrendered to. 






What did you do with true love? 






… Honestly, neither of them still didn't know. 

Love was a fickle thing and behaved in strange ways. 

It could shatter your heart and reduce you to tears before making it soar and bringing you to cloud nine. 

Love wasn't smooth sailing like in fairy tales where everything finished "happily ever after" and wrapped with a neat bow. No matter how much they knew they had each other's hearts, it didn't always mean that things would be picture-perfect.

But every small bump on their path made every loving moment worth even more.

Taiga let out a pleased hum as Hokuto caught his lip between his own and tilted Taiga's chin up with his knuckles to take another kiss. 

They were nearly completely lost in their own world, Taiga tugging Hokuto closer by his apron with Hokuto running his fingers along the back of Taiga's ear and into his hair until a knock pounded on the door, making them both nearly jump.

Taiga laughed quietly into Hokuto's collar as Hokuto folded a protective arm around and over his shoulders. Taiga clutched his hands into Hokuto's uniform, just as embarrassed as he was surprised, hearing Hokuto's heart racing in his chest as fast as his own while Hokuto called back to the door in a loud voice.

"Yes??"

Jesse's voice called back.

"Hokuto? I won't ask what's going on, but I want to tell you the orders are piling up. I'll need you back here pretty soon!"

"Ah, okay! I'll be there soon!"

"Alright!"

They both waited until they heard the squeak and thump of the kitchen door closing before their shoulder relaxed, Hokuto releasing a sigh of relief while Taiga drew away from his chest. 

"Back to work?" Taiga asked, fixing the tie on Hokuto's uniform he had pulled from its neat place around his waist.

"Unfortunately, but let me fill up before I go."

Taiga squeezed his eyes shut as Hokuto placed chaste kisses over his forehead, cheek and neck, getting his serving of his own boyfriend before he had to send him back to his editor.

When Hokuto finished with a last kiss on Taiga's lips, Taiga extended it, holding the sides of Hokuto's neck to make him stay for just a moment longer. 

People say that commutation is important in a relationship, Hokuto and Taiga knew that better than anyone.

So even if they knew, they made sure to say it.

Hokuto grinned, tapping his head to Taiga's, knowing his time was running out.

"I love you."

Taiga chuckled, holding Hokuto's cheek, already anticipating when Hokuto would return to his door again tonight.

When tonight, like every night, Hokuto would show him exactly what to do with true love. 

"I love you too."
